When Ashley narrowed her eyes and stroked her fur, Lavigne quietly closed her eyes and relaxed into the touch. Seeing this, Marlene also smiled back, creating a peaceful atmosphere.

Princess Stephania looked slightly surprised at the scene before smiling herself. Perhaps she was happy to see how Marlene and Rosemary’s relationship had changed from before.

“Ah, I can see it now.”

Ophelia leaned her face out the window and spoke in a delighted voice.

“Is that Ophelia-sama’s family home?”

“Yes. Everyone, welcome to the Marquisate of Fobrester.”

Ophelia made a joking bow. The port town surrounded by outer walls, with its uniformly brick-roofed buildings, had a certain charm and atmosphere.

The town center was built on a small hill, where a stately castle stood. The townscape spread out from the base of the hill.

Since across the sea was already foreign territory, it was quite an impressive castle. Though compared to Theoreme Castle, the royal castle of Termwills, it was still within the bounds of conventional architecture.

“Should we head directly to the castle?”

“Yes. I’ve spoken with Father. Preparations for our reception should be ready, so could you have the dragon palanquin land in the castle’s courtyard?”

“Lindwurm. Head for the castle.”

Lindwurm turned his head and let out a cry in response to my voice. The dragon palanquin moved at a leisurely pace toward the castle of Marquis Fobrester.

Ophelia waved to the soldiers on the watchtower of the castle walls. The soldiers, having noticed Ophelia, straightened their posture and returned a crisp salute.

We passed over the castle walls and descended into the visible courtyard, landing gently.

Being wyverns from the royal castle, they were well-trained – but Lindwurm seemed to be acting as leader and coordinating the wyverns well, making them quite easy to handle.

“Good work, Lindwurm.”

After getting out of the palanquin and lightly stroking Lindwurm’s nose, he responded with a rumble in his throat.

They must have been preparing for our arrival in advance. Marquis Fobrester appeared with his servants almost immediately, without making us wait.

“Welcome to the Marquisate of Fobrester. As lord of this land, I extend my heartfelt welcome. You must be tired from your long journey. First, let me show you to your rooms. If you have any luggage, please feel free to ask the servants.”

Marquis Fobrester bowed and delivered his welcome speech.

“It’s been a while, Marquis Fobrester.”

“It has been too long, Your Highness Stephania. Ambassador, welcome.”

“Thank you, Marquis Fobrester.”

He then turned to Marquis Zilbolt.

“How many years has it been since we last met, Marquis Zilbolt?”

“It has been quite some time, Marquis Fobrester.”

While they exchanged greetings, the servants respectfully accepted our luggage. Though it wasn’t much, since we planned to load the entire dragon palanquin onto the ship. We moved toward the guest rooms under Marquis Fobrester’s personal guidance.

“I’m home, Father.”

“Ah. Welcome back, Ophelia.”

Marquis Fobrester smiled in response to Ophelia’s words during our movement. The guest rooms were nearby quickly – rooms lined the corridor facing the courtyard. The courtyard had a fountain, and the sound of flowing water was pleasant. Quite a nice place.

“We have prepared a modest banquet. When dinner is ready, we will call for you, so please wait a little while. If there’s anything you don’t understand, please ask the servants.”

With that, we were shown to the VIP suite.

The room was quite spacious. There was a large living area and several private bedrooms, giving it the appearance of a small mansion. Apparently, this entire area counted as one VIP suite.

Since they sometimes host foreign nobles, it’s designed so that escort units can stay in the same room as the VIPs.

The bedrooms contained canopied beds and intricately decorated dressing tables, with rather lavish interior decoration.

Now then. We certainly couldn’t all sleep in one bed. Rooms would be assigned according to the layout and beds…

We needed to discuss how to divide everyone up.

“How about placing the escorts at intervals, with Your Highness Stephania and Marquis Zilbolt and his family on either side?”

“That works for me.”

“We have no objections either.”

Well, there probably wasn’t need for that much caution in Marquis Fobrester’s castle, but we did have escort duties.

Princess Stephania would be in the innermost room. Next to her would be Sheila, Irmhild, Seraphina, Tephra, and Viola. The Zilbolt household. Next to them, me and my fiancées. Then Alfred next to that. This way, we could respond if anything unusual happened in adjacent rooms.

For sleeping, we’d place Lavigne and Ambrum in the living room. With Caduceus outside the window – that should be perfect.

“Well then, Theo-kun. I’ll be working for a while longer.”

“Mm. Don’t push yourself too hard.”

“Well, if I finish my work early, the rest will be like a vacation.”

Alfred laughed like that and, along with Viola, set up at the edge of the room to continue his armor-making work until dinner. Ophelia also seemed concerned about Alfred’s work progress and went near him. Once the work was done, he could spend time relaxing with Ophelia.

The three members of the Zilbolt household headed for the bedrooms. They said they wanted to rest a bit as a family.

“Then, Ambassador, until later.”

Elmer and the others also separated and headed to other VIP suites.

“Phew.”

Now that assignments were decided – could I relax until dinner? I settled onto the sofa. Even though it was a large dragon palanquin, with so many people… It was a relief to be able to stretch my limbs. As I sat relaxing on the sofa, the servant assigned to our room made tea for us.

“Still, Rosemary. You’ve changed quite a bit, haven’t you? You seem to be getting along well with Marlene too.”

Perhaps because Marquis Zilbolt had left, Princess Stephania said this to Rosemary while tilting her teacup.

“Is that so?”

Rosemary shrugged her shoulders and opened her feather fan. Since Marlene was smiling happily, Rosemary seemed rather uncomfortable.

“Yes. You used to be much more tense, but perhaps it’s thanks to the Ambassador?”

“…It’s because the environment changed. If there’s no need, I don’t have to be hostile. If you want to call that thanks to Theodore, then I suppose so.”

“Hmm.”

Princess Stephania smiled somewhat mischievously. As Rosemary hid her expression with her feather fan and turned away, Grace smiled wryly and asked a question as if to change the direction of the conversation.

“Speaking of which, what are the plans starting tomorrow?”

“We’ll probably work on preparing the ship. Well, we also promised to meet with the knight order members of the marquisate and train… but our stay is short too.”

I wondered how much training we could accomplish in that time. But Marquis Fobrester and Ophelia said it would be fine.

“I believe Theodore-sama’s usual approach will be more than sufficient to stimulate them. Just letting them glimpse a higher level once should make them more dedicated to their subsequent training,” said Ophelia.

I see. So my role is something like boosting their morale. Judging by the soldiers’ movements before we entered the castle, they already seemed quite skilled, so that should be fine.

+++

# **246 – Dance with the Golem**

The work of loading cargo onto the large sailing ship docked at the harbor was progressing. The dragon palanquin we had ridden from Termwills was scheduled to be loaded onto the ship and cross the sea as is.

The crew members were busily making preparations for the voyage, loading food, water, and other supplies.

“Come to think of it, this is my first time on such a proper sea voyage.”

“Mine as well. I’m looking forward to it.”

Claudia and Tephra smiled as they watched the crew working. Seraphina seemed to be—standing atop the mast, enjoying the view.

The wyverns led by Lindwurm would also be boarding the ship, but having them stay on board until departure would probably be too cramped.

Therefore, we removed the wyverns’ gear on deck and let them relax for a while at Marquis Fobrester’s castle.

“Lindwurm, please return to the castle courtyard with the others.”

With those words, Lindwurm led the other wyverns back to the Marquis’s castle. After this, we planned to conduct training at the knight order’s outpost near the harbor.

Though it started with a verbal promise, Marquis Fobrester said he would pay me an instructor’s fee.

“Well then, Ambassador-dono. I look forward to working with you today,” said Marquis Fobrester.

“Understood. Then let’s begin.”

Together with everyone, I boarded the carriage and headed toward the knights’ outpost at the harbor.

Though the knight order of the Marquisate of Fobrester was located facing the sea… the battles they anticipated weren’t limited to land. Naturally, they also had combat on ships and at sea in mind.

Regarding the training, when I asked King Melvin about it, he told me I could do as I pleased.

Or rather, given the current situation where I had friction with Crown Prince Zadias, there were aspects of improving the Marquisate of Fobrester’s technical capabilities that I wanted to advance.

Aerial combat techniques could be used regardless of whether on land or sea, making them perfectly suited for the Marquisate’s knight order. Well, being told I could freely do various things made it easier for me too.

The knight order’s outpost was a building surrounded by walls. Within the grounds was a quite spacious training field, where the main members of the knight order and guards were lined up. I could see magicians among them too. Since they anticipated fighting on ships, many wore easily manageable cutlasses at their waists.

When we descended from the carriage, their gazes gathered on us. The fact that their attention was particularly focused on me… might mean the Marquis had given them some explanation about today’s training content. It was convenient to skip the explanation process.

Marquis Fobrester had also attended the spring dinner party in Termwills. He probably brought escorts from his domain then, and those escorts likely attended the knight order-hosted dinner party too. If so, they probably already knew about the aerial combat gear.

Following Marquis Fobrester, I stood before them as they formed ranks. The knights and soldiers placed their hands over their chests and returned the salute.

The Marquis looked over the assembled officers and soldiers, then opened his mouth. His voice echoed across the square.

“Everyone, well done. The reason I’ve gathered you here today is none other than this. You’ve all likely heard about the flight technique using magic tools. Today, we have the magician from Termwills who devised this flight technique, Otherworld Ambassador Theodore-dono, gracing us with his presence to provide personal instruction.”

At Marquis Fobrester’s words, simultaneous applause arose from the officers and soldiers. The Marquis nodded at their reaction and continued speaking, introducing each guest one by one. Princess Stephania, Princess Marlene, Baroness Silun, and Grace who holds a knight title. Just those introduced here as guests represented quite an impressive lineup. As knights, they must be quite motivated too.

“—I expect today’s training to be fruitful for everyone. Well then, Ambassador-dono. May I ask you to proceed?”

“Yes. Then—”

I nodded and stepped forward. Now then, where to begin?

“What about the aerial combat gear?”

“After the dinner party in Termwills, I had magicians and magic engineers research it, and while it’s still a prototype, we’ve managed to create something.”

Hmm. In that case, perhaps it would be good to start by showing them the movements. Something like a demonstration.

The reason being, when I was introduced, some had shown slight expressions of confusion.

They probably had professional military pride proportional to their high level of training, and while I might be treated as the founder, the truth was they probably thought my age was too young to be an instructor.

So first, I needed to destroy that preconception and make them acknowledge me as qualified to be an instructor. That would make it easier for them to accept what I said, and the training would proceed more smoothly.

“Well then, I think I’ll start by showing an example of movement in aerial combat. If you have aerial combat gear, you probably already know the principle, but forming shields as footholds in the air, combining levitation and air blast to kill or add momentum… using that to move freely in the air—well, when explained, it’s surprisingly simple.”

I casually formed shields on the soles of my feet. As if climbing stairs, I casually took two, then three steps into the air and stood in midair. I snapped my fingers and generated aqua golems, positioning them in the air.

“Now then—I’ll begin.”

As soon as I spoke, I kicked off a shield and charged toward the farthest golem. I used levitation to increase the initial speed at the moment of kicking off, then accelerated with air blast. Through circulation, I heightened my magical power and made Ouroboros gleam with a pale blue light. Just like that, as I passed by, I sliced through the golem’s torso. Leaving a trail of blue light in the air, the golem was cleanly bisected from the torso.

I instantly regenerated the golem. Without a moment’s delay, I made it counterattack. Through levitation control, I killed inertia, kicked off a shield to fly upward while tracing an arc. I avoided the weapon of that sword-shaped golem, took its back, and brought Ouroboros straight down from above. Earlier was horizontal. This time, bisected vertically.

As if that were the signal, the remaining golems all moved at once. Reading the movements of the automatically controlled golems closing in from all directions, I dodged, received, redirected. Or made them attack each other. Spinning round and round, swapping heaven and earth as I danced. Using the dragon staff’s movements to disrupt stances and swap positions, I mowed them down with Ouroboros when they clustered together.

As I finished swinging Ouroboros, the golems at a distance fired water bullets at me.

I flew left and right at high speed to evade the bullets, then used form shift to slip through the barrage of deviation shooting. When two golems aligned in a straight line, I deployed a shield in front and charged at maximum speed. Thrusting Ouroboros forward, deploying shields around my body while adding a spinning drill-like rotation, I pierced through both golems’ torsos at once.

That left one golem remaining. I flew upward once, then immediately descended at a sharp angle. Pressing down from above, I surrounded it with shields on all sides to seal its movements, then accelerated just like that. As I slammed it into the ground, I swung Ouroboros through, gouging out the ground along with the golem, splitting it in two.

I kicked off the ground to disengage. Shifted form in midair and landed. The training field ground being gouged out would be inconvenient. I’ll properly fill in the soil later.

“…Well, that’s about it.”

I only used the three basic types of magic essential to aerial combat. The rest was martial arts.

When I turned my face toward the assembled officers and soldiers, almost all of them had their mouths hanging open. Marquis Fobrester’s eyes were wide open too.

“As expected… of Theodore-sama.”

“It’s been a while since I last saw it—but it’s still amazing. And you were controlling the golems at the same time, right?”

Ophelia and Princess Stephania, who had seen my movements before, remained calm. When they applauded along with Marlene, one by two people remembered and joined in the applause—which spread throughout the entire group, becoming cheers.

“Thank you. While magic tools alone can’t achieve such improvisational movements—I believe that with sufficient mastery of magic tools, something close should be possible.”

As I said this, the knights’ expressions—or rather, the look in their eyes—changed. They were certainly biting well. With this, the training should proceed with enthusiasm. Later, as a practical example, having Sheila and others demonstrate against golems might be even more effective.

“Well then, let’s proceed with the training. That said, since time is limited, what I can convey is also limited. I think we’ll do this clearly in a practical combat format, so please organize the units.”

When I said this, the knight order’s senior members exchanged glances.

“Everyone, just like I did earlier, you’ll be facing aqua golems. I’ll make the aqua golems perform movements characteristic of group tactics used by those with aerial combat gear, so please think of countermeasures and incorporate any tactics you find effective into your regular training.”

The aqua golems were already prepared.

I had created a golem unit with clearly defined roles from their appearances—some with water stretched long to mimic spears, others with bow-shaped weapons. Seeing this, the knights and soldiers’ faces twitched slightly.

“…I hope their spirits don’t break.”

“It’s fine. Theodore is good at adjusting difficulty levels with those.”

As Rosemary murmured while hiding her mouth with a feather fan, Sheila closed her eyes and answered like that.

“That’s right. He takes it step by step.”

“Theodore-sama also gives advice.”

“That’s true. With the aerial combat gear, we too found ourselves able to use it like our own limbs before we knew it.”

At Sheila and Irmhild’s words, Ashley nodded, and Grace smiled as she chimed in agreement.

Well… against aqua golems, there’s little worry about injuries. Plus, even if the content is somewhat hard, if it leaves an impression, they won’t easily forget it. If the goal is content that becomes ingrained in a short time, I have no choice but to use this method… but as Sheila said, I’ll adjust the difficulty to some extent.

I can stay until dusk today. Today’s training curriculum is to find breakthroughs through trial and error against the tactics I use, until they can handle them. In other words, I’ll keep the difficulty at a level that can be managed in half a day.

+++

# **247 – Dragon Scale Armor**

Though the knight order, soldiers, and magicians training together meant we had large numbers… I had them divided by unit, and by increasing the number of golems to match, we could run training on a considerable scale all at once.

With limited time, I wanted high-density training, but making it too difficult would cause problems. I also made sure to create enough leeway for them to take breaks in shifts. After all, if they injured themselves during training, we’d lose everything we were working toward.

Since it was summer, I used dark magic protective spells to cover the training grounds from above, weakening the sunlight and lowering the temperature to prevent heatstroke.

Beyond that, I made sure they properly replenished their water and salt intake, conducting training with rotations and breaks interspersed.

Even during breaks, I had them observe. Watching others’ movements and learning from both failures and successes was important. Seeing successful examples served as mental training, and failures could lead to improvements and revisions in their own movements if they applied the lessons to themselves.

“Kuh!”

One knight failed to properly receive a golem’s spear thrust, nearly losing his footing and throwing off his balance.

“Don’t think of it as manipulating a magic tool. You need to familiarize yourself with the sensation until it feels natural, as if the ground is taken for granted where you step.”

Some were still unfamiliar with operating magic tools. I offered advice, but ultimately, it came down to practice. For this, there was no choice but repetitive training.

“Nuooh!”

A golem descended directly from above, spear at the ready. Since it was only formed from water, it wouldn’t cause injury, but a direct hit would count as being unable to fight, forcing withdrawal. Whether it was knightly pride or dignity… gritting his teeth, he twisted his body at the last possible moment to avoid it. Quite a good reaction.

“Remember you can move not just left and right, but up and down as well. As you can see, descending is the fastest movement, but until you’re accustomed to it, it’s better to avoid that due to the risk of falling. Since attacks from below are easier to block with a shield, it’s good to allocate more awareness to attacks from above.”

“B-but this is— kuh!”

Golem archers leaped out from behind the spear formation, simultaneously firing water bullets instead of arrows. While deflecting them with his shield and cutlass, he charged toward the golems.

Spear tips closed in on the knight who had advanced ahead, but soldiers from the same unit followed behind, crashing into the golems. They stunned them with body slams and immediately crossed spears.

Good judgment and fighting spirit too. Their skill level is high. With this, maybe I could have the golems perform slightly more demanding coordination?

When I made the golems float as if turning heaven and earth upside down, the officers’ and soldiers’ faces twitched. Both offense and defense would completely change in nature because of that alone.

Simply being able to deploy shields from their soles wouldn’t enable that. If attempting it with magic tools, they’d need to properly maintain their posture through control of Levitation and Air Blast. Well, by showing them this now, eventually someone capable should emerge.

We continued training in that manner until evening fell.

The knights kept up until the very end, and while many soldiers were leaning on their spears when we finished, they all stood on their own feet, looking straight ahead. Their determination was quite commendable.

“How was it?”

“Well, truly… it was most meaningful training.”

The Knight Order Commander, questioned by Marquis Fobrester, was breathing heavily from his shoulders but answered while regulating his breath.

“I’d like to incorporate what we learned today into training starting tomorrow.”

“Mm. Everyone, you’ve worked hard today. Let’s have a round of applause for Theodore-dono, who instructed us.”

Applause rose from the officers and soldiers. I bowed in response.

After returning to the castle, we sat down for dinner. Being a port town, the served dishes featured many seafood items. Fish and shellfish soup. Steamed fish. And lobster cheese bake. All were delicious, but the cheese bake in particular was exquisite.

“How was it? Today’s training.”

He sought my impressions regarding the knight order. Marquis Fobrester seemed in high spirits.

“Well, I think their skill level is high. Their morale and discipline are sufficient, so there were no dropouts, I imagine.”

“I believe it served as good stimulation for them. Actually, they’ve had a slight sense of rivalry between land and sea forces for some time now.”

“It didn’t appear that way to me…”

“Meaning it wasn’t to the extent of becoming problematic. As long as it doesn’t turn hostile, it can be a part of mutual improvement—that’s what the Knight Order Commander and I had discussed.”

“In that regard, regarding aerial combat, they share the same lack of experience. It’s important regardless of land or sea forces.”

“Precisely. Having been shown concrete examples, ideal movements to aspire to, and clear goals for the future, they’ll likely cooperate, remain aware of each other, and strive even harder in their efforts.”

I see. Since they have an appropriate level of competitive spirit, even somewhat difficult training should fuel their desire for improvement.

The fact there were no dropouts was partly because they were showing off to each other too. Marquis Fobrester is impressive as expected.

“The golems Theo controls during training… how should I say, they move in ways you wouldn’t think were golems. Almost human-like, or something… completely different from my dolls.”

Rosemary said.

“Ah, that’s probably because I create pseudo-decision-making time and coordination delays for each golem. Otherwise, it wouldn’t be training assuming group combat.”

While I, controlling them, can grasp the situation, I deliberately impose a time lag where the golems themselves recognize the opponent’s movements before acting. Furthermore, having other golems recognize their comrades’ movements, then coordinating accordingly.

If you remove such play, the whole should coordinate like a single organism. That would be suitable for different training, though.

“The golems stagger when hit, don’t they?”

Claudia said with a wry smile.

“But, Theo anticipates those movements and when we act accordingly, he even reproduces the golems moving while enduring pain.”

“I once took a golem’s suicidal attack.”

“…Even hearing the explanation, it sounds like a joke.”

At Grace and Sheila’s words, Princess Stephania’s smile twitched slightly.

“Those aspects too, I’ve incorporated into the golems’ movements after training with everyone.”

“Compared to the early days, their movements have become much more human-like.”

Ashley said.

“I see… So we’re benefiting from Theodore-dono and everyone’s diligent training. I must express my gratitude once more.”

Marquis Fobrester closed his eyes and quietly bowed his head.

“Ah, finally finished!”

Sometime after returning to the guest room after dinner, Alfred raised his voice happily and threw his limbs onto the sofa.

“Dragon scale armor?”

“Yeah. Exactly enough for everyone. Could you try them on and see if there are any parts that hinder movement?”

The armor was distributed to all party members, handed over by Viola. Since Viola took the measurements, the equipment fit everyone’s physique perfectly.

“I can wear it too!”

Seraphina exclaimed happily.

“They’re custom-made, after all.”

They’d even made Lavigne’s protector.

“Well then, we’ll go change in the bedroom.”

Irmhild said. Everyone went together into the bedroom. I changed quickly too.

The Arachne silk fabric felt quite pleasant to the touch. The dragon scales covered key areas like the heart, throat, and abdomen. The white dragon scales were also smooth and felt nice.

A magic stone was embedded in the throat piece. It should have the defensive magic Protection enchanted onto it. On top of that, having fire resistance made it absolutely perfect.

“How is it?”

I thrust out a fist, bent my elbow. Twisted my waist, lifted my leg—trying out various body movements.

“Good. Light, and the dragon scale parts don’t hinder movement.”

Grace and the others emerged from the bedroom. Their appearance hadn’t changed from when they entered. Since it was armor meant to be worn under clothes, whether it allowed easy movement had to be judged while wearing clothes.

“No parts that feel hard to move in?”

“Seems fine.”

“Marlene?”

When I asked Marlene, she nodded, placed a hand on her chest, and smiled. Apparently, no issues.

“Well, good. This time was cutting it quite close, wasn’t it?”

Alfred was in high spirits after completing a big task.

“Good work. Anyway, this means both Alfred and Viola can move into their vacation period.”

“Yeah. Seems like I can take it easy with Ophelia for a while.”

“Can we explore the town? I’d like to visit this town’s blacksmith.”

Said Viola. Viola too… she’s diligent, even though she just finished work.

“Shall I ask Ophelia to arrange an escort for you?”

“Thank you.”

“Hmm. So departure is finally tomorrow, then?”

Tephra closed her eyes. Right. Starting tomorrow, it’s several days of sea travel. The route itself isn’t particularly special, and the destination is Marquis Zilbolt’s territory, but we’ll be entering Silvatoria’s coastal waters, or rather, their sphere of influence, so being too careless wouldn’t be good either.

Anyway, having the dragon scale armor completed before crossing over is reassuring.

+++

# **248 – The Voyage to Silvatoria**

“Well then, Theo-kun, take good care of yourself.”

“Yeah. Next time, in Termwills.”

“It feels a bit strange that we’re seeing you off here, then meeting again in Termwills when we return.”

“That’s true.”

Alfred, who had come to see us off at the harbor, and I exchanged wry smiles.

The next day. Blue skies with summer clouds. A transparent sea. It was a perfectly clear day, ideal for departure.

Alfred would be staying in the Marquisate of Fobrester for a few days. After that, he planned to return to Termwills with Ophelia and Viola in a Dragon Palanquin, escorted by the Marquisate’s Knight Order. So, the next time we’d meet would likely be after teleporting back from Mt. Tephra.

“Well then, everyone. May fortune favor you.”

“Ophelia-sama, let’s meet again in Termwills.”

“Yes. Ashley-sama.”

Ashley and Ophelia took each other’s hands as they exchanged words.

“Romina-sama, please stay well too. Do come visit Termwills again.”

“Yes, definitely.”

Ophelia and Romina seemed to have become quite friendly during their journey together. Ophelia had apparently helped bring Talcott and Cindy together as well, so she seemed to be good at looking after others.

Next to them, Princess Stephania and Marquis Fobrester were also exchanging farewells.

“Marquis Fobrester. Thank you for your warm hospitality.”

“I pray for the safety of your journey, so that Your Highness may fulfill your duties without incident and return safely to Termwills.”

“Thank you.”

Marquis Fobrester turned to face Marquis Zilbolt and bowed.

“Well then, Marquis Fobrester. I look forward to the day we meet again.”

“As do I, Marquis Zilbolt.”

“Now then—shall we go?”

Princess Stephania said quietly.

We climbed the gangway and all boarded the ship. The crew hurriedly ran about the deck, the anchor was raised, and sails were hoisted on the mast.

The sails caught the wind, and the ship began to move. From the deck, we waved to Alfred and the others who had come to see us off. They waved back, their figures slowly growing smaller.

Beyond the sea lay the country where Mother was born. And—the country that had driven Mother out.

“—Silvatoria, huh.”

“Is that… Lady Lisa’s homeland?”

When I murmured while watching the shrinking harbor, Grace responded. Ashley also looked concerned. Neither of them thought Mother was at fault. So that was… probably their concern for me. Had something shown on my face?

“Yeah. I think that’s probably correct.”

I smiled and replied.

“…It’s fine. It has nothing to do with our life back then.”

I put my arm around Grace’s waist and held Ashley’s shoulder.

“—Yes.”

The two nodded quietly and gently leaned closer.

Patricia the magician from Silvatoria, and Mother—Lisa. There was likely no doubt they were the same person.

Based on what Marquis Zilbolt had told me, it wasn’t hard to imagine that Mother had been associated with the academy head’s faction at the Sages’ Academy.

Driven by the Crown Prince’s schemes and the effects of the Faction Conflict, she probably fled the country to protect some kind of magic, technique, or item—and herself. But if that were the case, Mother had done nothing wrong. She was simply tossed about by the whims of those above her.

After holding the two for a while, I met Marlene’s gaze.

“Marlene.”

When I called her name, she came over with slightly quickened steps. When I pulled her into an embrace, she hugged me back, pressing her cheek against my chest. Marlene had probably overheard my conversation with Grace and the others.

When I then glanced at Claudia and Rosemary, Claudia’s cheeks flushed slightly, and Rosemary covered her face with her feather fan.

“If being on deck is the problem, should we go to the cabin?”

“No, it’s fine. I heard the conversation.”

“…That’s right. There’s no need to hold back.”

I pulled Claudia into an embrace, and Rosemary moved around to my back on her own, wrapping her arms around my shoulders. A brief embrace.

Or perhaps… if it were Zadias, he might call the elders sending Mother away an act of betrayal against the country. But as far as we’re concerned, accusations stemming from the Crown Prince’s convenience are none of our business. Mother’s life after she escaped—that was everything to me, and that’s all that matters.

Yeah. There’s no need to be nervous at all. Let’s change my mindset.

“Ah… Should I ask the captain if we can go fishing? Sheila, we brought several fishing rods, right?”

“Mm. I brought extras.”

Sheila nodded. Since we knew it would be a sea voyage, Claire the Arachne had prepared long fishing lines for us, thinking it might help pass the time on the ship.

Well, if the captain said no, then it would be a no… but judging by his appearance, he seemed like a rather bold person. We might get permission.

Right now—it was just after departure, and he seemed busy at the helm, so maybe I should ask a crew member to relay the message.

“Excuse me, would it be alright if we went fishing later?”

I asked a crew member wearing a bandana. The crew member showed his teeth in a cheerful smile on his sun-tanned face.

“Fishing? Got it. I’ll ask the captain.”

“Any time when he’s free is fine.”

“Is that so? Then I’ll come to your cabin later to let you know.”

“Until then, I’ll play something.”

“Hmm. I like the sounds Irmhild plays.”

Tephra, with Seraphina on her shoulder, reacted to Irmhild’s words.

“Then I’ll have to work hard to live up to your expectations.”

Irmhild rolled up her sleeves, flexing her arm as if showing off her muscles, and laughed.

So we all headed to the cabin. The cabin’s interior was quite luxurious, with high livability.

Marquis Fobrester had said that since we were escorting Princess Stephania to Silvatoria, he had prepared a ship and crew worthy of that task… I see.

Once we settled in the cabin, Irmhild immediately began playing her lute. She said it was a piece she learned from Justia the Siren.

A knock echoed through the cabin.

“Come in.”

When Princess Stephania responded, a bearded man holding a pipe entered the cabin. He was dressed exactly as you’d expect—captain’s hat and coat. This was Captain Montague, whom Marquis Fobrester had strongly vouched for as a trustworthy person.

Apparently, he had originally belonged to the Knight Order and now mainly transported goods between Termwills and the Marquisate, or was often used when the Marquis himself traveled to Termwills.

“Sorry for the rush. Took me a while to get back to you… oh, pardon me. An old habit slipped out. The sailors seem more comfortable with this way of speaking.”

Captain Montague gave a wry smile at his own manner of speaking, shook his head, and corrected his broken speech.

“Not at all. Sorry for the trouble.”

I hadn’t expected the captain to come here personally just for something like fishing permission.

“Not at all. You’re important guests, after all. I was planning to come greet you anyway. Her Highness Stephania and the Otherworld Ambassador.”

“I see.”

“So, welcome, everyone, to my Emeraldia.”

“Pleased to meet you, Captain Montague.”

At Princess Stephania’s words, Montague returned a salute. I see. It made sense that he was formerly a knight. His knight-style salute was polished, you could say. Though normally he’s probably a man of the sea.

“About the fishing—I’d like you to wear safety ropes if possible. The deck can be a bit unsteady, and it can be dangerous if you’re not used to it.”

“In that case, we can use magic or Magic Tools to fly in the air. How about that?”

“Ah, that’s right. Well, having magicians on board is reassuring, and the sailors are happy about it too.”

“Is that so?”

“Yes. You can create wind even in a calm, and make drinking water too.”

I see. So if something unexpected happens during the voyage, having magicians aboard means they can handle it.

“Then please let us help with water replenishment and Purification until we arrive.”

“Oh, that would be wonderful! A voyage with abundant water is unheard of normally!”

The captain grinned, showing his teeth. It seemed more appreciated than I had imagined. Certainly, I’ve often heard that fresh water is precious during sea voyages.

By replenishing water ourselves, we can also use water abundantly without hesitation. Though it’s a sea voyage, being able to do laundry, bathe, and such freely is probably quite luxurious.

The captain is frank and reasonable, and with this, the voyage to the Marquisate of Zilbolt seems like it will be quite enjoyable.

+++

# **249 – Silvatoria of the Northern Country**

Irmhild sat on the edge of the deck, playing melodies on her lute to accompany the sailors’ sea shanties. The music seemed to be Irmhild’s improvisation matching the sailors’ songs. Beside her, everyone was lined up fishing from the ship.

The sea voyage was proceeding smoothly. It was summer. They had favorable winds while heading north, and since this was one of the established routes, the risk of being attacked by large monsters was originally low.

The wyverns were also flying around the ship for their amusement, making things even safer. Thanks to that, even small monsters didn’t approach.

If they could have crossed the sea using the Lindwurms, it would have been faster, but when transporting the dragon palanquin, even the wyverns needed to rest their wings periodically. Hence the sea voyage.

“—Got one.”

Sheila pulled her fishing rod and a red fish was hooked.

“You’re quite good at fishing, Sheila.”

At Claudia’s admiring words, Sheila nodded.

“During my Thieves Guild training days, I survived by fishing.”

“I see…”

…That would certainly make one skilled. There’s a saying that one excels at what one enjoys, and it seemed true that she genuinely loved all kinds of seafood. Previously, when they tasted the giant mantis shrimp hunted in the Magic Light Water Vein, it seemed her evaluation of it completely flipped.

So, combined with her sharp senses, Sheila had been achieving considerable fishing results for days.

Everyone was fishing, then simply cooking the catch—grilling with Fire Magic or boiling in pots—before eating.

In the ship’s hold, Lavigne was also freeze-preserving them, so the food lasted longer. With their diet being so fulfilling, the sailors seemed to be in good spirits too.

“I hear we’ll reach Marquis Zilbolt’s territory today… Should we save this for dinner?”

“Yeah. I’m looking forward to it.”

Sheila nodded while looking at the bucket piled high with the day’s catch. If possible, she wanted to use seasonings lavishly when eating them.

“Land ho—!”

A crew member’s voice came from atop the mast.

Silvatoria—the land of Marquis Zilbolt’s territory. The captain gripped the helm, and the sailors’ movements became hurried.

The port town gradually drew closer. The roofs were mostly orange or brown, and the walls cream-colored—warm-toned buildings predominated. It was quite a colorful townscape.

In the distance, a castle—and a large mountain mass were visible. That was Marquis Zilbolt’s castle residence. And beyond that, Mt. Tephra.

“What a pretty town… There are many houses with rich colors.”

“Since the winter cold is severe, they color the house walls like that to receive the sun’s warmth.”

“I see… So there’s a proper reason.”

At Ashley’s words, Princess Stephania, who was familiar with Silvatoria, provided an explanation. Marlene nodded thoughtfully alongside Ashley.

Hmm. Indeed… In warm climates like the Mediterranean, the image is of port towns with white houses and small windows. The north is the opposite—colorful townscapes with large windows.

Marquis Zilbolt’s castle residence was also quite colorful overall, with a reddish, brick-like hue and turquoise roofs.

“Well, my territory is located in southern Silvatoria, and we also have Lady Tephra’s blessings, so it’s relatively warm and comfortable to live in. However, it’s good that you all came during summer. For those accustomed to the Kingdom of Verdugal’s climate, I think you’ll find it cool and pleasant.”

Marquis Zilbolt added further explanation to the impressed Ashley and Marlene.

“That’s certainly true. The coolness doesn’t seem to be just because we’re on the ship.”

Rosemary murmured, reaching her hand out to the wind.

“Please be careful not to get cold at dawn.”

“That’s right. I don’t want to catch a summer cold. But there are hot springs, aren’t there?”

“Yes. Hot water is piped to both the castle and the town.”

“Ah. That must be Mt. Tephra over there.”

Grace said while looking at the distant mountain. Tephra nodded in response to Grace’s words.

“Indeed. Words of welcome… might be something I should not say, but perhaps Zilbolt should.”

“That may be so. Then, once again—”

Marquis Zilbolt placed his hands on his hips, bowed respectfully, and smiled.

“Welcome, and thank you for coming. I welcome you all.”

The ship continued onward into the dock. The mast was folded, the anchor dropped, and the gangplank lowered.

…My mother’s home country. Not exactly her birthplace, I suppose. Still, with slight emotion, I stepped onto the dock.

As soon as they disembarked at the port, soldiers approached for procedures. However, upon noticing Marquis Zilbolt, who had removed his hood, they saluted with surprised expressions to welcome him.

“Wha—! Marquis…!”

The ship was different from the one they took to Termwills, and their return was earlier than expected. For them, it must have come completely out of the blue.

“Indeed. You all, good work on your duties.”

“Yes, sir!”

“While I was away, was there anything unusual?”

“Nothing abnormal, sir!”

At the soldier’s report, Marquis Zilbolt nodded quietly.

“We will now head to the castle using the dragon palanquin brought on the ship. Relay that to the guard post. However, due to the emergency situation, do not leak information to outsiders. Those who recklessly leak information will be punished. Understood?”

“Y… Yes, sir!”

The soldiers began moving hurriedly at Marquis Zilbolt’s words.

So… after notifications were completed with the Knight Order and soldiers, they would move via the dragon palanquin.

After that, they planned to proceed with formal wanted notices using Alvelinde’s bust and portrait. There were also other tasks like having his subordinate Intelligence Unit report any visits from the Crown Prince’s agents… With many miscellaneous tasks, the Marquis would likely be somewhat busy.

“Marquis. We intend to move to collect information to verify the soldiers’ words and check if there’s any information they aren’t aware of.”

Said Elmer.

“Indeed.”

As the Marquis nodded, Elmer, Donovan, and the Intelligence Unit quickly ran into the town.

While waiting for the soldiers to finish notifications and return, they proceeded with preparations for moving—unloading luggage and hitching the wyverns to the dragon palanquin.

“Notifications completed without issue, sir.”

“Indeed. Good work.”

Marquis Zilbolt gave a brief reply to the returning, saluting soldier.

“Well then, Captain Montague, thank you for your care.”

Princess Stephania said to the captain.

“Your words are too kind, Your Highness. I am proud to have safely delivered you to Silvatoria. We will be docked here for several days awaiting the arrival of Marquis Zilbolt’s ship, correct?”

“Yes. I’ll count on you again then.”

“As you wish, Your Highness.”

They would part ways here with Captain Montague and the sailors for now. In a few days, Marquis Zilbolt’s ship carrying his household servants was scheduled to arrive at this port.

At that time, there might be movements from people dispatched by the Crown Prince’s side. They planned to use the ship as a base to monitor that or capture them.

Until then, the sailors were free. Getting shore leave seemed to be long-awaited time for the sailors, as their excitement was quite high. Especially since there were hot springs too.

In contrast, the sailors remaining on deck were probably those on standby for ship watch duty. Their morale was so low the divide was stark. What’s called “half the crew ashore,” I suppose.

“You lot! I get that you’re excited to be ashore, but behave yourselves properly so you don’t embarrass yourselves in front of the guests we brought!”

“Aye, Captain!”

The captain was scolding the excited shore-leave group.

Guests—meaning since this is the Marquis’s territory, don’t go overboard and cause trouble.

Sailors have to maintain discipline at sea, so it’s a common story that they tend to get too excited and rowdy once they reach land.

Now then. While all this was happening, the dragon palanquin was ready. First, they would head to Marquis Zilbolt’s castle residence, and once safety was confirmed, then Mt. Tephra… probably.

However, right now there was fog covering the mountaintop. Conditions were somewhat poor for heading there directly via dragon palanquin.

“Hmm. I’d like to reach the point where I can take this off soon.”

If Tephra walked around the Marquis’s territory, it would likely cause a huge commotion. For now, she was covered from head to toe in a long robe to remain inconspicuous, so she seemed somewhat cramped.

Tephra’s hair resembled flames, but for some reason, the hood didn’t burn. In Tephra’s case, it was just warm, not hot.

“Once we’re inside the dragon palanquin, you can probably take it off, right?”

“Is that so? Then I’ll take you up on that.”

Saying this, Tephra eagerly boarded the dragon palanquin. Seraphina entered the dragon palanquin following Tephra. Ignis, Ambrum, and others who would cause a commotion if seen were already inside.

“Alright. Then, head for the castle.”

Once everyone was aboard the dragon palanquin, I gave instructions to the Lindwurm. The Lindwurm had also grown accustomed to acting as the leader of the wyverns; with one command, it masterfully coordinated the flock.

Looking down upon the Marquis’s colorful townscape below, the dragon palanquin carrying us flew toward Marquis Zilbolt’s castle residence.

+++

# **250 – Preparation for Counterattack**

“First, I shall gather the main individuals we can trust in the castle’s great dining hall. We must report what has transpired and give instructions for what comes next.”

“May I also be present?”

“Of course. To smoothly proceed with matters once we head for the royal capital, we must unify and communicate our intentions.”

Inside the dragon palanquin, Marquis Zilbolt and Princess Stephania were coordinating their plans for after arriving at the castle. As her escort, I needed to be present for that.

Considering Tephra’s recognition within Marquis Zilbolt’s territory, having her attend would be the quickest way to facilitate smooth discussions.

“If I’m leaving the palanquin, I suppose I should keep this on a bit longer.”

“Indeed. My apologies for the discomfort.”

“Think nothing of it. It’s for my friend.”

Tephra smiled as she wrapped herself in her robe.

Even though we were having Tephra attend to gain trust, we needed to carefully select who would see her true form.

When the dragon palanquin landed in the castle’s training grounds, knights immediately came running.

“Welcome back, Marquis.”

“Yes. You’ve done well guarding the territory in my absence.”

The knights bowed to the Marquis while briefly glancing at us. However, they seemed determined to maintain their position of waiting for the Marquis’s explanation without saying anything.

“Gather everyone. I wish to hear reports from my absence. I will also explain what has transpired during this time.”

“Yes, sir!”

“As for who to summon—”

The knights ran off after receiving detailed instructions from Marquis Zilbolt. The Marquis turned to face us and spoke.

“My apologies for the haste. Under normal circumstances, we should be welcoming you properly.”

“Given the situation…”

“Indeed. Let’s save the festivities for after everything has been settled.”

At my words, Princess Stephania and the Marquis twisted the corners of their mouths.

“Then, this way.”

We were led to the castle’s great dining hall under the Marquis’s guidance. Soon, the territory’s key figures were gathered.

“Everyone, you have done well protecting the territory during my absence. First, your reports.”

“Yes, sir!”

A man wearing armor with feather decorations on the shoulders stood up and assumed a salute. He appeared to be the Knight Order Commander of the territory.

Though his title was Knight Order Commander, he was also responsible for skill training for the intelligence unit.

“The town remains calm. There have been several minor incidents like fights, disputes, and theft, but no major problems have occurred.”

“I see.”

The Marquis nodded and scanned the room, where another person—a man in robes who seemed to be a magician—stood up and saluted like the Commander. This person appeared to be responsible for training successors in magic skills for the intelligence unit.

“Same as the Commander. No notable movements in the surrounding areas either.”

“What about visitors to the territory?”

“We have not identified any requiring special mention. As previously notified, only Viscount Foble has visited for hot spring treatment. As for merchants coming and going, only our regular large-scale traders from the past.”

Just as the soldiers at the port had said. At least within their knowledge, no major problems seemed to have occurred in Marquis Zilbolt’s territory. Well, that was assuming we exclude the Crown Prince incident.

“Hmm… Continue with your respective tasks as before. Report promptly if anything changes.”

“Yes, sir!”

The Commander and magician answered in unison.

“Now, I must address what everyone is curious about—but first, I want you to see this.”

Saying this, the Marquis placed a wooden box on the table.

When he took out Alvelinde’s bust from inside, their expressions changed.

“This person—”

“A w-witch…”

Both of them contorted their expressions. These two were looking at a witch. At the very least, those gathered here were key figures who knew some of the Marquis’s circumstances.

“I shall inform you that the witch problem has been resolved by the hero of Termwills. The concerns about the spirit of Mt. Tephra and the corrosion affecting my wife and daughter have vanished.”

As the Marquis spoke, Tephra first removed her hood, then took off her robe.

A stir ran through the room at Tephra’s appearance.

“A sp-spirit…! F-fiery hair and those goat legs… c-could it be…!?”

“Spirit Tephra…!?”

“O-oh…!”

The eyes of those present widened. Tephra answered calmly.

“I was saved by my friend in Termwills. To repay that debt and friendship, I am here now.”

“…That witch was a demon who called herself Corrosion Princess Alvelinde.”

“Corrosion Princess!?”

The magician’s eyes widened.

“Indeed. In any case, the Crown Prince had connections with demons. Understand that this is a grave matter that could lead to crisis for Silvatoria’s survival… no, potentially even worse.”

The consecutive bombshell statements from the Marquis made the key figures either widen their eyes or swallow hard.

“I have also had an audience with His Majesty Melvin, King of Verdugal. His Majesty Melvin has dispatched his first princess, Her Highness Stephania, as an envoy to our country. Once preparations are complete, I must go to the royal capital and, together with Her Highness, inform His Majesty about these events.”

“I-I see. Then, this person here is…”

“Precisely. Her Highness Stephania, First Princess of the Kingdom of Verdugal. That is who stands before you.”

Princess Stephania, introduced by the Marquis, gracefully bowed.

“Not only Her Highness Stephania, but all are distinguished guests without equal. Ensure there are no mishaps.”

“Yes, sir!”

The Marquis was somewhat vague in his introductions.

No attention came to me. Though I wasn’t wearing my disguise ring, I was dressed as a butler. Being seen as just an attendant to Princess Stephania and remaining completely unnoticed was easier.

“Have copies made of this plaster statue. Prepare to issue notices identifying her as a felon within and outside the territory. The existence of the plaster statue, my return, and the visit of the Verdugal Kingdom’s envoy group are to be kept secret until further orders. Understand that anyone who leaks information will not be forgiven, regardless of reason.”

“Yes, sir! As you command!”

“…Due to that individual’s deeds, we have long tasted bitterness… but that has come to an end, I take it.”

The Knight Commander stood at attention while saluting, and the magician looked up at the sky as if overcome with emotion. Tears even welled in the corners of his eyes.

“…Come to think of it, I’ve put you all through considerable hardship.”

At the Marquis’s words as he closed his eyes, the Knight Commander also took a deep breath and said quietly.

“Your words are too generous. Though we have endured drinking muddy water together with our lord, if we consider it all for this day, this moment, then it feels rewarded.”

“Then… what we must do next is be wary of collaborators, I suppose.”

Right. We couldn’t rule out the possibility of such individuals being among us.

“Have them always move in groups of three, and restrict out-of-territory travel for those involved. Not even we are exceptions. As for issuing notices and arrangements regarding the witch’s appearance outside the territory… ensure it’s done with the minimum necessary information.”

“Very well. For the witch’s crimes, identify her as the perpetrator of attempted assassination of nobility. The date for issuing notices will be after my ship returns to port.”

“Yes, sir! Then… regarding team assignments, I would like to show you the details later and receive your approval.”

“Understood. Begin immediately.”

“Yes, sir!”

This efficiency was perhaps worthy of an intelligence unit leader. They returned the salute and left the great dining hall to attend to their duties.

Well… We’ve somewhat secured safety within the castle. That means once the mountaintop fog clears, our next step should be heading to Mt. Tephra via dragon palanquin.

“Sometimes the fog doesn’t clear until dark. First, you should rest from your journey and recover your energy.”

The Marquis said to me.

“That’s true. Since we still have time, going to Mt. Tephra doesn’t need to happen immediately. Let’s check the situation tomorrow morning.”

Whether the Crown Prince’s associates would appear when the ship entered port. We didn’t know what Alvelinde had planned after returning to Silvatoria… but when the time came, we would have everything prepared to depart for the royal capital by dragon palanquin.

“Then… let me show you to the guest rooms.”

In the end, the fog didn’t clear until evening. The trip to Mt. Tephra was postponed until tomorrow.

We would stay at the castle tonight, and everything would begin tomorrow.

While we were all relaxing in the guest room around dinner time, a knock sounded at the door.

“Enter.”

Marquis Zilbolt prompted entry.

Since they were protection targets, the members of Marquis Zilbolt’s household were also in the guest room. With many people to protect this time, having them gathered in one place made things easier for us.

“Excuse me.”

Elmer entered as he spoke. Kneeling on the spot, he reported.

“It appears the magic knight Benedict has visited our territory. I came to report immediately.”

We inadvertently exchanged glances. That royal guard official employed by the Crown Prince… the masked magic knight.

If his purpose was to welcome the witch… it wouldn’t be strange for him to appear early and stay in the territory… Well. Whether he had other purposes or not.

“Surveillance?”

“We have it in place. Benedict himself appears to be staying at an inn within the territory.”

“…He won’t come to the castle? Benedict probably knows the Marquis is currently absent.”

“That… seems likely.”

That Benedict wasn’t visiting the castle was… well, normal.

“The question is whether he knows anything beyond that, perhaps?”

As Grace tilted her head, Rosemary played with her feather fan while pondering and answered.

“If he suspected a trap, he wouldn’t stay within the territory. If any collaborators visited him, they could be captured in one sweep.”

“What about the possibility he’s acting as bait to probe the situation?”

“I wouldn’t say it’s impossible… but it’s a dangerous move.”

At Ashley and Claudia’s exchange, Marquis Zilbolt placed his hand on his chin and thought deeply, but soon gave instructions to Elmer.

“Continue surveillance. If anyone from the royal castle approaches him, capture them. However, do not make any moves against him personally.”

“Yes, sir!”

Elmer saluted and left the guest room. Conversely speaking… if there were collaborators, this would be a good opportunity to smoke them out.

“Well. What should we do?”

“Nothing changes. The ritual at Mt. Tephra should remain our top priority.”

This was absolutely essential for securing our retreat route.

“Beyond that, we monitor and judge whether Benedict himself is friend or foe based on how he moves when he learns the witch has been designated a felon… that’s about it. Since he might be a demon, carelessly making a move from our side would be dangerous.”

“Indeed…”

At that time—I needed to prepare a situation where I could directly confront him.

+++

# **251 – To Mount Tephra**

“Could you tell me where Benedict is staying?”

“One moment, please. I’ll have someone bring a map.”

The Marquis gave some instructions to his servants, and they prepared a map for us.

“According to the contact, Benedict is staying at this inn.”

I compared my memory of the town’s layout from above with the positions marked on the map. The location Marquis Zilbolt pointed to—I see. So he’s taken up residence at an inn near the harbor. It would be best to send Caduceus nearby and keep watch from here as well. This way we can grasp the situation faster than waiting for messengers and respond immediately if there’s any movement.

Caduceus, having received my instructions, liquefied and slipped out through a window crack. As for Benedict… we’ll observe the situation as it is for now.

“As for Mt. Tephra… let’s depart early tomorrow morning while checking the weather. Moving by Dragon Palanquin will be conspicuous, but we can disguise it with Light Magic and Illusion Magic so it can’t be seen from town.”

“Understood.”

Marquis Zilbolt is also contractually involved in managing the Gate connecting the Termwilz Ritual Site and Mt. Tephra. Therefore, the Marquis himself needs to accompany us. That means our escort targets need to move together as a group.

“I hope the fog clears.”

“What about using my eyes?”

“In that case, Seraphina and I too, perhaps?”

Sheila and Irmhild responded to Princess Stephania’s words.

Indeed… even with poor visibility, the two’s detection abilities and Seraphina’s capabilities should handle most situations, but…

“…Right. We have time, and I’d prefer to take it easy if possible.”

“Yeah! I’ll do my best too!”

Seraphina clenched her fists and darted around left and right.

Hmm. Since Benedict arrived early, we can’t afford to be that leisurely anymore. To some extent, it can’t be helped.

“Alright. Then… let’s go while also incorporating detection training.”

Everyone nodded at my words.

The next day. In the slightly chilly early morning air, we prepared to head for Mt. Tephra. We readied cold-weather gear and preserved food just in case. Our destination was the summit—near the crater.

The distance from the Marquis’s castle town could be said to be right under our noses—but since it’s quite a high mountain with proportionally wide foothills, it’s somewhat far to the summit.

“Shall we go then?”

“What about Wind Protection Magic?”

Rosemary inquired.

“Can you use it?”

“Yes. I learned it before thinking it might be useful in case something happens.”

In case something happens, huh. It feels more like a card prepared solely for emergency escape measures…

“Then, please handle it.”

The Wind Protection Magic when riding the Dragon Palanquin is for atmospheric pressure countermeasures.

Normally, we don’t fly the Dragon Palanquin that high, but it might be necessary when heading for the summit. We’ve learned from operating Dragon Palanquins that suddenly gaining too much altitude can cause problems.

“We used to transfer casually anywhere in the labyrinth… but since the altitudes differ between Mt. Tephra and the ritual site, should we be careful?”

“You should be able to transfer to locations corresponding to the ritual site’s position. Though the contract itself requires going to the crater.”

Claudia answered for us.

“I see. As long as it’s away from populated areas… we just need to transfer to lower elevations then.”

It seems we don’t need to be too careful. Let’s go then.

“Alright, let’s go, Marlene.”

Marlene gave a small nod.

Instead of riding the Dragon Palanquin, I flew beside Lindwurm. Marlene’s Lantern covered us from behind with the sky’s color, and I further refracted the scenery with Light Magic for camouflage. This should make us nearly invisible from below. Once we’re farther away, we’ll use Water Magic to cover our rear with fog, making us undetectable from a distance.

Leaving the Marquis’s castle town, a tranquil hilly area covered in green spread out before us. This area already constitutes Mt. Tephra’s foothills. Purple and yellow flowers bloomed here and there across the green carpet, swaying in the morning sunlight.

“What a lovely view.”

Grace peeked her face out from the Dragon Palanquin’s window, her expression softening.

“If we weren’t in a hurry, it would have been nice to explore around here.”

“Indeed. That wouldn’t be bad either.”

“In the river flowing from the mountain lake, there are places where hot water springs forth.”

Romina explained happily.

“Natural open-air baths? Tempting, but… after we resolve everything.”

Once we can establish the Gate, we’ll be able to visit casually.

We advanced while enjoying the scenery for a while until the slope gradually became steeper. It was about time to use Water Magic to create fog covering our rear and release the Light Magic camouflage.

“Okay. Marlene, thank you.”

At my words, Marlene gave a small nod and showed an unclouded smile before returning to the Dragon Palanquin.

“Then, I’m coming out.”

In exchange, Sheila and Irmhild emerged from the Dragon Palanquin. Seraphina and Lavigne also came out.

The plan was for Ashley and Lavigne to coordinate and grasp terrain information. Furthermore, by having Seraphina—riding on Lavigne’s back—send sounds, Sheila would detect them through sound perception. Irmhilt would sense Lavigne’s temperature.

This way, even with poor visibility due to fog, the Dragon Palanquin could proceed safely without colliding with the mountain.

“I’ll let you know when caution is needed.”

“Understood. Lindwurm, slow down moderately while we proceed.”

Receiving my instructions, Lindwurm made a sound. The Dragon Palanquin reduced speed and carefully advanced through the fog.

Now then. What about the town’s situation? Caduceus was waiting in the shadows of back alleys near Benedict’s inn.

Then… movement. The figure emerging from the inn’s entrance. Instantly recognizable.

A tricorne hat and surcoat outfit. On his face—a mask covering from forehead to nose, like one worn to a masquerade. Well… unlike those for balls, the decorations seem modest.

The left side of his face. Burn scars around the cheek. Slightly protruding from the mask… To hide the burn scars? I see. That story doesn’t seem to be false.

But still… even without seeing his features, he’s quite conspicuous.

That said, being conspicuous probably doesn’t work against Crown Prince Zadias’s interests. After all, since he believes he’s holding Tephra, the Marquis’s wife, and daughter hostage, he must think we can’t make a move even if his people flaunt their presence in the territory.

Rather, Benedict showing himself could be said to have the meaning of warning the people of the Marquis’s territory.

In that case… his role is either to welcome the witch or simply confirm the witch’s return and report.

Benedict’s footsteps were in a Natural Stance. A leisurely pace like taking a stroll… but it’s actually an inconvenient speed for tailing. Showing relaxation while leaving no openings—seems the stories of his competence are true. Elmer and the others must be having some difficulty dealing with him too.

It appears he intends to walk to the harbor. I had Caduceus follow him, sliding from shadow to shadow across surfaces.

Eventually Benedict reached the harbor. Still at his relaxed pace, he looked around the buildings near the wharf and the docked ships. Probably scouting the harbor area?

A sea breeze blew. Benedict held down his tricorne hat with his hand.

Apparently disliking it nearly flying off, he took the hat in his hand and let out a small sigh. White hair—no, silver hair. From the impression of his mouth, he doesn’t seem elderly though…

Having finished checking the harbor, Benedict returned to his inn via the same route he came.

“Hmm…”

“Something wrong?”

“No, Benedict showed himself. He seemed to be scouting the harbor before returning.”

I answered Sheila’s question.

As Mt. Tephra’s elevation increased, the Dragon Palanquin also gained altitude, causing the temperature to drop considerably. Plants became sparse, and rugged rocks became prominent.

There seem to be wild goats too. Perpetual snow is visible in the shade.

“I see it. The crater.”

Tephra said. The summit forms a clear depression. There’s no visible magma or smoke rising… but if this erupted, Marquis Zilbolt’s territory would certainly be in trouble.

“Okay. Lindwurm, circle around and look for a place to land the Dragon Palanquin.”

We slowly circled the crater and carefully landed the Dragon Palanquin on a somewhat flattened rocky area… The balance is a bit unstable?

“I’ll support it from the lower side of the slope.”

“Understood. It’ll just be for a short while.”

“Yes.”

Grace smiled. After releasing the seal, Grace got out of the Dragon Palanquin, went around, and placed her hands on it to secure it from rolling.

“Then, let’s begin.”

Claudia, Tephra, and Marquis Zilbolt descended into the crater. When Claudia held her hand over the ground, a large Magic Circle spread from her feet.

“Tephra, Marquis. Step into the circle.”

“Right.”

“…Is this alright?”

“Yes. Then, I’ll begin.”

The patterns of the Magic Circle spreading from Claudia’s feet began to Spin. The rotation gradually accelerated—until a pillar of faint light rose up.

“Give your consent to my words. First, Tephra.”

“Right.”

“I build a path here. Spirit Tephra. Do you acknowledge the gate’s existence in this land?”

“I acknowledge it.”

The moment she answered, phosphorescent light wrapped around Tephra’s body.

“Marquis Zilbolt. As the lord governing this land, will you bear the responsibility of safeguarding the key?”

“Indeed, I shall take custody with responsibility.”

Similarly, phosphorescent light wrapped around the Marquis. The light shone brightly for just a moment before disappearing like bursting.

Claudia exhaled deeply and opened her eyes.

“…It’s done. I built the path, Tephra acknowledged the gate, and the Marquis safeguards the key.”

Good. Now we’ve safely secured our retreat route too. Once we verify the Gate’s performance, we’ll focus on the Benedict problem.

+++

# **252 – Operation Begins**

“Alright, we’re moving now.”

From Mt. Tephra to the ritual site. We moved together with everyone and the wyverns.

The moment light spread from the teleportation magic array expanding from Claudia’s feet, we found ourselves in the courtyard of the ritual site in the next instant. Although we had notified them via communication device, the shrine maidens of the Moon Temple wore slightly surprised expressions.

When Marlene waved her hand, the shrine maidens broke into smiles and returned a bow. Good.

“How’s your magical power consumption?”

“…Well. It’s more draining than regular labyrinth teleportation, but with the contract and Tephra’s power helping… I think it should be fine as long as we don’t do it repeatedly in a short period.”

Claudia answered while opening and closing her hand.

This was assuming circulating ki, but… it should be well within practical limits.

“This is my second time doing this… but it’s quite reassuring.”

Marquis Zilbolt nodded while looking around.

“Master.”

Then Cecilia arrived. We’d been communicating with Termwills through regular contact via communication device, but I’d contacted various parties via communication device last night to inform them we were heading to Mt. Tephra. It seemed Cecilia had been waiting for us at the ritual site.

“I’ve prepared everything as requested. They’ve been loaded onto the carriage.”

“Okay. Thank you.”

Cecilia bowed quietly.

“Then we should start loading the supplies immediately.”

I generated the Golems, had them carry the no-longer-needed luggage to the carriage, and loaded the supplies prepared for us—food, clothing, equipment, and such—into the dragon palanquin.

“You’ve arrived, Theodore.”

While we were working, King Melvin and Alfred also came.

“Yes. Zadias’s men have been spotted in Marquis Zilbolt’s territory.”

“…Hmm. We can’t afford to take it too easy then.”

“That’s right. We need to return soon.”

We could tell whether there were any abnormalities over there through Caduceus’s communication device, but it was beyond the range of the Five Senses Link. We needed to return there as quickly as possible.

“Take utmost care.”

“Yes. We’re off.”

I smiled and nodded at King Melvin.

“Welcome back from your sea voyage. How’s the armor treating you?”

Asked Alfred.

“Ah, I’m back. I tested it on the ship, and it’s quite easy to move in and feels good. How was your vacation?”

“Thanks to you. I was able to spend quite a relaxing time with Ophelia. I ended up making some magic tools while I was there too.”

Alfred said with a wry smile.

“Hmm. What did you make?”

“Self-defense magic tools for the Marquis. You know. The one we only had a concept for before—the one that emits a bright light when smashed against the ground.”

“Ah, that one.”

In other words, it was a flash grenade using light magic. Since it consumed magic stones, there were cost issues for regular use, but considering it for VIP protection in emergencies, that shouldn’t be a problem.

“I made some extras when I had time after returning to Termwills. I’ll give them to you, Theo-kun.”

“Oh. Thank you.”

He handed me a wooden box containing the magic tools. They were perfectly suited magic tools for heading into enemy territory. It would be best if we didn’t need to use them, but as they say, better safe than sorry. I gratefully accepted them.

“The loading is complete.”

Ashley came to call me.

“Understood. Then, we’re returning to the other side.”

“Okay. Be careful.”

“Right. I’ll contact you via communication device.”

Amidst the farewells from King Melvin, Alfred, and Cecilia, we flew again using Claudia’s teleportation magic.

“Then let’s go.”

Enveloped in light—when I opened my eyes, we were by the lakeside halfway up Mt. Tephra.

Cool, humid air. There didn’t seem to be anyone else around besides us.

While assessing the surrounding situation, I first linked with Caduceus. …Hmm. There don’t seem to be any particular changes. In that case, we should first return to the castle and proceed with preparations as planned.

After returning to Marquis Zilbolt’s territory—it could be said that my work had temporarily settled down.

While my role as escort remained, since the castle staff were handling the arrangements for announcing the witch, all I had to do was monitor Benedict and the ship returning from Termwills.

Since I had some free time, I stationed myself in the castle’s watchtower and used light magic to create a telescope to watch the sea.

This was to know as soon as possible when the ship from Termwills arrived. Meanwhile, Benedict’s side still showed no notable movements.

Apparently, that magic knight was officially here on vacation… but given how he was carefully investigating where alleys connected throughout the town, he might have been informed of some degree of danger. The question was—how much did he actually know?

But all that ends today. Once he’s informed about the witch, we should be able to determine whether he’s friend or foe based on his reaction. The situation was set to move simultaneously with the ship’s arrival.

“Can you see the ship?”

Ashley popped her head up after climbing the ladder from below. She had some cut sugar candy in her hand. It seemed she had come to bring us some. Princess Stephania and Romina were with her too.

“No, not yet. It should be appearing any moment now though.”

“Is that so? Romina-sama and I stopped by the kitchen to bring some treats. Would you like some?”

“Thank you. Shall we eat together?”

“Yes.”

Ashley smiled and nodded.

“Let me join you too. I’ve always—somewhat admired this kind of work.”

Said Princess Stephania who had come along.

“Is that so?”

“Yes. The more mundane military work is often the most important. However, at the royal castle and my territory, I’m rarely allowed to enter such places.”

…I see. Since there are no surveillance eyes now, she has freedom of movement. Princess Stephania is quite active for someone so approachable.

“Understood. Then, please do.”

“Thank you.”

We brought a table to a position with a view of the sea and decided to take a break while satisfying our snack cravings.

“I’ll make some tea.”

Ashley used water magic to fill the teapot with hot water and poured it for everyone.

“Thank you, Ashley-sama.”

“You’re welcome.”

Romina, who had received tea, exchanged smiles with Ashley.

“Speaking of which, you two seem to have become quite close.”

When I asked, Romina nodded.

“Me deciding to stay here as much as time allows was something Ashley-sama and I discussed and decided together.”

“Saying it like that makes me a little embarrassed, but.”

“Fufu.”

Ashley looked somewhat shy, and Princess Stephania smiled seeing that.

Ashley’s position… indeed, Romina might see some parallels with herself. The only daughter of a marquis household. With the possibility of becoming the heir, and having suffered health issues due to the mental strain from curse magic. It wouldn’t be strange if they found common ground to empathize with each other.

Romina and the marquise… seemed to have chosen to remain in Marquis Zilbolt’s territory until the last possible moment.

Originally, Marquis Zilbolt wanted Romina and the others to stay in Termwills rather than accompany him… but apparently, Romina and the marquise wanted above all else to show the household retainers their curse-free forms.

And indeed, I think that actually helped boost morale. They were supposed to remain in Marquis Zilbolt’s territory until we departed for the royal capital… so that decision was made after seeing Ashley, was it?

Yet deciding to go to Termwills if the situation moved… probably stemmed from not wanting to become a burden to her father. That aspect might overlap with Ashley, who had conflicts about being assigned to the rearguard.

While we were drinking tea and finishing off the sugar candy like that, a ship appeared on the distant horizon.

“…It’s here.”

Magnifying with the telescopic lens—it was indeed Marquis Zilbolt’s ship. I could sense the tension increasing in everyone’s expressions.

“The ship is visible. I think we should head to the port immediately.”

I made a brief appearance in the VIP room to have a meeting with everyone before we began operations.

“Any changes to the plan?”

Claudia asked.

“As planned. Marquis Zilbolt will handle persuading Benedict. Grace and I will escort the Marquis. If it comes to combat with Benedict, I’ll take him on.”

“Yes. I’ll accompany you.”

We confirmed everyone’s positions for reassurance. Grace placed her hand on her chest and nodded quietly at my words. The reason Grace and I were escorting the Marquis… well, partly because our appearances were less likely to raise suspicion.

“Sheila, Irmhild, Lavigne—in case Benedict attempts to escape, maintain readiness to pursue while keeping distance, and wait on the ship.”

“Mm.”

“Understood.”

And the remaining members would handle escorting Princess Stephania and Tephra, Romina and the marquise.

“The escorts are Ashley, Marlene, Claudia, Rosemary, Seraphina, Ignis, and Ambrum. When Benedict appears at the port, Caduceus will return to the castle.”

This group would handle escort duties and evacuation. When I looked around at everyone and spoke, each of them nodded. With this arrangement, Ashley could monitor the port situation while remaining at the castle. Ambrum was scheduled to take Princess Stephania’s form and act as a shadow clone.

But even though it’s escort duty at the castle, we can’t let our guard down. Assuming there were collaborators with the crown prince, if they decided to use force, the timing would likely be here. They might think they could gain control by taking Romina or the marquise hostage right before the Marquis made his move.

That’s why we’re returning Caduceus—but everyone’s expressions show they’re quite determined. Romina and the marquise chose to remain in the territory until the last possible moment to eliminate future worries. They probably want to honor that sentiment.

“Pass these out to everyone.”

I distributed the flash bombs I received from Alfred to the escort team. I’ll carry one too.

“These are the magic tools Alfred gave you?”

“Yes. They emit a strong light when smashed against the floor. When throwing them, notify everyone and close your eyes.”

“Understood. Well… I don’t think it matters for Ignis though.”

Rosemary giggled while holding the spherical magic tool up to the light. Hmm. Being able to move without any time lag after the flash bomb… that’s quite a vicious coordination.

…Anyway, the operation is finally beginning. Once it starts, it’ll be like rolling down a hill. Whether Benedict is black or white—we’ll soon find out.

+++

# **253 – The Knight in the Mask**

We waited at the soldiers’ guardhouse in the harbor for Marquis Zilbolt’s ship to arrive.

“It appears they’ve arrived.”

“Then, shall we go?”

Just as the sailing ship bearing the Zilbolt family crest approached from offshore, Benedict appeared at the harbor.

“Sir Benedict.”

Marquis Zilbolt called out to Benedict’s back as he watched the sailing ship entering the harbor.

“This is… Marquis Zilbolt.”

Benedict turned around to face Marquis Zilbolt.

Grace and I stood behind like servants accompanying Marquis Zilbolt. We were prepared to block any attacks with a Shield if necessary.

If Benedict were a demon, Ashley would detect it and inform Marlene and Claudia, triggering the Blessing.

“I heard you were away. Why is the Marquis here?”

Benedict asked in a tone with little emotional fluctuation.

Since the ship hadn’t arrived yet, it was strange for Marquis Zilbolt to appear at the harbor first. He probably found this suspicious, but with most of his face hidden, his emotions were hard to read.

“Actually, a problem has arisen. I returned to my territory a bit early to deal with it and give instructions.”

“Oh? And what problem would that be?”

“This.”

Marquis Zilbolt opened a wooden box, revealing the plaster statue of the witch inside. This was a tactic to gauge reactions by revealing critical information without preamble—but Benedict merely glanced at the plaster statue in the box without showing any notable reaction.

“…She is a felon who attempted to assassinate my wife and daughter. Since she’s dangerous, I thought I must go to the royal capital as quickly as possible to report and make arrangements. That’s why I’m having my retainers prepare various things.”
