Benedict remained silent. They faced each other at a fixed distance. The tension in the air was palpable.

“Sir Benedict. You know this person, don’t you?”

“Why… would you think that?”

Faced with this direct question, Benedict evaded giving a clear answer. Marquis Zilbolt continued without waiting for a response.

“She is someone I came to know through an introduction from His Highness Zadias. Both you and I are close to His Highness Zadias. As for me… I can’t help but wonder if there might be some reason other than vacation for your visit here. Especially… coming to this harbor on this day, at this time.”

Our goal was to strike without warning, without informing the Crown Prince beforehand. To prevent the Crown Prince from preparing his defenses, we needed to detain Benedict by some means.

That’s why we were indirectly conveying to Benedict that he was suspected of being a felon’s accomplice without explicitly stating it.

The problem then became that we didn’t know how much Benedict understood about the situation.

Given the Marquis’s earlier statement left interpretation to the listener, it could also be taken as implicitly questioning whether Benedict might be betraying Crown Prince Zadias. This gave no definitive statement from the Marquis while probing what information the recipient might possess.

“I see. I understand what the Marquis means to say. Indeed, I am acquainted with her. I received orders from His Highness Zadias to oversee her accompaniment with the Marquis. It’s only natural to be suspicious.”

“If you understand, then I must ask you to stay in my territory for some time. Actually, there are numerous witnesses who saw her emitting miasma. There’s even suspicion she might be a demon. Given the importance of the matter, it’s merely a precaution.”

Though he said “ask,” these were the words of Marquis Zilbolt, the territorial lord. This was effectively a command.

If Benedict were to refuse this peacefully, he would need to argue in a way that proved his own innocence.

In other words, whether he was betraying the Crown Prince. Whether he himself was a demon.

Since there was a possibility he conspired with the witch to betray the Crown Prince or attempt assassinations of the Marquis’s family members, we could say we couldn’t permit Benedict to go to the royal capital or accompany the Marquis.

And—if Benedict refused these and resorted to force like drawing his sword against Marquis Zilbolt, or tried to break through and escape, we could counter that we would detain him to maintain public order as the territorial lord. After all, Benedict was the one under suspicion.

If he complied quietly, we would first have him prove he wasn’t a demon. Probably—by circulating his ki, we could determine whether he was a demon or not.

Either way, since he would be detained in the Marquis’s territory, Zadias and Benedict would be separated. This would eliminate one of Zadias’s key combatants in advance and also block information flow.

“A demon… That is… certainly important but—gh…”

Benedict groaned softly, bringing his hand to his forehead through his mask. His body swayed as if he’d experienced a dizzy spell. He staggered unsteadily.

…What was that just now? Through the gap in his mask, I thought I saw something like mist for just a moment—

“Are you all right?”

“—My apologies. I occasionally get headaches like this.”

When Marquis Zilbolt asked, Benedict shook his head in response.

“It’s temporary, so no need for concern. Let’s return to our discussion. I cannot comply with that request.”

“…Why is that? Do you have a reason?”

“With all due respect. Has the Marquis’s own innocence been proven?”

“Oh.”

At Benedict’s words, the Marquis’s eyes widened slightly. Benedict had essentially accused the Marquis to his face of possibly being the Crown Prince’s enemy.

“But if we’re saying that, the same applies to you, Sir Benedict.”

“His Highness Zadias found me when I was severely injured and had lost my memory, and he elevated me. I must repay that great debt. If there’s any possibility of danger approaching His Highness, I must rush to the royal capital to protect him. My loyalty and innocence need no proof to anyone—I alone need know them as truth.”

“I respect your conviction as a knight… but do you know how much His Highness Zadias is aware of? Is not remonstrance also the duty of a loyal retainer?”

Without giving any definitive statement, the Marquis was suggesting that Zadias might have known Alvelinde was a demon.

“That matter… has nothing to do with me. Even if it were true, it would be the same.”

Again. Benedict wavered, but this time he recovered as if something had switched in an instant, responding with flawless speech.

“Unfortunately. Until your innocence becomes clear in my eyes, I cannot grant you freedom of movement. These are the words of your territorial lord. And of a noble serving His Majesty the King of Silvatoria.”

“…Then the answer is decided. If you block my path, I will force my way through.”

Benedict drew his rapier.

Based on the gathered information and our interaction so far… Benedict had seemed rational.

But this was clearly a bad move, somewhat rash. And Benedict’s condition earlier. Unstable, unnatural… something felt off.

He said he was found after losing his memory. He did say that.

Anyway, from here on it’s my job. I stepped forward to confront him in place of the Marquis. Grace also stepped forward.

“Come, Ouroboros.”

The Dragon Staff flew from the soldiers’ guardhouse in the harbor and landed in my hand. I spun Ouroboros like a windmill before planting it on the ground, facing Benedict directly.

“I was wondering why women and children were present here. You are the Marquis’s escorts?”

“That’s right. Your opponent is me.”

“…You heard our conversation earlier. Even if you’re a child, if you’re a magician, I’ll have no choice but to fight with full force. If you don’t interfere and let me pass, no one will get hurt.”

But he still gave a warning. It didn’t seem demon-like, but we couldn’t rule out the possibility of acting. Well, we’ll just have to fight to find out.

“Regardless of the truth of your innocence or loyalty—if the fundamental premise is wrong, then they have no meaning.”

“Oh… Do you mock His Highness?”

Benedict reacted to my words.

Premise. Meaning, I was suggesting that the favor the Crown Prince supposedly showed Benedict might have been fake.

While I said it partly as a provocation to get Benedict’s attention, that wasn’t the only reason.

The Crown Prince found a person who had lost his memory, treated him, and elevated him to magic knight.

But that was only Benedict’s subjective view. While we could somewhat trust Benedict’s words and actions, we couldn’t trust anything about Zadias’s supposed kindness based on what we’d seen so far.

I’ve witnessed several dark magics like brainwashing or perception manipulation. Benedict’s earlier instability and his current unwavering stance. Seeing both sides and that earlier scene… for example—I began to suspect that mask might be such an item. Or there might be a secret beneath the mask.

“That’s right. I have no evidence. But since there’s a possibility you’re connected to demons, I can’t let you go elsewhere. If that’s your intention, then I’ll just have to force my claim through by strength.”

When I smiled back in response, a smile also formed at the corner of Benedict’s mouth.

“A remarkably clear and understandable story. Probably—you are the Marquis’s strongest combatant, aren’t you? Then—I shall cut my way out of this town with my own hands.”

Swinging his rapier wrapped in magical brilliance two or three times, Benedict took his stance.

Caduceus had joined the escort team too—but it seemed there was movement at the castle as well. Apparently, things were starting to happen everywhere.

+++

# **254 – The Origin of Benedict**

By the time Caduceus flew into the castle, things had already become quite hectic.

He began assessing the situation within the castle. There was a possibility that demons might be present here as well, but if that were the case, he would need to consider Claudia’s evacuation via Teleportation Magic while also having Grace and Sheila’s group provide backup.

Caduceus moved smoothly along the castle’s ceiling—through the shadows. Below him was a mixed group of young knights and magicians. Six in total. That was two squads’ worth of people.

Since their preferences had been considered during squad assignments… it was only natural they’d be exposed like this.

“Captain Volis, aren’t there guards in the VIP room as well?”

“I heard foreign nobles brought their own security. Perhaps out of deference to them, the number of soldiers is low. And that security consists mostly of women and children. Nothing to fear!”

“If we capture Lady Belinda or Lady Romina, we win, right?”

“Exactly. At worst, we should at least be able to escape the town along with Sir Benedict who’s currently here!”

“The Vice-Commander is right. Hurry! Our movements will be discovered soon!”

Well, that was the general tone. Belinda referred to the Marchioness… but these were hardly the words of loyal retainers.

Where they were moving within the castle, what their objective was—everything was being transmitted clearly through the communication devices.

Their target was the VIP room. Today was the day the sailing ship returned, so many personnel were occupied with security throughout the town. The castle’s guard was somewhat thin, creating a perfect opportunity for the traitors… but that too was part of the exposure strategy, playing right into their hands.

They’d deliberately made the security around the VIP room light today as well. Though admittedly, the guest in question possessed considerable combat power, so their assumptions were wrong from the very beginning.

“There she is! Romina!”

Romina’s figure appeared at the end of the hallway. Upon seeing the men—and their fierce determination—she showed a panicked expression and fled like a startled rabbit.

“Capture her! Flank her! The target is alone!”

Romina fled toward where the guard presence was thinner. She descended the stairs as if avoiding those trying to flank her, heading toward the underground training ground inside the building. Given the current emergency situation, the training ground was empty. The men exchanged glances and laughed. She was like a rat in a trap.

They noisily descended the stairs and cornered Romina deep within the training ground.

“Please remain calm. You might get hurt if you resist,” a soldier told Romina, but she gave a faint smile and held something high. A flash grenade. The men who didn’t know what it was followed it with their eyes.

The moment it was smashed against the floor, Caduceus hid behind a pillar and weathered the flash. A blinding white light filled the training ground, painting everything pure white.

“Gwaaah!?”

“Y-you bastard!”

The men who had taken the full brunt of the flash drew their weapons while covering their faces.

“Stop! Don’t draw your swords! You’ll end up fighting each other!”

Then—Ignis charged in from behind. It sent a robed man flying with a powerful fist, crushing his leg to eliminate any means of escape.

Ignis’s target—was first and foremost the troublesome magicians.

Even though they could use magic, they too valued their lives. So by taking their legs and sealing their escape routes, it created a situation where even if they tried to counterattack with magic, they ultimately couldn’t escape. The aim was to rob them of the very will to fight.

Meanwhile, Ambrum—who had been disguised as Romina—revealed his true form as a Doppelganger and fled to a corner of the training ground.

Ambrum’s original role was to be Princess Stephania’s Shadow Clone. But once they learned the enemy’s objective was the Marchioness and Romina, Rosemary chose encirclement through diversion rather than defensive repulsion.

The group still hadn’t recovered from their confusion. During that time, Ignis brought down its combined fists on a second man, crushing him.

“Uwaaah!”

As one screamed uncontrollably and tried to run away, projectiles—Saucers, chunks of ice, and Sound Bullets from a horn—flew down from the top of the stairs, blowing him away.

Ignis scattered them indiscriminately. Its heavy armor made counterattacks meaningless. Even if they managed to get through the narrow passage—Dullahan was waiting at the top of the stairs. At this rate, the traitors would be subdued quickly.

Now then—time to focus on the matter at hand.

I was facing Benedict while raising my magical power. He showed no sign of being disturbed by the magical radiation enveloping Ouroboros.

After gradually closing the distance, I stepped in all at once. With enough force to snap his rapier, I slammed my entire body into him.

But what deflected it was a large shield. An ice shield formed on his left arm. While forcefully parrying with the shield, his magic-wrapped rapier flashed.

He unleashed a series of shallow thrusts aimed at my face. Feinting a straight thrust, he subtly altered the trajectory of the tip through wrist movements.

I avoided them with just neck movements and Steps, then bent my upper body and scooped upward with Ouroboros.

He jumped. Benedict leaped backward. While jumping, he swung both arms to the sides, and intersecting ice shotgun blasts formed a barrage closing in.

I didn’t create distance. I didn’t dodge. Because if he escaped, it would all be for nothing. I deployed a Shield in front and charged straight through. My target—was his landing point.

A Magic Circle glowed on Benedict’s left hand. An ice wall grew to block my path. I feinted left, then kicked off the Shield mid-air to fly right. Drawing a trajectory that seemed to bounce left and right, I closed in on Benedict.

“Such dexterous tricks!”

Instantly, Benedict’s right arm—from the elbow down—was encased in ice. The rapier transformed into a massive Greatsword, and he swung it down from the upper left to knock aside my attack. Simultaneously—ice vines crawled across the ground from Benedict’s right foot. A diagonal attack, but I could see it.

I fired a Fireball from my toe as if executing a roundhouse kick, blowing away the vines, and using the momentum of the kick, I stepped in and shifted form. I avoided the ice Greatsword and closed in.

Close combat again. I shattered the Greatsword from the middle, revealing Benedict’s original right arm and rapier, which immediately came to meet me.

Gripping the Dragon Staff at its midpoint, I unleashed chain attacks from both sides, exchanging blows with Benedict. The clang of steel rang out as we engaged in ground combat, trading thrusts and strikes as if dancing a waltz.

A blow from the Dragon Staff slipped past the rapier and struck his flank. Against a human, it would break ribs; against a demon, it would at least stagger them.

But what returned was a hard sensation. Benedict was clad in ice armor.

No matter. I slammed a magical shockwave along with a palm strike.

Gritting his teeth, Benedict took a step back. Bending his body, he used both his body’s spring and magic to charge in at maximum speed. I flew past the bracing Benedict as if slipping through his side.

As we passed each other—Nemea leaped out, swinging her claws.

“What!?”

A snapping sound like a string breaking. A hat and mask dancing through the air.

My target from the very beginning was his mask. That string connecting the mask to Benedict’s head was in the way.

“You bastard!”

Benedict’s face twisted in rage as he leaped back. His face—from his left cheek to his temple—definitely bore a single burn scar. Whether exposing it was humiliating or not, Benedict covered the scar with his left hand and glared at me.

But the problem wasn’t the burn. My attention was focused elsewhere.

The gem embedded in the center of his forehead. And… that face.

Silver hair and purple eyes. They held some resemblance to someone close to me—.

From the deck above, Lavigne’s long, long howl echoed. Her voice seemed to be desperately trying to tell me something.

…Ah. I understand. I get it now, Ashley. So that’s it? That’s how it is?

I created distance again, facing each other. After a few beats of silence, I spoke.

“…You’re Elliot Silune, aren’t you?”

“What… are you talking about?”

Benedict showed a confused expression as if he didn’t understand what I was saying. Was the amnesia real? Or was that gem sealing his memories?

Elliot Silune. Ashley’s older brother, who was said to have died in a ship accident six years ago.

The ship sank, but his body was never recovered.

His study abroad destination shouldn’t have been Silvatoria—but perhaps the ship docked somewhere in Silvatoria along the route. Or maybe he survived and washed ashore somewhere in Silvatoria. I don’t know what circumstances led to it, but Elliot is here.

The reason for wearing the mask too. While ostensibly to hide the burn scar, the real purpose was probably to hide that gem.

“It’s your real name.”

“Nonsense…!”

“It’s the truth. I know your sister too, and she’s in this town right now.”

Benedict… no, Elliot’s eyes widened.

I relayed instructions through Caduceus. The traitors in the castle had been subdued. There was no problem with Ashley coming here.

“What is that gem? Was it prepared by Zadias? What is it for?”

“Silence! I have no need to tell you anything!”

As I spoke, the gem on his forehead flickered, and haze wrapped around him. Yes. Every time I shook him.

Whenever Elliot considered doubts about Zadias or past memories—that gem interfered. Which meant—the gem’s control wasn’t complete.

“Brother Elliot!”

Riding on Lindwurm’s back. Ashley came rushing from the castle. Right to my side. Jumping down from above.

When Elliot saw Ashley landing on the ground, his eyes widened in astonishment.

If a girl resembling him appeared, he couldn’t just dismiss it as nonsense. Elliot shook his head.

“I… I don’t know you. I don’t have a sister. My sister was much smaller. So, no. That can’t be right…”

Elliot’s words became incoherent. The gem flickered more intensely. As Ashley watched, he muttered something under his breath, but eventually Elliot began to laugh.

“…Yes, yes. If you say you’re my sister. Then you should serve His Highness Zadias alongside me! Ah, that’s good! That’s perfect! Come, Ashley. Come with me!”

At Elliot’s laughing words as he extended his hand, Ashley showed a sad expression and shook her head, then spoke clearly.

“…I won’t go. My place is by Theodore-sama’s side. Brother Elliot, who left long ago and never returned, please come back. Me, the butler… everyone in Silune has been waiting for your return all this time.”

As she spoke, Ashley no longer wore an expression of sadness. She looked straight at Elliot as if having resolved something.

“Oh… ah…”

As if overwhelmed by the strength of will in her eyes, Elliot retreated one step, then two.

I took a deep breath and raised Ouroboros.

“…Another reason not to let you escape has been added. No matter what happens, you will remain here—no, you will definitely return alive to Ashley’s side.”

“Theodore-sama…”

I met Ashley’s eyes and nodded. Ashley also nodded while looking at me.

“Ha—haha! Ah? So, that’s how it is!”

Seeing this, Elliot laughed. He laughed with wide eyes.

“You! It’s because of you that Ashley won’t come with me!”

Magical power surged from Elliot’s entire body as he closed in. I—stepped forward to meet him.

He slammed his Fighting Spirit-wrapped rapier with brute force. After blocking two, three times with Ouroboros, he leaped back while raising his rapier overhead and deploying a massive Magic Circle. Not even disguised. The Spell Formula was exposed.

7th-class Water Magic Frozen Beak. A giant ice bird began to take shape. At 7th-class, the destructive aftermath would be significant. To avoid involving the surroundings, I also deployed a Magic Circle and flew upward.

“I won’t let you escape!”

Elliot swung his rapier. In sync with that motion, the ice bird was released. Flapping its wings, it charged toward me with ferocious speed.

“Naive.”

Just before impact, my magic completed. Compact Leap. Using short-range Teleportation Magic, I circled behind Elliot, wrapped my arm around his neck in one motion, and tightened my grip.

It’s been since Talcott. Choking him out, taking him down unharmed.

“Wha—!?”

Elliot, whose distance had been nullified, cried out in astonishment. He tried to stab his rapier into my arm, but it was futile. Nemea and Capella clung to him, sealing his arm movements.

“Guh…!”

Completely locked in. As Elliot cried out, the Frozen Beak that should have passed by drew an arc and headed toward us. Probably intending to smash me along with it, but that won’t happen. I made a promise to Ashley.

“Grace!”

The next instant, a purple flash ran from ground to sky. Piercing through the Frozen Beak’s torso and leaving an afterimage, it shattered the ice statue to pieces.

“Interference is unnecessary.”

It was Grace, enveloped in Fighting Spirit. Seeing this, Elliot struggled even more. Struggling, he released ice spears from his entire body. But I wouldn’t let them through. The Dragon Scale Armor with activated Protection couldn’t be pierced.

Ice fragments grazed exposed parts like his face and hands—but such things weren’t even worth considering.

“Ash… le…”

With those words, all strength left Elliot’s body.

Simultaneously with his loss of consciousness, I applied a Magic Seal and moved away from Elliot. Then restrained him with Light Bind.

“Haa…”

“Theodore-sama! Brother Elliot!”

It was over. I let out a deep breath, and Ashley came running over. At any rate, Elliot was unharmed.

“It’s fine. Elliot isn’t hurt.”

When I answered, Ashley looked like she might cry, but after confirming the situation, she showed a relieved expression. Then she shook her head slightly.

“But Theodore-sama… you’re injured.”

She healed the minor wounds on my cheeks and elsewhere with Healing Magic.

Her complexion was somewhat pale. Right. At the end, I was close while blocking the ice spears… from Ashley’s perspective, she wouldn’t want either of us getting hurt.

Well, mine were just grazes. I should thank Alfred. And the Water Dragon and Arachne too.

Now then. This gem. Whether it’s alright to destroy it as is.

There are two people knowledgeable about such hidden techniques and ancient secret arts. The proper response would be to consult them first.

+++

# **255 – The True Nature of Gems**

Elliot remained asleep. We decided to transport him to the castle immediately and have everyone examine him.

Just then, as if perfectly timed, Lindwurm returned to the port leading our companion wyverns from the castle.

“Thank you, Lindwurm.”

Normally, Lindwurm refuses to let anyone but me ride on his back… but perhaps because this was an emergency, he allowed Ashley to ride. When I praised him and stroked the area around his nose, Lindwurm narrowed his eyes and purred.

“We’re returning to the castle. Can I count on you?”

Lindwurm nodded. I cast Levitation to carry Elliot and mounted Lindwurm. Everyone else rode their wyverns back to the castle. Upon arriving at the castle, everyone immediately gathered.

We laid Elliot down, and Claudia and Rosemary examined his forehead.

“…This is…”

“It’s not so much attached as it is embedded.”

Claudia’s eyes widened, while Rosemary frowned.

“Do you know what this gem is?”

“I… don’t know.”

When I asked, Rosemary shook her head. Judging by her reaction, Claudia seemed to know something.

“…It’s a Caex Gem. It looks like a gem, but it’s actually a type of magical creature.”

Claudia explained.

“It disrupts magical power and replaces the third eye. It blocks the mind’s eye, distorting perception and memory. That’s why it’s also called the Blind Gem.”

The third eye… I see. So that’s why it attaches to the forehead?

It certainly looks like a gem… but depending on how you look at it, it could also resemble a vertical eye.

Come to think of it, Elliot had acted as if having it on his forehead was normal. While the Caex Gem should have been the thing to hide, when his mask was removed, he was concerned about the burn scars on his face.

For Elliot, this gem probably didn’t feel particularly unnatural.

“What’s the countermeasure?”

“Since it’s blocking the proper flow of magical power—I’ve heard it can be broken through depending on the strength of the person’s own magical flow.”

“I see…”

Essentially, by increasing the momentum of the correct flow, we can push the obstruction out of the way. But… there’s something I need to confirm first.

Ashley was using magical reflection to examine Elliot’s forehead.

“…How does it look? Is the gem embedded deeper than the bone?”

I asked Ashley. If the Caex Gem appeared to reach the brain… then rash intervention would become difficult.

In that case, we’d have to abandon removing the Caex Gem itself and look for another approach.

For example, applying a Sealing Technique with the same properties as Grace’s Ring to the Gem itself, as a magical creature, to neutralize it and resolve the situation… That would probably be the direction we’d take. Even then, it should be possible to restore Elliot to his senses.

“It’s fine… I think. It might be touching the bone… but it seems to stop there.”

Ashley’s assessment seemed positive. First hurdle cleared, I suppose. Just to be sure, I also checked with Circulating Ki, and if there were no issues, we’d proceed with removing Elliot’s gem.

“Alright then, let’s begin.”

“Yes.”

I knelt beside Elliot, raised his upper body, and touched his back. Closing my eyes, I sent weak magical waves like ripples and concentrated on their reflection.

I carefully examined the forehead area, verifying whether Ashley’s assessment was correct. …Hmm. Indeed. This should work.

Next, Circulating Ki. I heightened and refined my magical power. Claudia said it could be broken through depending on magical strength… but given how Elliot, with his level of skill, was in that state, breaking through this would require considerable magical power.

So, I refined it more than usual. Circulating, circulating. I refined and heightened the flow of magical power, correcting the flow disrupted by the Caex Gem back to its proper form. Like pushing aside trees blocking a river’s flow. As excess magical power began radiating from both Elliot’s body and mine, the Caex Gem embedded in his forehead started trembling violently.

“Begone!”

I intensified my magical power—and with almost disappointingly ease, the gem was pushed out, making a dry sound as it rolled onto the floor.

The surprise came afterward. What appeared to be an ordinary gem grew what looked like claws or legs from its edges and tried to escape.

“…How persistent.”

Rosemary said this and stomped on the Gem with her toe as it tried to cross in front of her. The Gem let out a high-pitched shriek.

Rosemary seemed displeased with both the reaction and the squirming sensation under her boot, frowning with distaste.

“This… what should we do with it?”

“…It’s evidence. We’ll package it with Earth Magic and use a racial characteristic seal.”

“I see…”

Since Rosemary seemed disgusted, I decided to quickly package it and apply the Sealing Technique. While I was working on that, Ashley used Healing Magic to close the wound on Elliot’s forehead.

The forehead wound—well. Perhaps because the Healing Magic was applied quickly, it seemed it would close cleanly. I also checked once more with Circulating Ki to ensure there were no abnormalities. Elliot still hadn’t woken up… but his magical flow was now completely normal.

From the impression of his magical power, it’s like that of an ordinary sleeping person.

“First… let’s have Lord Elliot rest on a bed. We’ll need to take some time for discussion.”

Marquis Zilbolt said.

We laid Elliot on a bed. Ashley used Water Magic to fill a bucket with cold water, soaked a hand towel, and placed it on his forehead.

“Ashley, are you okay?”

Seraphina flew close to Ashley who was nursing him, and Marlene drew near. Ashley smiled and told them both she was fine.

While monitoring Elliot’s condition, we lowered our voices and began our discussion.

“How is the situation within the castle?”

“The collaborators have been captured and imprisoned. Any remaining ones should be identified soon.”

Right. The part about the collaborators possibly panicking and making moves went as expected. Accounting for the confusion and time needed for instructions, our departure for the royal capital is scheduled for the day after the ship arrives.

“Preparations for departure to the royal capital are proceeding as scheduled.”

Well, it seems the issues in the Marquis’s domain have been mostly resolved.

“The problem is Sir Elliot’s condition.”

Princess Stephania slightly furrowed her brow.

“From what I can see of his magical power, it seems like he’s just sleeping normally.”

“How long will it take for him to recover?”

“That’s the question.”

I nodded at Grace’s words. Will his memory and perception return immediately? Or will there be confusion? Depending on that, we’ll need to decide what to do with Elliot.

If he wakes up and his perception doesn’t improve immediately… for example, we could use Teleportation Magic to send him to Termwills and have him recuperate there for a while.

“We should probably observe until tomorrow morning. We just need to determine things before departure.”

Claudia said with her eyes closed.

We should contact Termwills via the Communication Device about the outcome of this incident.

“Why did Zadias target him, I wonder?”

Irmhild tilted her head.

“That is indeed questionable. Using magic on a noble’s child from another country—even if I found a Gem, I wouldn’t choose someone so risky.”

“If Zadias didn’t know his background… that might be possible.”

Rosemary tilted her head while toying with her feather fan, and Sheila responded.

I see. Did he pick him up after he lost his memory?

“That might be it. Taking advantage of his amnesia, he performed procedures to prevent memory recovery under the pretext of protecting him. That way, he’d have nowhere to return to and could keep him close. Or, even if he knew there were problems, he might have wanted to recruit him after seeing his magical talent.”

“A guard with specialized magical aptitude for Water Magic… is indeed a desirable asset.”

Being able to use healing and detoxification magic, and skilled with a sword. And as long as the Gem was functional, he wouldn’t betray. Thinking that way, it might be worth the effort… I suppose.

“Is the forehead always where the Gem is embedded?”

Grace tilted her head.

“That’s right. The position can’t be changed. Originally… it wasn’t meant for use on humans.”

According to Claudia… it seems it’s used for creatures like dragons, difficult-to-control beings, to forcibly subjugate them.

However, to subdue an opponent like a dragon with a Gem, you’d need to create a considerably large and high-performance Caex Gem.

Hmm. That mask was to hide the Gem. The burn scars were the justification. So, he probably couldn’t use the method of embedding Gems in multiple people…

“…I think I can answer some of the questions.”

While I was pondering various things, such a voice echoed through the room.

“Brother Elliot!”

Ashley’s face brightened. Elliot was lying down, staring at the ceiling as he opened his eyes.

…I had considered the possibility he might become violent, but he seemed calm. I released the Light Bind restraint, and he quietly took the hand towel placed on his forehead and sat up.

“You shouldn’t move yet…”

“It’s alright, Ashley. I don’t feel that bad. It’s like the fog in my head has cleared. Various things I’ve wondered about until now… they’ve fallen into place, so to speak.”

Elliot gave a wry smile, then turned to me and bowed deeply.

“You are Theodore-dono, correct? First, let me express my gratitude. It seems you have saved not only my life, but my mind as well.”

“Not at all. I’m just relieved you’re safe. But first, please listen to what Ashley has to say.”

When I answered Elliot like that, he widened his eyes slightly, then nodded gently.

“Ashley… I’m sorry. I’ve caused you trouble all this time.”

“…No. Welcome back.”

Ashley smiled softly and began telling her brother about what happened after he disappeared. Elliot occasionally asked questions or made responses to Ashley’s story, appearing quite composed.

With the Gem gone, the factor inhibiting memory recovery had been removed, it seemed.

“—And so, I became engaged to Theodore-sama.”

“Eh? R-really?”

Ashley’s topic turned to me. At her words, Elliot’s eyes widened. Ashley smiled gently at such an Elliot.

Elliot seemed surprised for a moment, but eventually broke into a wry smile and said.

“—Well. Congratulations, Ashley.”

“Yes!”

At her brother’s words, Ashley bloomed into a flower-like smile and nodded, then smiled at me as well.

+++

# **256 – Memories of the Voyage**

“…I suppose I should also talk about what happened to me.”

Elliot spoke after Ashley had finished her story.

Though his words seemed directed at Ashley… the fact that he glanced toward us as well implied this would involve Zadias.

“Before that, perhaps we should first introduce ourselves properly.”

“Ah, yes.”

Elliot rose from the bed, bowed slightly, then took a deep breath before stating his name.

“Elliot… Rodias=Siln. It’s a pleasure to meet you all properly.”

What emotions were contained in that introduction? After stating his name, Elliot closed his eyes briefly.

“Theodore Gartner. The pleasure is mine.”

“Ah. So you’re connected to Count Gartner.”

“That’s my family home. Though I’ve left it now.”

As Elliot introduced himself, our group reciprocated with our own introductions.

Elliot’s eyes widened when he learned three members of Verdgar’s royal family were present, and when my engagement was mentioned afterward, he let out a somewhat dry laugh.

“W-well… with that level of ability, I suppose such things happen.”

Hmm. It seems he retains memories from when the Caex Gem was attached to him. In that case, we might be able to gather various information about the Crown Prince as well.

Elliot cleared his throat once and shook his head as if to refocus.

“Let’s return to the story. Right. It began six years ago, I suppose.”

“You remember it?”

“…At the time… I probably had truly forgotten.”

Touching the burn scar on his face, Elliot spoke.

Just as I thought. His memory loss had been recovering, but the Gem was suppressing it.

“Six years ago—after receiving a letter from Kennel-san, I boarded a ship to return to the Barony of Silun. But… on the return journey, we were attacked at sea.”

“By whom?”

If the ship incident wasn’t an accident or natural disaster but an attack—the likely candidates would be Zadias’s subordinates. Or perhaps an accidental encounter with demons, monsters, or pirates. But it seems unlikely that Zadias would stage an attack specifically to acquire Elliot… or does it?

“Zadias… and his subordinates. Though I can only say this now that my memories have returned.”

But Elliot stated it wasn’t just Zadias’s men—it was Zadias himself.

“Why did they target you, Lord Elliot?”

“They weren’t targeting me specifically—they had another objective. That is… they were after another passenger. A magician was fighting the attackers. The attackers’ goal from the beginning was that single magician, and they apparently intended to kill all other crew members and passengers who might serve as witnesses.”

“That… could it be Lady Lisa’s…”

Grace frowned.

“Yes, perhaps.”

A magician pursued by Zadias. Judging from what we know, perhaps someone like Mother’s colleague who fled from the Sages’ Academy. Either Zadias discovered their location or cornered them. In any case, they tried to escape by ship. But they couldn’t escape completely… and unfortunately encountered their pursuers on the same ship Elliot was aboard.

“I resisted as well. I defeated several of them, but was blown back by magic, hit my head, and lost consciousness.”

And then. When he next regained awareness, he had lost his memories and was receiving treatment somewhere. That’s when the one leading the attackers—Zadias himself—appeared. So Elliot recounted.

Zadias was impressed by Elliot’s skill in defeating his subordinates and his magical aptitude specialized in Water Magic, so he tried to incorporate him into his own forces without even caring about his origins.

Should we call that a silver lining? Perhaps Elliot’s resistance paid off in a way.

Moreover, with Elliot having suffered memory loss from the head injury, with the Caex Gem, the very perpetrator of the attack could even pose as his benefactor.

“At that time I was injured, unable to move, and in a daze… but I do remember some of the conversation Zadias had with others. He said something about the Gems being an experiment. That eventually he would make the citizens wear them, and that he was observing the effects of long-term wearing for that purpose, things like that.”

“Such… such a thing, Brother Elliot…”

“What foolish talk…”

Ashley frowned, and Princess Stephania shook her head.

…Forcing citizens to wear those Magical Creatures? What kind of dystopia is he dreaming of? If Zadias becomes king like this, it will be terrible.

But well, I understand the general sequence of events now.

“And so I was given the new name Benedict. While my wounds were being treated, I continued with training and magic studies.”

Treatment and training. After that concluded, he was judged sufficiently capable and recommended for the Magic Knight Order. That was roughly two years after the ship attack.

By the time the commotion over the maritime accident had died down. Zadias could claim he found a skilled Magic Swordsman who had lost his memory and recommended him, making it both an achievement for the scoundrel and something he could use as a heartwarming story.

“You mentioned Zadias had his subordinates carry out the attack, but…”

“…It wasn’t us. Given our position, it was difficult for us to investigate Zadias’s information…”

Marquis Zilbolt shook his head. Well… that makes sense. After all, he had taken hostages against Marquis Zilbolt, released collaborators, and even used him as a scapegoat.

“They are independent magic knights directly under Zadias. An elite force selected by Zadias himself, called the Black Knights. I also served as a liaison between the regular Magic Knight Order and the Black Knights, so…”

“Black Knights… Are they being controlled by the Gems as well?”

“To my knowledge… there shouldn’t have been anyone else like me.”

The Black Knights directly under Zadias. If they’re not being controlled, then they must be Zadias’s trusted blades, his true pawns, his trump cards.

“That sounds troublesome. If they’re entrusted with work that can’t be made public, and are following him of their own will.”

Rosemary frowned, and Claudia nodded.

“If Zadias falls, those fellows will be ruined too.”

Right. If they’ve undertaken the dirty work as executioners, they’re tied to the Crown Prince’s fate. We should assume that when cornering Zadias, these particular individuals won’t surrender and will likely fight.

“…I understand the situation.”

“If I may be so bold… there’s something I’d like to request.”

“What is it?”

“Could you take me to the royal capital as well? As you can see, I’m not injured anymore. I want to be of use.”

Elliot spoke with a serious expression.

“That… you would be an important witness, so we’d be grateful for that… But even if you choose to return to the Barony of Silun, no one will blame you. You must want to see Kennel-san and everyone from your hometown too.”

“To turn a blind eye like this… I have acquaintances in the royal capital too, so if something happens, I’ll regret it. Besides, my sister will be accompanying Theodore-dono, won’t she?”

…I see. So being freed from the Gem overturned his assessment of the Crown Prince, but his feelings toward the people of Silvatoria were separate.

Even while receiving some guidance from the Caex Gem, as long as it didn’t concern past memories or suspicions about the Crown Prince, he likely retained some degree of free will.

The mechanism probably worked such that the Caex Gem only interfered when specific matters were touched upon. It makes sense why Benedict himself didn’t have a bad reputation.

If that’s the case, then not everything about the days he lived as Benedict was false. Precisely because he’s been freed from the Gem’s constraints, there are probably things he wants to confirm for himself.

When I glanced at Ashley, she seemed to hesitate slightly but nodded back with a determined expression.

“Understood. Then we would appreciate Lord Elliot’s assistance as well. However, you’re still recovering, so please don’t push yourself too hard or do anything reckless.”

“Thank you. I have a Hippogriff waiting near the town. I thought it wouldn’t cause any trouble for transportation.”

Elliot bowed deeply as he said this.

Hippogriff. That’s the hybrid of a Griffin and a horse, isn’t it? I hear they’re calm-tempered and easy to tame for riding. Probably something he prepared outside town as an escape method without being able to bring it into town. So he had a plan to escape back to the royal capital if he could break through the encirclement.

But well, it seems we’ll be able to depart for the royal capital as scheduled.

Since Elliot will be accompanying us, we’ll first need to retrieve his luggage and such from the inn.

+++

# **257 – Towards the Royal Capital**

We began preparing for departure before the sun had even risen. I fed the Lindwurms Orc meat to fill their stomachs.

Elliot was also preparing for the journey. He seemed to be checking the condition of the Hippogriff’s saddle and reins. Elliot had traveled alone to Marquis Zilbolt’s territory. Since he moved by Hippogriff, his luggage was quite minimal.

After retrieving his belongings from the inn and loading them onto the Dragon Palanquin, he called the Hippogriff to the castle. All that remained was to check the equipment, and his travel preparations would be complete.

When I glanced at Elliot, I noticed he was wearing the mask that covered his eyes again.

“Brother Elliot, you’re wearing the mask to go, then.”

Although the string of Elliot’s mask had been cut… it seemed he had several spare masks. When he went to retrieve his luggage, he apparently also recovered his feathered tricorne hat.

“Yes. I’ve always been like this in Silvatoria. I feel bad about it toward Ashley, though.”

“…I see. If you were to remove the mask at this point, people might mistake you for someone else instead.”

“That’s right. The mask is just an ordinary item I ordered and had made in the royal capital, so there’s no need to worry.”

According to Elliot, it seemed that Zadias was indeed the one who instructed him to wear the mask.

“Perhaps it’s better if I don’t go out too much either.”

Hmm… If someone who knows what to look for sees Ashley’s appearance, they might realize we’re siblings. The fact that Marquis Zilbolt didn’t recognize us probably means most people don’t know.

“In that case, I have a good method.”

Rosemary spoke up.

“What is it?”

“I can make hair dye for disguise. It won’t damage your hair, and you can wash it off immediately if needed. It’s quite an excellent product, I must say.”

Oh ho. Then I might ask for it too. If we’re talking about origins being revealed through hair color… someone might connect my appearance to Mother.

“Then, shall we go shopping after we arrive?”

“Thank you very much, Lady Marie.”

“Yes. I’ve tested it on myself, so you can rest assured.”

I see. So she’s been doing various things, not just the Disguise Ring.

Anyway, if we’re going to hide Ashley’s origins, this should suffice.

“Ah, that’s right. Elliot-san. Please take this.”

Since Elliot’s hands seemed free, I handed him the Amulet of Evil Repulsion I had brought as a spare, along with a ring-shaped Magic Tool.

“A Magic Tool…?”

“The necklace protects against effects from Curse Magic and Magic Potions. The ring is a Magic Tool embedded with a Magic Shield. I thought it would be just right as support.”

“Ah. When I fought Theodore-dono…”

“Yes. This is meant to be attached to your leg, allowing you to use the Shield as a foothold. Since you don’t need to control the Spell Formula yourself, you can move quickly in the air with the help of Levitation.”

In Elliot’s case, there were aspects where he fought while controlling multiple Techniques. Since he also has knowledge of Martial Arts, I judged that it would be practical enough if he combined it with Levitation.

“…I see. I’ll practice a bit during my free time. Did Theodore-dono also use this?”

“Theodore does everything on his own.”

Sheila, who had been checking the luggage, answered, and Elliot’s mouth twitched slightly.

“He does all of that… by himself?”

“Well, yes.”

“Theodore-sama thought of it and spread it.”

“I see… The world is vast… I must work hard not to become complacent.”

At Ashley’s words, Elliot nodded, clenching and unclenching his fist. …If it’s serving as motivation, that might be just right.

Just as we finished the final check for any forgotten items before the journey, the Lindwurms seemed to have finished their meal and let out a cry to inform me.

“Well then, my lord. I pray for your martial fortune.”

“Father. Please be careful.”

“Mm. Don’t cause trouble for yourselves.”

After exchanging words with Marquis Zilbolt, the Marchioness, and Romina, they quietly embraced each other.

The Marchioness and Romina were to be sent to Termwills by Claudia using Teleportation Magic. The preparations for their reception at the stay facilities in the ritual grounds were complete, so all that remained was for Claudia to evacuate them there using Teleportation Magic.

“Sorry to keep you waiting.”

After taking a moment, the members of the Marquis’s family spoke to Claudia.

“Are you ready now?”

“Yes.”

“Then, I’ll send you.”

Claudia’s Teleportation Magic activated, and the Marchioness and Romina were sent to Termwills.

After a short while, a message came through the Communication Device from Mercedes, saying that they had safely taken custody of the two and would protect them with the pride of the Knight Order.

“It seems everything is fine on their end. Shall we depart soon?”

As the eastern sky began to lighten, I looked around at everyone and spoke, and they nodded.

“Hmm. We might be able to take it a bit easier on the way. I was beaten by Marlene on the ship, after all.”

When Tephra said this, Marlene smiled mischievously. They were talking about the card games on the ship.

“Elliot-san, won’t you ride in the Dragon Palanquin?”

“Ah. I need to pay a little attention to Saphir… I’ll join you in there during breaks.”

Elliot answered while stroking the head of Saphir, his Hippogriff. Apparently, if he didn’t, Saphir would get in a bad mood. Perhaps because she had been waiting outside the town for a while, there was a sense of her rubbing her nose against Elliot and acting spoiled.

Hmm… That’s true. If Elliot rode in the Dragon Palanquin in this state, she might indeed get upset.

So, Elliot mounted his Hippogriff, and the rest of us boarded the Dragon Palanquin. Elmer and the others also boarded a separate Dragon Palanquin, and thus we all set off for Silvatoria’s royal capital.

Traveling by Dragon Palanquin in Silvatoria’s mainland was basically no different from that in the Kingdom of Verdugal. We flew through the sky along the highway. What was different from before was probably that Elmer’s Dragon Palanquin had the Zilbolt family’s Emblem attached to it.

The Dragon Palanquin we rode in had an Emblem attached to it indicating we were envoys of the Kingdom of Verdugal. This allowed us to pass through regional cities without much hassle.

“This is—Marquis Zilbolt. And Sir Benedict as well.”

“Mm. Well met.”

Marquis Zilbolt leaned his face out the window of the Dragon Palanquin and informed the soldiers stationed at the watchtower on the city’s outer wall of our destination and purpose. When the watchtower soldier raised a blue flag, another watchtower also raised a blue flag.

The blue flag meant “The Dragon Palanquin will not enter the city interior and will pass through directly.” By performing these procedures and using flag signals, smooth passage was ensured. Well, it’s like air traffic control.

Since Dragon Palanquins pulled by multiple Wyverns aren’t very maneuverable, if they were targeted by ballistae, they would normally be shot down.

While Dragon Palanquins aren’t something that ordinary bandits can easily prepare, there’s still a chance of the unexpected. So, by going through these procedures, both the city side and those traveling by Dragon Palanquin could feel at ease.

“Please, proceed.”

We were seen off by the saluting soldiers and advanced along the outer wall.

“Shall we land the Dragon Palanquin for a break a little further on?”

“That sounds good. There’s a place with a nice view along the highway from here.”

When I spoke to Elliot through the window, that was the reply I received.

“Then, let’s rest there.”

“Understood.”

The place Elliot guided us to was a sunny embankment beside the highway. A small stream flowed nearby, and beyond it, flowers were blooming… it was quite a peaceful spot. Seraphina, who had gotten out of the Dragon Palanquin, flew around happily, and Lavigne trotted after her.

Caduceus in cat form on top of Ignis’s head. Then Ambrum in servant form. These guys were really marching to their own beat. They sat together on the embankment.

“It’s a beautiful place.”

“I’m glad you like it.”

Elliot and Marquis Zilbolt smiled.

“I borrowed the castle’s kitchen and prepared some light snacks.”

Grace brought out a basket from inside the Dragon Palanquin. It was a bit early for lunch, but having a snack while resting wasn’t a bad idea.

“I’ll prepare drinks now.”

Ashley used Water Magic to prepare tea for us.

The contents of the basket were what you’d call sandwiches. White bread with lettuce, tomato, cheese, ham, eggs, etc., sandwiched in between, making them quite colorful and enjoyable to look at. They were perfect for eating in a place like this.

“Marie and I helped too.”

Claudia said.

“Is that so?”

“Well… it’s not something that took much effort. Just cutting the ingredients and sandwiching them.”

“But Marie helped with smoking the ham, didn’t she?”

When Claudia smiled at her, Rosemary opened her feather fan and looked away. That’s right. It seemed the ingredients themselves were brought from Termwills. Smoking should be quite labor-intensive.

“Yeah. It’s delicious.”

When I said that after taking a bite, Claudia and Grace exchanged smiles. Rosemary remained hiding her face behind her feather fan.

We had prepared blood sausage for Irmhild, but that didn’t mean ordinary food was meaningless to her. She was also eating the sandwich with apparent enjoyment.

“—What kind of person is Zadias normally?”

The post-meal conversation inevitably turned to matters after arriving at the royal capital. For the sake of planning tendencies and countermeasures, it would be good to grasp Zadias’s external stance.

“A confident person… you could say. One might even call him arrogant.”

Marquis Zilbolt answered. Ah. That might be a common character type among nobles and royalty.

“Zadias used to say that having us manage the magical technology held by the Sages’ Academy would lead to the people’s happiness. I thought that was correct too… but looking back now, there were several times when I found him suspicious and was controlled by the Caex Gem.”

Elliot touched the area around his forehead on the mask.

“I believe… there was talk of an engagement between my elder sister and Zadias, wasn’t there?”

“…Ah. That matter.”

At Rosemary’s words, Princess Stephania made a subtle expression as if enduring a headache. It might have been a topic she didn’t want to touch on.

“Indeed… when I was young, there was talk of a marriage alliance with Silvatoria’s royal family or high-ranking nobles. When I went on a goodwill visit, Zadias showed an unusual interest upon hearing I was a Magician… That’s precisely why it ended up in limbo.”

According to Princess Stephania’s words, that discussion took place before Zadias’s bad reputation spread. It seemed that with the incident of the political upheaval as a turning point, the topic died out, or rather, both sides stopped bringing it up.

From Silvatoria’s side, they probably found it hard to bring up because Zadias had caused problems. On the other hand, the Verdugal side didn’t actively want to pursue an engagement with a problematic Crown Prince either, and then with the matter of the King of Deathly Slumber, they were busy dealing with domestic issues… and so it went.

“However, it seems Zadias hasn’t given up.”

“That’s right…”

Zadias himself seemed fixated on the fact that Princess Stephania possessed considerable magical skill, and he apparently exerted pressure on other blood relatives with rights to the throne and domestic nobles.

Because of that, not only in Silvatoria but also in surrounding countries, they were hesitant about marriage talks with Princess Stephania.

“You understand why I dislike him, don’t you? I want to give him his final dismissal properly in this matter.”

Saying that, Princess Stephania shook her head.

+++

# **258 – The Royal Capital Vinesdora**

“We can see it now.”

Elliot leaned out from the dragon palanquin’s window and pointed ahead. Beyond the pale outer walls stood the royal castle with its blue roofs and tall spires. The royal capital of Silvatoria – Vinesdora.

“Shall we do some shopping first? Then we’ll head to my residence.”

“After that, we’ll need to arrange for an audience,” Princess Stephania nodded in response to Marquis Zilbolt’s words. There were many things to do upon arrival, so they couldn’t afford to rest first.

They first headed to the outer wall’s watchtower to complete the procedures for entering Vinesdora.

“This is Marquis Zilbolt.”

“Well met. We wish to enter Vinesdora – would that be acceptable?”

“Yes, sir! Please proceed.”

They passed through the outer walls as the saluting soldiers saw them off.

The dragon palanquin flew slowly over Vinesdora’s townscape. Reddish-brown roofs and cobblestone-paved roads. White stone pillars stood at various street corners. Crystals atop the stone pillars… those were street lamps. I’d seen them lit up at night in BFO screenshots.

While not particularly innovative as magic tools, they were items limited to major cities like Vinesdora and Termwills.

In terms of scale, it could certainly be called a major city comparable to Termwills. However, compared to Termwills which developed as people settled around the labyrinth, everything from the royal castle to the townscape and outer walls had a unified feel with well-defined districts, giving a much more orderly impression.

Vinesdora should also be a historic town… but since it was built after Beriondora was destroyed, it must have been constructed with thorough urban planning.

The main avenue stretched straight to the castle at the city center. Major facilities also seemed to be located along this avenue.

“That building near the square is the coliseum. You can see the public baths too. That large building is it.”

Marquis Zilbolt gave them a brief tour of the city. Like Termwills, the area around the castle was apparently where the wealthy residents lived.

“Where is the Sages’ Academy?”

“From here, it’s beyond the castle – at the city’s edge. That tall tower is it.”

“Ah… that one?”

At the city’s edge stood a massive tower nearly as tall as the castle’s spires.

“The academy’s magicians basically lived around the tower. Now… there’s some turmoil there.”

“Due to the conflict with Zadias?”

“Yes.”

I see. Buildings could be seen even on the tower’s surrounding grounds. Then… that would be where Mother was, I suppose.

“Should I guide you to the alchemist’s shop?”

“Yes.”

Rosemary nodded at Elliot’s words. Elliot emerged from the dragon palanquin and leaped into the air, landing astride Saphir.

“Then I’ll lead the way.”

“Lindwurm, follow Saphir.”

Lindwurm turned back and called out. The organized wyverns followed Saphir.

They landed the dragon palanquin in front of an alchemist’s shop in one corner of the city. True to an alchemist’s shop, strange odors hung in the air around it.

“Well then, I’ll go do some shopping.”

Rosemary disembarked from the dragon palanquin and entered the shop.

After quickly completing their shopping, they headed next to Marquis Zilbolt’s villa.

It was a large Western-style mansion befitting a marquis’s family, located near the castle.

When they landed the dragon palanquin in the courtyard, Elmer and others disembarked and hurried off to secure the mansion’s safety.

“Master, welcome.”

Soon a servant working at the villa appeared. The servant’s eyes widened at the unexpected visit from the marquis but bowed deeply.

“My apologies. Urgent business delayed our arrival notice.”

“Not at all. We’re always prepared to welcome you, Master.”

The elderly servant smiled as he responded to Marquis Zilbolt’s words.

They hadn’t brought servants from the marquis’s territory. Since this was a sudden visit without prior notice, apparently only a few housekeepers remained to watch the place.

So Marquis Zilbolt had said it might be somewhat inconvenient… but well, we’ll just have to take care of ourselves. Shouldn’t be a problem.

First, let’s get the hair dyeing done. It wouldn’t do if the escorts couldn’t move.

“May I borrow the kitchen?”

“Of course. This way.”

Guided by Marquis Zilbolt, they entered the mansion. They passed through corridors laid with red carpets and headed to the kitchen.

“Well then, shall we begin right away?”

Rosemary arranged the materials bought at the alchemist’s shop on the cooking counter. Tree fruits about the size of a clenched fist, like blueberries. Some liquid in a flask. Powdered medicine wrapped in paper.

Furthermore, what you might call standard ingredients for such mixtures. There were even dried geckos and bat wings.

“…What about a large cauldron?”

“It’s not that elaborate, so a regular pot will suffice.”

She put the tree fruits into the pot and crushed them with a pestle. Adding water to the pot and heating it, she slowly stirred while pouring in the liquid and powder.

“After this – just simmer it a bit and it’s done. Apply it to a comb and comb your hair. We’ll need to apply it to eyebrows and eyelashes too, but we have makeup tools so that shouldn’t be a problem.”

“…It really is simple to make.”

The pot was filled with black liquid. Since this would dye our hair… probably it would become purplish-black hair, I guess.

While waiting for the dye to complete, Rosemary was simultaneously mixing another medicine in a separate pot. This one seemed to use the dried ingredients and wings.

“This one is for removing the dye. Water won’t wash out the color, but this medicine can extract just the tree fruit’s pigment.”

“Huh…”

Convenient stuff. You could call it a decolorant or something. However, this one seemed to require more effort, as she was adding various magical processes like incantations while mixing.

“I wonder if it will become the same hair color as me?”

Claudia said while peering into the pot containing the dye.

“I think it will be a similar color. We could have made other colors, but this one is the safest.”

Well, certainly. Since it has to work for both me and Ashley.

The dye boiled and after coming to a boil once, she removed it from the heat.

“…Well then. Shall we divide the work and get it done?”

“Yes.”

Grace and Marlene brought two chairs.

“Take off your jackets. The color might stain them.”

“Mmm. Understood.”

“Marquis Zilbolt, do you have any spare sheets?”

“I’ll have them prepared.”

And so the hair dyeing preparations progressed rapidly.

After removing my jacket and sitting on the chair with a sheet draped over me, Sheila brought a makeup case from the dragon palanquin. Brush-like tools were taken out and arranged on the cooking counter.

“Hmm. Interesting stuff. Though I doubt it would work on my hair.”

Tephra peered in with interest.

“Fufu. These kinds of preparations are rather fun, aren’t they?”

Princess Stephania laughed.

Though it was for disguise… not just Princess Stephania, but everyone seemed somewhat cheerful. …If I had to describe it, the atmosphere was like preparing for cosplay at a cultural festival.

“First, let’s try dyeing just a little bit and check the color development. If the shade is too light, we’ll add more tree fruits; if too dark, we’ll dilute it.”

Me first. Applying dye to a brush, she combed the tips of my hair. Everyone peered in with serious expressions.

“Here. Theodore.”

“Mmm. Thank you.”

Seraphina held up a hand mirror to show me the result.

One lock of my bangs had become glossy black.

“Yeah. Seems good.”

“Yes. It’s a natural color.”

Irmhild nodded.

“Well then, let’s proceed carefully bit by bit. Try to avoid getting dye on the scalp.”

“Understood.”

Grace and Rosemary divided the work, dyeing my hair from left and right. As each section was dyed, Ashley used magic to remove moisture and dry my hair.

Marlene and Claudia took dye-covered brushes and carefully applied it to my right and left eyebrows. I tried to remain as still as possible so their hands wouldn’t slip. Somewhat ticklish.

“Perhaps we should leave the hair roots and eyelashes to Sheila?”

“Mmm. I’ll handle it.”

Sheila approached directly with a brush. When I closed my eyes, I felt a tickling sensation as she lightly brushed my eyelashes. Then she lifted my hair and lightly brushed the dye onto the still-undyed roots.

“While Sheila does the finishing touches, shall we proceed with Ashley’s hair dyeing too?”

“Yes. Please do.”

Next to me, Ashley also began her hair dyeing. They were dyeing from the tips first while checking the color development. Though using the same dye, since Ashley and I have different natural hair colors, the results seemed slightly different.

“Done.”

“Thank you.”

Sheila handed me the hand mirror.

I checked myself by lifting my hair to see if any spots were missed. For the back, Seraphina held another mirror, showing me through double reflection.

Yeah. Seems good. Since Ashley’s hair is longer, it will probably take more time than mine.

“Safety check of the mansion is complete.”

Elmer returned at that moment. Well, I suppose the disguise and securing our base are mostly complete? While we’re at it, it might be reassuring to create an emergency hidden room in the marquis’s villa too.

+++

# **259 – Princess Stephania's Visit**

“How does it look?”

Ashley’s hair dyeing was complete. Perhaps because her original hair was silver, the black color turned out slightly lighter on her than on me, with a somewhat purplish tint.

…Somehow. Combined with her eye color, it suits Ashley quite well.

“Yeah. It looks good on you.”

When I answered honestly, Ashley nodded happily.

“What other colors are available?”

“Well—”

Perhaps because the results turned out well, everyone was enthusiastically discussing hair dyeing. Since the color could be easily removed and wouldn’t damage the hair, it seemed they could enjoy coloring it casually. They were getting quite excited about what colors would suit Marlene and such.

Hmm. It’s a harmonious girls’ gathering, but I should do what I can before we go out.

“If you’d like, I was thinking of using Magic Construction to create an underground passage and hidden room. What do you think?”

“An underground passage?”

When I brought this up to Marquis Zilbolt, he showed a slightly puzzled expression.

“Essentially, it’s an emergency shelter. You could also station soldiers there secretly.”

“Oh? That sounds quite interesting.”

Since Marquis Zilbolt seemed enthusiastic about the idea, I had him show me the floor plan of the villa and decided to create the entrance to the underground passage in a secluded study that would be difficult to breach from outside.

I created an underground passage by making the entire wall with bookshelves into a Revolving Concealment, and made a room large enough for everyone to enter.

I also created an exit from the emergency room side. The design was such that attackers who thought they had cornered someone in the study would instead find themselves attacked from behind. I would have liked to install other anti-intruder mechanisms as well… but I had to head to the Royal Castle to arrange the meeting appointment. For now, I decided to keep it to the bare minimum to maintain appearances.

“Well, that should do for now. If we get surrounded or invaded by enemies, we can retreat to the study to prepare for counterattacks, and both Surprise Attacks and pincer attacks would be possible… that’s the idea.”

“…I’ll have weapons and preserved food brought in.”

Marquis Zilbolt grinned.

“This is quite amusing.”

Princess Stephania seemed to really like the bookshelf Mechanism. She kept going in and out of the passage by rotating the Revolving Concealment bookshelf.

“Hmm, hmm hmm… Well, I suppose we must go to the Royal Castle and arrange the meeting procedures.”

Princess Stephania seemed to notice our gaze and cleared her throat, straightening up as if regaining her composure.

…Whether it’s abundant curiosity or something else. I’ve heard that Princess Stephania has a reputation as a well-behaved lady… but this is probably her true nature.

“What about making something similar in your sister’s territory?”

“I don’t mind.”

I nodded in response to Rosemary’s words.

“Oh? That would be wonderful.”

Princess Stephania’s territory is also relatively close to Silvatoria. Having such emergency shelters might provide some peace of mind.

Let’s wrap up the emergency room discussion here for now and get moving.

We boarded the carriage driven by Sheila disguised as a servant and headed to the Royal Castle. Tephra, Elliot, and Marquis Zilbolt remained at the villa for temporary standby. We also left Caduceus, Lavigne, Ambrum, and Ignis behind as combat power and communication liaisons for the villa side. I planned to keep our cards hidden until the very last moment before the meeting when things would start moving.

Apparently, King Eberhart of Silvatoria and King Melvin of Verdgar had some level of interaction even before each ascended to the throne and were old acquaintances. Princess Stephania’s marriage arrangement likely started from that connection.

“Your Highness Stephania, you mentioned you’re acquainted with His Majesty Eberhart, correct?”

I asked Princess Stephania.

“Yes. When I was little, I was invited to tea parties with Father and Josiah. …I remember him as a calm, gentle person.”

“Are there any trusted figures among His Majesty Eberhart’s senior advisors?”

When Rosemary asked, Princess Stephania thought for a moment before answering.

“They’re not exactly senior advisors, but… there are several.”

“If those individuals view the Crown Prince as problematic, they might become allies.”

“That possibility is quite high.”

I nodded at Grace’s words.

Having multiple people on our side who are familiar with Silvatoria’s domestic affairs, including the positions of others, is reassuring. If anyone makes contact with us, we’ll assess them while considering their background.

The carriage crossed the Royal Castle’s drawbridge and stopped after entering inside the castle gates. The maid serving at the Royal Castle who came out to greet us seemed slightly surprised when she saw Princess Stephania disembark from the carriage, but only for a moment. She bowed respectfully to Princess Stephania. They seemed to be acquainted.

Well… that makes sense. We have the Emblem indicating we’re envoys from Verdgar displayed on the carriage. When assigning someone to handle the reception, they would likely choose someone familiar.

“Princess Stephania. How wonderful to see you.”

The maid nodded at her words, and Princess Stephania conveyed her purpose.

“It’s been a while, Carmela. I heard about His Majesty Eberhart’s condition and have come, though rather belatedly.”

“That… His Majesty the King would surely be delighted.”

The maid… Carmela smiled.

“However, I don’t expect to be able to meet him immediately. Since I don’t know the detailed circumstances, there might be various inconveniences with such a sudden visit. That’s why I’ve come today.”

It would be diplomatically unacceptable treatment for both countries if a foreign princess visiting to see the king wasn’t granted either a formal audience or a private visiting opportunity.

So by first arranging a meeting appointment, they could schedule it for when King Eberhart’s condition is better, and give the Silvatoria side preparation time, thus considering both sides’ dignity… that’s what Princess Stephania was saying. It’s somewhat roundabout… but precisely because they used his sickbed as pretext to hesitate granting an audience during the previous envoy’s visit, it would be difficult to refuse this.

“Understood. Please come this way.”

“Please handle this appropriately.”

From the maid’s position, this wasn’t something she could answer or promise. Carmela proceeded to guide us inside the Royal Castle.

We were Princess Stephania’s companions, also serving as attendants and Escorts. Therefore, carrying swords inside the castle was permitted to some extent. This must be unique to royal visits.

We proceeded through the spacious castle corridors and were shown to the Royal Castle’s guest room. It was a lavishly decorated room.

The maid who guided us relayed information to other servants. The servant who heard the maid’s words bowed and left the room. They probably went to inform the appropriate person about Princess Stephania’s visit and its purpose.

“Will Your Highness Stephania be staying at the Royal Castle?”

“I came to Silvatoria accompanying Marquis Zilbolt, who was visiting Termwills. I plan to stay at the lodging he recommended.”

That high-class inn right near the Marquis’s villa. Well, actually, it would be Ambrum disguised as Princess Stephania staying there.

“Marquis Zilbolt, you say?”

Carmela’s eyes widened.

“Yes. It’s very close to the Marquis’s villa. Besides my attendants, the Marquis has arranged Escorts for me, so I feel quite secure.”

When Princess Stephania responded with a smile, Carmela’s expression clouded.

Carmela briefly showed a gaze that seemed to be gauging our expressions. Noticing this, Princess Stephania asked.

“…Is there something about the Marquis?”

“N-no. It’s just, well…”

“It’s alright. They’re all from Verdgar and trustworthy individuals. Please speak freely without hesitation.”

Princess Stephania encouraged Carmela to continue with a gentle smile.

“Well… I recalled that Marquis Zilbolt was close with His Highness Zadias…”

Carmela said hesitantly.

“…I see. So that’s how it is.”

“Um… I…”

“Don’t worry. Given your position, saying more would be difficult. I’ll keep your words in mind. I won’t let them reach other ears.”

Princess Stephania answered with a quiet smile. At this response, Carmela showed a relieved expression. What had crossed her mind was clearly wariness toward Marquis Zilbolt—and toward the Crown Prince behind him.

Yes. We were also considering the possibility that someone opposed to Zadias might attempt contact with Princess Stephania, either to warn her or request cooperation.

Officially, Marquis Zilbolt is close to Zadias. So if someone concerned about Princess Stephania’s safety who appears to trust the Marquis, they would likely be apprehensive about the Marquis providing Escorts. That’s why the Marquis didn’t accompany us this time.

Conversely, those who make contact under such pretexts would be emotionally on our side.

Carmela had been worried about Princess Stephania enough to reveal that she holds a poor impression of Marquis Zilbolt and Zadias.

From her position, trying to convey that must have taken considerable courage. That she tried to communicate something difficult to say is probably due to Princess Stephania’s virtue.

Of course, we know the circumstances the Marquis faced, so we trust him, and the Marquis himself agreed to use his ill reputation to distinguish friend from foe. …Once the Zadias matter is resolved… we must absolutely restore the Marquis’s honor, that’s for sure.

In any case… Carmela seems like someone we could trust to some extent, as long as it doesn’t burden her. If we want to probe the situation within the Royal Castle, she would be our starting point.

“Is His Highness Zadias here now?”

“No. He’s currently absent. He’s staying at the Sages’ Academy, saying he’s busy with Magic research and development.”

Oh ho. That’s convenient. He probably sent Elliot because his hands were tied to begin with.

Still, if he’s at the Academy, he’ll likely notice Princess Stephania’s and Marquis Zilbolt’s visits before too long.

He’ll probably… make contact with us. As for Alvelinde… should we have Elliot spread misinformation to buy time until the Surprise Attack?

Hmm… That one was a Demon, so how about hinting that she went to Beriondora for some reason?

+++

# **260 – The Purpose of That**

As I was pondering various countermeasures, a knock echoed through the room.

“Come in.”

When Princess Stephania invited the visitor in, an elderly man entered.

He was a well-built man whose appearance suggested high status.

“Ah, Your Highness Stephania, what a pleasure to see you. Welcome.”

“It’s been too long, Lord Stanley.”

Stanley greeted Princess Stephania with a friendly demeanor.

“I heard you’ve come to pay a visit.”

“Yes. How is His Majesty Eberhart’s condition?”

At Princess Stephania’s words, Stanley closed his eyes.

“His Majesty’s condition is… somewhat delicate. We cannot speak carelessly about such matters. However, I shall do my best to accommodate Your Highness’s wishes as much as possible.”

“I leave it in your hands.”

When Princess Stephania bowed slightly, Stanley’s expression softened momentarily. But he quickly returned to a serious demeanor.

“Regarding an audience, we must first confirm His Majesty’s wishes and consult with the court physician to select a suitable day. For that reason, I cannot make any definite promises at this moment…”

“You mentioned His Majesty’s wishes?”

“There is a possibility he may not wish to be seen in his weakened state. He hasn’t appeared in public for some time now.”

“…I see.”

That certainly… matches the explanation for why the messenger couldn’t meet him.

“However, it shouldn’t take much time to convey His Majesty’s wishes regarding this matter. I came ahead to explain the current situation, as I felt you needed to be informed.”

Right. Even if he refuses, it’s much more acceptable than being told you simply can’t meet him after being made to wait. However, if he does refuse, things might become somewhat troublesome. Because we can’t confirm whether it’s truly King Eberhart’s intention.

“My apologies for the trouble. Actually, when visiting Silvatoria, we brought along those skilled in healing techniques, wondering if we might be of some assistance.”

“Oh?”

Stanley’s eyes widened.

“Of course, I’m aware of the high level of magic in Silvatoria. But we thought that techniques outside the norm—not just healing magic, but also Cursed Melodies, the Moon Goddess’s Blessing, and so on—might perhaps provide some aid in his recovery.”

“Is that so? Well, of course! Termwills of Verdgar is renowned for its wealth of talent! I shall convey this immediately!”

Stanley instructed the escort soldier to relay Princess Stephania’s words. The soldier saluted and left the guest room.

It was true that we actually possessed various systems of healing techniques. From our perspective, there were no flaws in this approach, and it gave us a reason to meet King Eberhart together with Princess Stephania.

Conversely… if they refused this, it would significantly increase the likelihood that King Eberhart’s absence from public appearances was due to some other reason.

This move was partly about probing the other party’s intentions… well.

As Stanley had said, the response from King Eberhart didn’t take very long.

“His Majesty says he would very much like to meet with Your Highness Stephania.”

Stanley, having received the report from the returned soldier, relayed this with a smile.

…So that means the story about his sickbed is likely true.

“That’s wonderful. So he will grant us an audience?”

“He appears delighted by Your Highness Stephania’s visit. Of course, your attendants are welcome to accompany you as well.”

“Then for today, we shall return to town and await the meeting date with anticipation.”

Saying this, Stephania provided the location of their inn.

Stanley seemed in high spirits, but when the conversation turned to Marquis Zilbolt’s escort, his expression clouded for just a moment. This man also must have some thoughts regarding the Crown Prince.

Stanley concluded the discussion at the royal castle by saying he would send a messenger from the castle to the inn where Princess Stephania was staying. While they would proceed while monitoring the King’s condition, there was probably also the aspect of setting up a reception to entertain Princess Stephania.

Although, at the inn, it would be Ambrum, the shadow clone, who would actually be staying.

Elmer’s subordinates were handling the personal security for the shadow clone. They knew Ambrum, and their loyalty to Marquis Zilbolt was unquestionable, so disclosing information to them wasn’t particularly disadvantageous.

Returning to Marquis Zilbolt’s secondary residence, I immediately recounted the events at the royal castle to everyone who had been waiting.

“Well, I suppose it’s a smooth start, wouldn’t you say?”

Claudia looked at me as she spoke.

“Yeah. There’s still much we won’t know until we meet.”

First, we needed to ascertain King Eberhart’s thoughts and verify his illness. We wanted to identify and eliminate possibilities like him being controlled, or a magical creature or demon impersonating him, as soon as possible.

We could counter curse magic and magic potions with the Moon Goddess’s Blessing and the Amulet of Evil Repulsion. The possibility of control or a fake. That could also be discerned using circulating ki. Since I knew what a real Doppelganger was like, I could detect differences even after a transformation.

“It’s good that we have a prospect for a meeting. But for my part, I’m curious about why Zadias is moving about in all these various ways.”

Rosemary tilted her head.

“What do you mean?”

“If it’s about the Crown Prince’s position, normally he would just inherit the throne by waiting. Even if he had ambition, acting openly without hiding it would only disadvantage Zadias in the succession.”

Saying this, Rosemary glanced at Marlene. Marlene nodded with a solemn expression.

In Rosemary’s case, precisely because her claim was weak, she didn’t take the straightforward approach and didn’t hide her ambition. In contrast, Roy had aspects where he maneuvered to keep himself inconspicuous.

If staying silent meant stability, then even if he harbored ambition, it would be more rational to act after inheriting the throne. Well, that’s how it would go.

“His objective… must lie somewhere other than the succession itself from the beginning.”

“Yeah. I agree with Grace on that. If he isn’t afraid of being disinherited, he might be considering usurpation in case of an emergency.”
