Zadias likely takes the succession itself for granted. That’s probably why he came up with the idea of managing the populace using Gems and is advancing preparations for that.

“It’s hard to imagine it’s for King Eberhart’s treatment… He wouldn’t need to use such methods; if he explained the situation, many people would cooperate.”

Ashley said this. Was this her thinking from her own perspective? That kind of thinking is important too.

If King Eberhart’s condition was top secret, they wouldn’t have revealed it to the messenger in the first place. So the line about not being able to explain the situation doesn’t hold.

“If we assume King Eberhart has had a chronic illness since long ago… that might be a plausible possibility, I suppose? For example, if it’s hereditary… he might become desperate for his own sake too.”

But that would require ignoring Zadias’s various methods.

In fact, Tephra looked somewhat skeptical.

“I understand why Tephra isn’t convinced. I’m just considering possibilities and ruling them out.”

“Hmm. I don’t really understand the thinking of human children. Well, I trust Theodore though.”

“Yeah. He helped me too.”

At Tephra’s words, Seraphina, perched on her shoulder, nodded. Hmm. Well, I do want to properly live up to that trust.

“What are your thoughts, you two?”

Prompted by Princess Stephania, Marquis Zilbolt answered.

“Regarding the details of His Majesty Eberhart’s condition, only a very limited few in the palace could know… However, the duty assigned to me was to grasp the weaknesses of the nobles. It didn’t seem very related to treatment.”

“…I remember now. About that, he said it was a pretext.”

Elliot, who had been thinking with his arms crossed, spoke up.

“A pretext?”

“He said that by claiming it was research for treatment, he could act with a certain degree of freedom. I heard him say that to his close Black Knights once.”

“I see…”

Regardless of the ultimate purpose, that explanation made some sense regarding his actions so far.

Using King Eberhart’s treatment as a pretext to justify his forceful methods. That might be part of the reason Zadias’s actions were tolerated. If he argued it was for treatment, it would be emotionally difficult to punish Zadias severely.

The same goes for his methods. Accusing the Sages’ Academy of withholding methods they had for treatment, and demanding information disclosure. He could probably argue that it was for the people’s benefit as well. Since it’s a royal family matter, such information wouldn’t be disclosed externally. Even so… Zadias’s bad reputation spread as a result.

The problem lies beyond that. Zadias’s actions far exceed what could be excused by that pretext. That’s probably why he used Marquis Zilbolt to carry out covert operations for things that couldn’t be covered by the treatment pretext.

If he had his Black Knights, who should normally be by his side, make conspicuous moves, there was a risk his schemes might be leaked to King Eberhart.

“In that case, it seems the secrets held by the Sages’ Academy, or the research Zadias is advancing, must be extremely valuable to him.”

“I think that explanation fits better too.”

I smiled wryly at Sheila’s words.

“What about cooperation between His Majesty Eberhart and Zadias?”

“Hmm. At this point, I think that possibility is also slim.”

This judgment was based on Zadias explicitly stating it was a pretext behind the scenes, and the fact that they readily accepted the visit.

However, the point Irmhild raised was, in a way, even more important than Zadias’s movements. We need to ascertain that part clearly.

That said, we can only judge further matters by observing the individuals involved. Not only the meeting with King Eberhart, but Zadias will likely make some moves before the messenger from the royal castle arrives as well.

+++

# **261 – Zadias and Elliot**

“May I have a moment?”

Elliot spoke up as the conversation reached a natural pause.

“What is it?”

“I too must go report to Zadias.”

Hmm. After this, Princess Stephania’s shadow clone was supposed to head to the lodging.

Given that the situation had calmed down, it would be natural for Elliot to go report to Zadias as well.

“Will I be asked to remove my mask?”

“No. If anything, I’m told not to remove my mask too often.”

From Zadias’s perspective, he’d probably want to avoid exposing the Caex Gem to public view.

“…Perhaps it would be better to make some slight disguise after all.”

Better safe than sorry, as they say. When I glanced at Rosemary, she nodded.

“Yes. I bought a similar-looking gem from an alchemist’s shop.”

Good. Let’s have him wear a gem. I shape and polish it using Earth Magic and Water Magic to resemble the Caex Gem. While working on it, I go over various details with Elliot, anticipating his conversation with Zadias.

“Regarding Marquis Zilbolt’s companion… Please hint that they headed in the direction of Beriondora. You can present it as hearsay from Marquis Zilbolt – that they said they’d caught some interesting information through Termwills and were going to meet an old acquaintance. That should be appropriate.”

“Understood.”

There’s no need to explain these circumstances in minute detail. Even if Alvelinde’s actions were somewhat unnatural, there’s no reason she would explain the details to Elliot or Marquis Zilbolt.

By dangling information related to that demon group, Zadias himself will read deeper into Alvelinde’s actions. That should also help determine whether Zadias knew Alvelinde’s true identity.

“Sheila. The sticky thread.”

“Mm.”

Using the Arachnear Ring’s sticky thread, I attach the gem to Elliot’s forehead after he removes his mask.

Hmm… Would it pass unless someone examined it closely?

“I’ll have Caduceus accompany you. He’s aware of the situation here, so if you sense danger, retreat. In that case, we’ll come to rescue you from here as well.”

“Understood.”

“Do you have a map of the town?”

“Yes. I have one prepared.”

Marquis Zilbolt brings a map. As expected of someone who commands an intelligence unit, he understands the importance of knowing the terrain. Well prepared.

“The meeting point should be near the Sages’ Academy… Somewhere inconspicuous would be best.”

“In that case, how about here?”

“Yes… I think this will do.”

While looking at the map, we discuss emergency procedures and assign Caduceus to stick with Elliot.

“Then I’ll be going.”

“Brother Elliot, please be careful.”

“It’s fine. I may be just a minor noble, but I should be able to handle some diplomatic maneuvering.”

Elliot smiled back at Ashley, put on his mask, threw on his surcoat, and headed to the courtyard. Mounting the hippogriff Saphir, he took off and flew toward the Sages’ Academy.

“I’ll prepare to move out immediately too,” Claudia said.

“Please do. I’ll also update Termwills on our progress.”

If worst comes to worst, we could lure them in and use teleportation magic to send them all to the labyrinth at once. Still, if we can just take down Zadias alone, that would be preferable. Using teleportation magic would essentially mean kidnapping the crown prince with teleportation magic.

I don’t want to worsen relations between Verdgar and Silvatoria.

Even if we ultimately crush Zadias, the process leading there is crucial. Ideally, we should properly lay the groundwork and reveal it at the right time.

“Sir Benedict.”

As Elliot landed with Saphir before the Sages’ Academy grounds, the gate guard greeted him.

“Good work. Is His Highness Zadias here?”

“Yes! He’s in the tower. Please wait in the guesthouse.”

“Acknowledged.”

The academy was surrounded by high walls. Within the grounds was a well-maintained small forest. Walking paths extended through it, creating a lush park-like atmosphere… a quiet ambiance isolated from the outside world.

…They said the academy’s magicians live here. So this would be Mother’s hometown then.

Various facilities seemed scattered throughout the grounds. The magic research facilities were probably concentrated in that tower area.

Figures of magicians. There were also magic knights clad in black armor. It appeared Zadias and the Black Knights had made this their base.

Elliot wasn’t led to the tower deep within the grounds, but to a room in the guesthouse located fairly close to the gate.

After Elliot waited in the room for a while, the door opened without even a knock. A well-built man with a smile plastered on his lips entered the room… It was Zadias.

“Your Highness Zadias.”

Elliot welcomed this completely improper entrance without protest, using a subordinate’s greeting as if he’d expected it from the start.

For a moment I wondered if he’d detected Elliot’s betrayal and burst in… but that didn’t seem to be the case. He hadn’t brought even one guard.

Zadias appeared to be in his mid to late twenties. Average build… From his physique, he seemed to have some martial arts training.

“Let’s hear your report. What about that woman?”

“Yes. I witnessed her accompanying the Marquis at his domain. However, she herself borrowed a carriage from the Marquis and apparently headed elsewhere. I also confirmed that Marquis Zilbolt and Verdgar’s First Princess, Her Highness Stephania, were traveling together.”

“Oh?”

Zadias raised one eyebrow, his expression turning suspicious.

Here, Elliot would provide information about Princess Stephania’s visit. Once Zadias returned to the royal castle or received communication from there, he would learn about it anyway.

“Her Highness Stephania apparently came to visit His Majesty Eberhart.”

“…So the messenger who came to Verdgar earlier must have informed her of my father’s condition.”

“I returned to Vinesdora while escorting the Marquis and Her Highness Stephania along their journey.”

“…Hmm. We’ll set aside Stephania for now. Tell me more about that woman.”

Zadias seemed more concerned about Alvelinde than Princess Stephania, urging Elliot to continue.

“I thought she would also accompany the Marquis… but she said she had business and was heading west by carriage. According to the Marquis, she said she was going to meet an old acquaintance.”

“West…?”

Zadias twisted his expression in displeasure. He crossed his arms, brought a hand to his chin, and seemed to be thinking.

“…Should I have gathered more detailed information? The escort swordsman seemed quite wary of me.”

“No. I shouldn’t have given you such orders.”

“Forgive my presumption.”

“Fine. That woman and her escort aren’t exactly my subordinates, and our trade has concluded. Since we’re each doing what we should, if she showed herself to you, she’s probably fulfilled her obligation.”

Though clearly displeased, Zadias said this and shrugged his shoulders.

…I see. So Zadias and Alvelinde were somewhat equal partners.

Given that he didn’t provide Elliot with much information and didn’t let him get too involved… we should probably assume he knows Alvelinde’s true identity. If he let Elliot stick his neck out recklessly, it could mean losing a pawn for Zadias.

But… then the content of their trade becomes the question.

What benefit did Zadias receive from Alvelinde, and what did he offer in return?

Bringing Marquis Zilbolt under his control was undoubtedly beneficial for Zadias. But what about his subsequent moves against Verdgar? Trying to secure Mihaela and Cecilia’s town? Searching for Patricia’s magic? Whose interests did each of these serve?

Or perhaps… their interests aligned. But at the very least, as compensation for the curse magic, Zadias must have provided something to Alvelinde.

“Her Highness Stephania apparently went to the royal castle and made arrangements to meet with His Majesty. She said she would take lodging near the Marquis’s secondary residence, and Marquis Zilbolt said he would provide personal security.”

“…Ah. That lodging. Well, I know the location.”

Zadias nodded.

“Benedict. You continue monitoring the Marquis and Stephania. Take a room at the same lodging and report if anything unusual occurs. If asked for a reason, you may say you’re the guard I assigned to the Princess.”

“Yes.”

By making Elliot’s proximity known, he probably intends to prevent anyone hostile to Zadias from approaching. Externally, it would look like he’s trying to score points by being attentive to Princess Stephania. Well… this works conveniently for us.

“Tell Stephania I’ll come greet her later.”

“As you wish.”

Elliot bowed. …So he’s coming to the lodging. I should probably station myself near Ambrum as part of the guard.

+++

# **262 – Demonstration**

“It seems Elliot-san was told to serve as Princess Stephania’s escort.”

“That’s good…”

Elliot was already en route on Saphir. When I briefly explained the situation over there, Ashley let out a relieved sigh. The tension among everyone seemed to ease as well.

“In this case, would that make him a spy from Zadias?”

“Probably. He’s supposed to report any unusual developments to Zadias, so we’ll need to coordinate our stories.”

I responded to Claudia’s words. If we’re going to use misinformation, the intelligence we feed them needs to be just right – not too much, not too little, with natural moderation. Since the risks are significant, we should avoid it unless absolutely necessary.

From our perspective, we can never be too cautious. If this is all an act and they’ve already detected Elliot’s defection while ordering him to monitor us, that would be quite impressive. Even if things are going well, we’re still in enemy territory, so we should assume that even a surprise attack wouldn’t be enough.

“Well then, Sister. Over here.”

“Yes.”

Rosemary, Princess Stephania, and Ambrum headed together to the adjacent room.

They were going to change Ambrum’s clothes to make him a shadow clone and send him to the inn. Though Ambrum was wearing servant’s clothes, transformation would cause issues with clothing sizes and other problems, so they needed to change him beforehand, which required some effort.

When they returned, there were two Princess Stephanias, but one of them was Ambrum… Probably the real one is the one wearing servant’s clothes and looking happy. It seems Princess Stephania has something like admiration for lifestyles other than that of royalty.

“Your Highness Stephania, your hand please.”

“Thank you, Ashley.”

Blood was needed for Ambrum’s transformation. Ashley used healing magic to seal the wound on her fingertip.

“Well then, let’s move.”

When the treatment was finished, I nodded at Grace’s words, and almost all party members moved to the inn where we planned to stay. However, the real Princess Stephania, Seraphina, Lavigne, Ignis, and Tephra were too conspicuous, so they remained at the villa.

“Once we secure rooms, I’ll connect the underground passage.”

“Okay. See you later.”

Seraphina and Tephra waved us off.

It would defeat the purpose if Marquis Zilbolt’s villa became underprotected. Though I feel bad for the innkeeper, we’ll connect an underground passage from Marquis Zilbolt’s villa to the inn room with the understanding that we’ll fill it in once we’re done.

“This is Her Highness Stephania. I’ve heard from the Marquis’s messenger. Please, this way.”

The innkeeper guided us to our rooms. To make it easier to connect to the underground passage, we took three rooms on the first floor. Ambrum would be in the middle room, with escorts staying in the rooms on either side to secure the area.

“These rooms don’t face the main street – will that be acceptable?”

“Yes.”

Ambrum, controlled by Rosemary, nodded.

Being on the first floor makes it easier to escape if something happens, and facing the back alley means that if they try to surround the inn, personnel deployment would be delayed and the encirclement would be thinner.

“I’ll be using this room during my stay in Vinesdora. Please take care of us.”

Ambrum paid a rather generous amount as an advance. Well, it includes what you might call inconvenience fees. The apologetic innkeeper initially tried to refuse, but when Ambrum said it was for taking care of us, he respectfully accepted.

It doesn’t hurt to make a good impression on the innkeeper and staff. Combined with Zadias’s lack of popularity, it might work to our advantage in various ways.

Hmm. So we’ve finally prepared for our stay in Vinesdora.

Zadias arrived the following day, in the afternoon.

Elliot was staying in a room facing the main street. Caduceus, who was waiting in the same room, kept watch on the main street and was the first to spot the group arriving in a carriage accompanied by knights.

“He’s here, it seems.”

Everyone nodded at my words. Though they were dressed as servants as part of Princess Stephania’s escort, everyone was armed with swords or wore dragon scale equipment under their clothes, maintaining full combat readiness. Since they appeared lightly equipped, they probably just looked like ordinary security.

That said, the military force Zadias brought with him was also small. At this point, we probably had enough leeway to disguise our equipment. I had a rapier, Grace had a staff – we switched our usual weapons to different ones, keeping our cards hidden until actual combat begins.

Even if they stormed our room, it would only create a scandal with no benefit.

Ambrum was waiting at a sunny table in the inn’s dining room, pretending to enjoy post-meal tea. Myself, Grace, Sheila, and Elliot were standing by as escorts nearby.

The others were with the real Princess Stephania in the inn’s basement. Caduceus would serve as the liaison between both groups.

“Sir Benedict. May I have a moment?”

“What is it?”

An inn employee called Elliot over and whispered to him. Elliot nodded and reported to Ambrum.

“Your Highness Stephania. His Highness Zadias has arrived.”

“Please show him in.”

Ambrum smiled and replied as if everything had been arranged. When Elliot conveyed Ambrum’s response to the inn employee, the employee bowed respectfully and returned to the lobby where Zadias was presumably waiting.

The flow is fairly smooth. If things got bogged down here, Elliot would probably be criticized for poor arrangements.

“Your Highness Stephania. You’re looking well.”

Zadias entered the dining room and bowed with a cheerful demeanor.

“Your Highness Zadias. It’s been too long.”

Ambrum stood up, gathered her skirt, and returned the bow.

“My, you’re as beautiful as ever.”

Zadias said things like that… but we already knew from his interactions with Elliot that he didn’t hold even a shred of respect for Princess Stephania.

“Thank you. Please, over here.”

Zadias was prompted to sit opposite Ambrum.

We had no intention of deliberately adopting a hostile stance to raise their alert level.

“My apologies for the delayed greeting. I’ve been rather busy, you see.”

“That’s unavoidable. As fellow royalty, I believe I can understand.”

“I’m relieved to hear you say that.”

After exchanging these diplomatic pleasantries, Ambrum spoke.

“Thank you for dispatching Sir Benedict. Thanks to him, I’ve felt secure both during the journey and since arriving in Vinesdora.”

“It’s nothing significant. Since he wears a mask, I thought you might be somewhat confused.”

“Marquis Zilbolt is someone of confirmed identity.”

“Was that so? However, arranging accommodation like this commoners’ inn… One might call that man lacking in refinement. The royal castle would be far safer, wouldn’t it?”

We anticipated he would suggest we check out of the inn and stay at the royal castle instead. Rearranging the structure to set up a security system to our advantage would be impossible in the royal castle. Even if it’s just a shadow clone staying there, we have no intention of moving from here.

“No, no. This is what I wanted. Sometimes I wish to stay at inns like this and enjoy the travel atmosphere and foreign air. Besides, this inn is quite high-class, and with Your Highness Zadias and the Marquis providing escorts, I have no complaints or concerns.”

Ambrum returned a smile with a rather Princess Stephania-like explanation. Apparently, it’s actually quite a high-class inn even for Vinesdora. The staff’s attentiveness is thorough, and I don’t feel any dissatisfaction either.

“Hmm. Then the lack of refinement was on my part. Since the escorts accompanying Your Highness are quite young, I became somewhat concerned about the possibility of something happening. I know this might sound misleading, but please don’t take it the wrong way.”

“Ah, I understand that intimidation is necessary for escorts. While they’re quite skilled, they don’t cause tension with their appearance, making them perfect for visiting an allied nation.”

“I see. So that was your reasoning.”

“Mathius.”

“Yes.”

When Ambrum called my name, I stepped forward. Though my hair was dyed, I wasn’t wearing a disguise ring. Well, it’s a pseudonym anyway.

“Since it’s a good opportunity. As entertainment during our tea, why don’t you demonstrate your martial arts for His Highness Zadias?”

“Oh?”

Zadias narrowed his eyes with interest. If he came to probe us, he’d probably want to gauge the extent of our combat capabilities.

“Though just a child, a Verdgar military officer. And serving as Princess Stephania’s escort at that… This is quite interesting…”

“Then, please excuse my poor display.”

I bowed in response. What I would demonstrate was rapier skills, not staff techniques, and fighting spirit, not magical power.

We moved together to the terrace seating facing the main street.

“Sheila. When I give the signal, could you toss some small stones to an appropriate height?”

“Understood.”

Sheila responded. I drew my rapier and sliced through the air several times, demonstrating rapier maneuvers referencing both the rapier movements Mihaela taught me and the movements of BFO players I remembered.

Occasionally, I showed thrust-based combat skills adapted from staff martial arts, stepping in simultaneously. When I signaled Sheila with my eyes, two, then three small stones were thrown upward.

“Hah.”

I exhaled briefly, bisecting one stone, then skewering two more stones in midair consecutively with my blade wrapped in fighting spirit.

“This is splendid. I didn’t expect someone of that age to move so well.”

“Right? I’m also looking forward to his future.”

Ambrum and Zadias applauded, and I bowed in response.

Zadias’s smile showed composure. Though my abilities exceeded what he expected based on my age, he probably thought this level wasn’t threatening.

After all, I was only applying staff martial arts and martial arts to rapier handling – I wasn’t using circulating ki or demonstrating even a single aerial combat technique.

From Zadias’s perspective, he has Elliot too, and he probably thinks rapiers are disadvantageous against the armored Black Knights.

Well, that’s fine. It’s more convenient for us if Zadias underestimates the military force Princess Stephania brought. Let’s have him keep underestimating our combat capabilities until just before we reveal our hand.

+++

# **263 – The Princess's Secret Letter**

“Speaking of which, I heard you’ve been looking into healing methods for my ailing father.”

“Yes. I thought I might be able to help if it involves techniques different from ordinary Healing Magic.”

The conversation seemed to have shifted to matters concerning the visit to the sickbed.

“Is that so? I’ve also been researching magic for my father’s recovery… but perhaps a different approach might offer some prospects.”

“I hope that proves true. Actually, I still haven’t been told anything specific—what exactly is His Majesty Eberhart’s condition?”

“You’ll understand when you meet him in person. If those around my father are keeping it secret, it would be better if I didn’t speak of it either.”

“Understood.”

“I pray it goes well.”

With those words, Zadias stood up.

“Well then, Your Highness Stephania. My apologies for the haste, but I must take my leave now. Messengers from the Castle might arrive as early as today.”

“Yes.”

Ambrum also rose to see Zadias off.

“Benedict. Make sure you protect Her Highness properly.”

“Yes, sir.”

From whom, and for what purpose was she to be protected? After offering Elliot superficially polite words meant only to maintain appearances, Zadias left the inn.

After Zadias departed, we went from the inn room down to the basement and reported everything to everyone.

“Honestly…”

After hearing the full account, Princess Stephania frowned with what seemed like displeasure.

“For someone of royal blood… his words carry remarkably little weight.”

Claudia also closed her eyes and shook her head.

The way he treated Marquis Zilbolt and Elliot differently in public versus private, or his pretense of researching magic for King Eberhart’s recovery. The gap between Zadias’s true intentions and his outward behavior must have given them thoughts about him as a member of the royal family.

Rosemary was hiding her mouth behind a feather fan, but she seemed to be smirking. Well, Rosemary herself had utilized her own infamy and never shied away from taking the forefront. Compared to her, Zadias’s methods—with his smooth path to succession already guaranteed from the start—probably seemed half-hearted.

“If Zadias isn’t researching for treatment… then what is he researching?”

Grace tilted her head.

“Magic that the elders of the Sages’ Academy had kept secret… or perhaps techniques brought about through connections with Demons?”

“Does Elliot know?”

“…Sorry, Ashley. I don’t know the specifics of what he’s researching either. Zadias seemed concerned about when Gem control occurs and what long-term effects it might have. When Gem-induced control seemed likely, he would at least provide some justification, even with me.”

When Ashley asked, Elliot answered with some apparent guilt.

He had been used for experiments… but since he was more useful to Zadias than expected, he probably wasn’t pushed to the point of being used up. If Gem control happened frequently, the burden on the wearer would likely be significant.

Even if the justifications seemed like flimsy excuses to normal observation, they served to facilitate the Gem’s control.

“I’m not very familiar with Zadias’s inner circle… but aren’t the current Black Knights composed of factions originally close to Zadias from the Magic Knight Order and Sages’ Academy?”

“I believe so.”

“Then outsiders likely can’t get involved. If he was only maintaining appearances, Lord Elliot would be in the same position.”

Marquis Zilbolt added to Elliot’s words as if supplementing them.

So Zadias was colluding with those who had won the Faction Conflict and taken control of the Sages’ Academy.

“What about Zadias’s influence over the entire Magic Knight Order? Just the official story is fine.”

“Official story… meaning if we ignore the collaborators, correct? In that case, moderately… I’d say. Not particularly strong.”

Elliot answered. In other words, typical for royalty.

This meant that if Zadias were clearly at fault, the entire Magic Knight Order serving King Eberhart wouldn’t side with him.

But thinking about it differently, it also meant that despite not controlling the entire national army, Zadias was maneuvering behind the scenes with that show of composure.

“Perhaps he’s confident that even if his plot is exposed, he can seize the throne by force, or he possesses enough military strength to show such composure.”

“…That’s not composure, it’s arrogance. When your methods succeed a few times, you start thinking they’ll work again. I’ve learned this painfully well, but it’s difficult to recognize when things are going smoothly.”

With that, Rosemary shrugged. Marlene nodded emphatically at her words.

Rosemary was probably thinking about her experience with me. Marlene might be recalling Roy’s actions. Well… I should take this to heart too, since I might get tripped up if I treat it as someone else’s problem. We have several unexpected cards up our sleeve, and I want to effectively utilize our strengths by pressing them advantageously.

“Ah. Another carriage has arrived.”

In Caduceus’s field of vision, a carriage appeared coming down the main street.

“This time? The messenger from the Royal Castle you mentioned earlier?”

Sheila tilted her head.

“Probably, yes.”

The carriage bore Silvatoria’s national flag. It was undoubtedly a messenger from the Royal Castle… but the escort seemed rather large for a simple envoy.

…Probably because they’re wary of Marquis Zilbolt? If so, it might be a messenger from someone who holds a grudge against Zadias…

“Hmm… Should I speak directly this time if it’s a messenger from His Majesty Eberhart?”

Princess Stephania tilted her head.

“Understood. Regarding the escort, we’ll continue as before. Also, I have a slight idea…”

As she said this, Princess Stephania blinked.

“—According to the court physician, His Majesty’s condition has stabilized. Therefore, the day after tomorrow or the following day… the sooner, the better. If Your Highness Stephania has any preferences, they wish to coordinate. Please convey any requests.”

The court lady who came from the Royal Castle seemed to be here to arrange the schedule for the meeting with King Eberhart.

“I too look forward to the day I can see His Majesty Eberhart again as soon as possible. I’m pleased to hear sooner is better.”

“Understood. Then shall we set it for the day after tomorrow?”

“Please proceed accordingly.”

She exchanged such words with the court lady.

“Your Highness, how do you find Silvatoria after your long absence?”

“Well, I’m still unsettled, so it’s not quite like sightseeing…”

The court lady’s gaze wandered about, seeming somewhat restless. Then, from the direction of the inn’s back entrance, voices that sounded like people arguing could be heard.

“…What’s going on?”

Princess Stephania tilted her head.

“I’ve been ordered to guard Your Highness’s safety. I’ll go check.”

With that, Elliot left his seat. The guards Marquis Zilbolt had assigned to Princess Stephania also peered out the back window as if trying to discern the source of the voices.

Noticing this out of the corner of her eye, the court lady smiled somewhat awkwardly.

“…Are these people escorts from Verdgar?”

“Yes. They’re all trustworthy individuals.”

When Princess Stephania answered with a smile, the court lady suddenly erased her smile, took a letter from her sleeve, and placed it on the dining table.

“This letter is from Her Highness Adriana. I also have a message from Her Highness. She said she’s looking forward to seeing you again.”

“I’ve received it. I’ll be sure to read it later… during a quiet, calm moment. Please give her my regards.”

Just in case, considering any eventuality, I took the letter. I didn’t detect any suspicious weight or magical power. As I hid it in my breast pocket to keep it from others’ sight, the messenger’s expression showed relief.

“…I’m relieved to have fulfilled my duty.”

The court lady let out a deep breath, smiled, bowed, and departed.

Hmm. Well, the convenient disturbance that caused Elliot and Marquis Zilbolt’s subordinates to leave their posts… was of course no coincidence.

If there were watchful eyes, a messenger from the anti-Zadias faction would find it difficult to act, so we intentionally created an opening. Those causing the commotion outside were both Elmer’s subordinates, so they’ll probably withdraw at an appropriate time.

“Adriana is my friend. She’s Zadias’s half-sister… and the First Princess of Silvatoria.”

Princess Stephania gave a brief explanation.

…I see. She went through the trouble of creating an opening to contact Princess Stephania. It seems safe to consider her an ally.

# **264 – The Memories of the Princesses**

Carrying the secret letters, I head from the inn room to the underground hidden room. First, I need to check the contents of Princess Adriana’s secret letter.

We gather in the underground hidden room from our respective guest rooms.

“I shall excuse myself. Regardless of the actual circumstances, Her Highness Adriana would not wish for the letter’s contents to reach me.”

After Elliot said this, Marquis Zilbolt also nodded.

“I see. In that case, I too should probably excuse myself.”

Thus, Elliot returned to the inn and Marquis Zilbolt returned to his separate residence. How dutiful of them.

“Here you go.”

I hand the secret letter to Princess Stephania.

“Thank you.”

Princess Stephania smiles as she receives the letter and begins reading it.

Her expression as she reads through the text… seems to show strong confusion about something.

“…There are many metaphors. I don’t want to misinterpret anything, so I’ll let everyone hear it too.”

After saying this and looking around, Princess Stephania reads the secret letter aloud. The letter begins with greetings. The problem comes after that.

“…As is customary for royalty, you must be feeling constrained with many eyes watching your every move. However, since there are many capable individuals around my brother, if they are protecting him, your stay should be peaceful and safe. I too feel somewhat constrained, but I accept this as the fate of royalty.”

Pausing there, Princess Stephania lifts her face.

…I see. Indeed, these are metaphors. Even if the secret letter were stolen, the content could be defended as mere small talk.

“This seems difficult for me to understand… but in terms of meaning, can we interpret this as saying Zadias has surveillance in place?”

When Tephra tilted her head and spoke, Marlene nodded as if affirming her words.

Marlene hardly speaks either, but she was born into royalty. Both of them are following the conversation well.

“Well, if we take the text at face value, there’s no need to be so cautious.”

“Then, the part about ‘I too feel somewhat constrained’ means that Her Highness Adriana herself is under surveillance and cannot act freely?”

“Probably. And the part about ‘peaceful and safe’ might also mean there’s no danger as long as we behave quietly?”

When Grace tilted her head, Rosemary nodded.

“Or it could also be interpreted as peace and safety from Zadias’s perspective.”

“…It doesn’t clearly state for whom it’s peaceful and safe. Perhaps it applies to both meanings. That as long as we don’t take action, we’ll be safe for the time being.”

In response to Ashley’s words, Claudia covered her mouth with her hand as she answered.

It’s highly likely that Zadias is plotting something, but if we don’t cause any disturbances, there shouldn’t be any problems. Well, that’s probably it.

Princess Stephania nodded and said, “I’ll continue reading,” then proceeded further with the letter.

“I too have been spending quite boring days, but when I heard Stephania was coming to Vinesdora, I’ve been looking forward to when we can meet again. Writing this letter reminds me of old times. Do you remember when we were little? We can’t behave like that anymore due to our positions… but sometimes I think it might not be bad to return to our childlike hearts occasionally. Peace is also something precious, so I can’t say that adventurous days like treasure hunting or monster extermination are unconditionally good. Well then, let’s meet again at the royal castle.”

…After reading up to that point, Princess Stephania places the letter on the table. That appears to be the end of the text.

“…This part is also metaphorical?”

“Probably. But… it might be something we wouldn’t understand.”

Sheila and Irmhild exchange glances.

Hmm… Indeed, unlike the beginning, this part is difficult to interpret. It could also be taken as conveying something only Princess Stephania would understand.

“She mentions peace again toward the end.”

Seraphina, riding on Lavigne’s back, mentions what she noticed.

“…Could it mean she wants our cooperation but doesn’t want us to force ourselves?”

Grace speaks while pondering. Considering the meaning of the first part, that would make sense. If the meaning of peace applies to both interpretations, this could also be taken to mean it would be inconvenient for Zadias.

“…She’s probably asking if I’m prepared. That she won’t blame me if I refuse.”

Princess Stephania closes her eyes.

“Do you have any idea?”

“…Probably. Long ago, I played in the orchard owned by Adriana and His Majesty Eberhart. There was a sapling that Adriana planted in the orchard… We would play treasure hunting games, hiding treasures at the base of the sapling and searching for them. We’d make riddles about which sapling it was and guess the location.”

…That’s it. She probably hid the real purpose there. If the destination is the orchard, Zadias would be less suspicious, meaning she has that much freedom of movement.

“…After sunset, I’ll send Caduceus. Do you remember the location of the fruit tree Her Highness Adriana planted?”

“Yes. I remember that… but is it alright if I don’t go?”

“I don’t think going alone would be a problem… but it might make Zadias suspicious. If it were just one of you, it probably wouldn’t have been a problem, but Her Highness Adriana went to the orchard after learning of Your Highness Stephania’s visit, right?If they visited in quick succession, even separately, it would likely raise Zadias’s vigilance. Besides, there should be no need for her to go in person if Caduceus alone can handle it.

“I’ll create a model of the orchard using earth magic based on Caduceus’s visual information. Please guide us.”

“I see… How convenient.”

After sunset, based on the map received from Marquis Zilbolt, we send Caduceus to the orchard. Once night falls, it’s Caduceus’s domain.

Upon arrival, he immediately begins creating a model of the orchard from one end using earth magic. The orchard is well-maintained. It has the atmosphere of a walled garden.

“This is the main gate.”

“Let me see…”

Many years have passed. Princess Stephania traces her memory while following the model with her finger.

“This way… no. Yes. Up these stairs—. It’s ahead there.”

We advance Caduceus according to Princess Stephania’s guidance.

“Third from the right. This tree. It’s grown much larger than I remember, though.”

“Let’s check the base.”

We have Caduceus examine the soil at the base.

“…Found it.”

From beneath the soil emerges a small wooden box. When I report this, Princess Stephania’s expression brightens. Let’s have him retrieve it and return.

Soon after, Caduceus returns. With the wooden box, without doubt.

“Well done, Caduceus.”

I take the wooden box from Caduceus and hand it to Princess Stephania.

“Thank you. I’ll open it now…”

With a slightly tense expression, Princess Stephania opens the wooden box.

Inside—there’s another letter. This must be the real one.

“I’ll read it.”

Princess Stephania reads the letter aloud for us again.

“You remembered the old times. Thank you, Steph. And I’m sorry for involving you.”

The letter begins with such an opening. The writing style is more casual than the first letter.

The letter states… that Zadias is searching for magicians from the Sages’ Academy. We already knew that much.

Princess Adriana had been hiding one of the magicians Zadias was searching for within her territory.

And—that magician apparently passed away some time ago. He was apparently elderly to begin with. At that time, he had entrusted something to her.

But Zadias has been continuously tracking the magician’s whereabouts.

There’s no guarantee that information won’t leak by some chance. It’s also unclear how Zadias will treat others with royal succession rights after he becomes king.

Therefore… she wants Stephania to take custody of what the magician left behind. She wants it stored in Verdgar until the time it’s needed. That’s what was written.

“…What was entrusted by the magician is an incomplete spell formula. That itself is the fragment of magic that Zadias is searching for… apparently.”

“An incomplete… spell formula?”

The content of the letter Princess Stephania was reading aloud struck a chord with me.

Could that be… the half-complete magic circle mentioned in Mother’s notes…?

Whether it was under development or something else. Compared to other items, there was less description, and I thought the full form of the spell formula would be revealed if we deciphered the codes on other pages—but.

“…This is it.”

Drawn on the second sheet, which was finely folded, was a half-complete magic circle. —Like a puzzle piece fitting perfectly, it formed a complete spell formula in my mind.

“I’ll continue. …The cornered elders sealed their own memories with their own magic. By doing so, they invalidated torture and all other means of extracting confessions, preventing the leakage of secret techniques. A hope to recover the sealed memories someday—after the tyrant has passed. They divided this and entrusted it to their comrades. And this spell formula is one part of that. I know this is a selfish request. When true peace returns to Silvatoria someday, could you deliver this magic to Vinesdora? …That’s the end of the letter.”

After finishing reading the letter, Princess Stephania closes her eyes and exhales deeply.

A spell formula to release sealed memories… I see… So this is the magic of Mother’s that Zadias was searching for.

…No, probably not just this. If she was entrusted with guarding the memory release spell formula, she must have been highly trusted by the elders, and likely possessed other secret techniques of the Sages’ Academy too.

And if Zadias understands the situation, he cannot carelessly kill the academy’s elders either. So that’s why… Mother left the country to protect them.

In that case, they’re probably imprisoned somewhere—deep within the academy or another location. If we eliminate Zadias, shouldn’t we be able to restore their memories using the completed spell formula?

+++

# **265 – The King's Illness**

“Mother likely took one half of the spell formula with her when she fled Silvatoria. Since I possess the other half… the complete form exists within my mind.”

As I spoke, everyone’s gazes gathered on me.

“Ah… So that’s why you had Marquis Zilbolt search for Lisa-sama’s magic.”

Grace closed her eyes and let out a small sigh.

“Yes. The current conversation has clarified several things for me.”

If we were hiding the Memory Release Formula from Zadias, we couldn’t conceal our own memories. Therefore, it was highly likely that we possessed the magic held by the elders. Whether there was concrete evidence or not, Zadias searching for magicians who had been at the Sages’ Academy was… well, only natural.

“I see… So Lisa-sama…”

Princess Stephania mentioned that when she crossed over to Verdugal by ship as a child, she had also met Mother.

In any case, Mother headed to Termwills, then became an adventurer who explored labyrinths… and eventually met Father.

Well, she might have met Princess Stephania after becoming an adventurer. Mother probably also investigated the situation in Silvatoria.

“I believe this must have been a matter of concern for Mother as well.”

“Theodore-sama…”

Ashley furrowed her brows with worry. When Marlene looked at Princess Stephania as if wanting to say something, she gave a wry smile.

“While you are the Otherworld Ambassador… unless you intend to hand that magic over to Zadias, Verdugal has no standing to comment on how that magic should be handled. I don’t believe you would use it for some negotiation with Silvatoria, and Father should feel the same. I received one half from Adriana… and similarly, I entrust that fragment to you.”

“Thank you.”

Considering Princess Stephania’s position, I needed to properly report to King Melvin via the communication device. Well… perhaps I’ll have Alfred convey it.

“At any rate. First, we should ascertain His Majesty Eberhart’s physical condition and thoughts, I suppose.”

Claudia spoke.

…That’s it. While the worst-case scenario of him being Zadias’s accomplice seems to have been eliminated, his actions must have caused considerable mental strain. Given that we’ve only been told he’s confined to his sickbed… depending on his condition, the question remains whether we should tell him the complete truth.

I’d like to minimize the shock King Eberhart would receive as much as possible.

“What about contacting Her Highness Adriana? Shouldn’t we inform her that we’ve taken over the matter?”

“I’ll send her a letter. She’s bored with the monotony, so if I write that along with greetings I’d like to play with her like when we were little, Adriana will understand that I’m cooperating. …I’d like to write about monster-slaying games, but that might be too direct even as a metaphor?”

Princess Stephania smiled wryly. Monster-slaying games, huh. That must be her frank opinion of Zadias.

“…Did you really do that? Such things.”

“Yes, yes. It’s from when we were children.”

When Rosemary showed a slightly exasperated expression, Princess Stephania blushed a little and cleared her throat.

“We should also ensure Her Highness Adriana’s safety.”

“Indeed. Well, let’s consider wording that wouldn’t be problematic even if intercepted.”

Since it would be based on Princess Adriana’s metaphorical secret letters, making the meaning comprehensible only to her… even if someone read the exchange from the middle, the underlying meaning would become even more obscure, perhaps.

They began discussing the letter’s wording in detail, saying this and that. Their consultation seemed rather enjoyable as well.

After sending the letter indicating our intent to cooperate with Princess Adriana, there were no more visitors, and we didn’t venture outside either, so superficially everything was quiet.

And soon, the day of our appointment with King Eberhart arrived.

“Please, this way.”

The maid who welcomed and guided us when we arrived at the royal castle by carriage was Carmela, the same as during our first visit.

Sheila, Tephra, Ambrum, Lavigne, Ignis and the others would remain behind for now. While Tephra is a witness to Zadias’s deeds, she couldn’t remain hooded indefinitely, nor could we risk another encounter with Zadias. We plan to have them join us with Marquis Zilbolt at the most effective timing while monitoring the situation here. If anything happens, we can communicate via the device, so it’s not a problem.

We proceeded through the castle’s spacious corridors, passing the audience chamber. When we reached the area before the royal family’s living quarters, Carmela turned to us and bowed.

“I shall take my leave here.”

Another court lady took over as guide. The fact that even among maids, access to the castle’s inner depths is restricted—it seems they’re quite meticulous about concealing information regarding King Eberhart’s condition.

“His Majesty Eberhart awaits. However, before entering this room, there are several things I wish to convey.”

When we reached an especially large door, the court lady turned to us and spoke.

“What might they be?”

“First of all… His Majesty’s appearance may differ somewhat from what Your Highness Stephania remembers. Additionally, regardless of the healing outcome, everything you see and hear about His Majesty must remain confidential.”

“…Understood. I swear upon the honor of the Kingdom of Verdugal.”

At Princess Stephania’s words, the court lady nodded and knocked on the door.

“Her Highness Stephania has arrived.”

“Hmm, let them enter.”

When the reply came from within the room, the door slowly opened inward.

A spacious room. Inside, several royal guard magic knights stood by. The court physician. And the Court Magician. Other royals didn’t seem to be present. Only close aides, it appeared. That Zadias wasn’t here… well, that makes things easier.

Princess Stephania bowed formally to the room’s master. We followed suit.

“…It has been too long, Your Majesty.”

“Well, you’ve come. First, raise your heads and show me your faces. Your attendants as well. You intend to treat me, after all. I’d like to see your faces properly.”

The room’s master—King Eberhart—lay upon a bed. The right half of his face had transformed into something resembling a dragon’s appearance. This… might be better described as mid-transformation rather than an illness.

“…Hmm. Princess Stephania, you’ve grown quite beautiful. While I have ended up in this state.”

After surveying our faces, King Eberhart narrowed his eyes. The dragonified half of his body also smiled.

“We heard you were confined to bed and were concerned for your well-being.”

“There is pain during progression… but no matter, it’s not life-threatening. Well, it is troublesome, though. Like this, I cannot appear in public.”

He said it jokingly… but I understand. So this was the reason he couldn’t meet the envoy.

“Ordinary healing magic doesn’t work, and even the unique healing magic passed down in Silvatoria is meaningless. While temporarily restoring my appearance is possible, it quickly reverts to this state. Since it only means experiencing intense pain for longer, I’ve left it as is.”

“I see… So that’s how it is.”

“My apologies regarding Verdugal’s envoy. Not to make excuses, but the timing was unfortunate. My condition was worse than now, and the pain made speaking difficult. There was also a proposal to use a shadow clone, but we hesitated since that might cause unnecessary misunderstandings among the nobles.”

“…I can imagine how you must feel.”

Silvatoria’s unique healing magic. That must be the reconstruction magic Mother used for healing.

But… if physical reconstruction doesn’t work and the condition progresses… this can hardly be called an ordinary illness. If not some form of curse, then perhaps related to magical aptitude…?

“It can’t be helped. This is something like the fate borne by Silvatoria’s king.”

“You know the cause? …What is it, exactly?”

“Remember, this must remain confidential?”

King Eberhart smiled ruefully.

“Silvatoria is said to be hated by ancient demons. Therefore, whoever becomes Silvatoria’s leader must perform a ritual each year to disperse the curse so it doesn’t target the entire nation. But… that ritual isn’t perfect and requires a small price.”

Is that… similar to how Verdugal’s king performs the Nation Protecting Ceremony?

“The price… could it be”

“Yes. The body is gradually eroded with each ritual. Normally, it only causes temporary health issues without major problems… but depending on magical aptitude, mutations like this can occur. I’ve grown old, I suppose. The mutation speed has increased.”

In other words, this is… erosion caused by miasma.

Demons are beings who leave nothing behind when they perish. If “ancient demons” refers to the demon lord, then this is…

The lord wasn’t destroyed. Only sealed. Awakening… meaning if the miasma characteristic of the demon lord that promotes demon mutation also applies to King Eberhart’s symptoms… the mutation aspects match in various ways. There’s also the example of the half-demons created by Gardinis.

“…That’s the situation. The point of telling you this is… you mentioned taking a different approach, but even if it proves ineffective, I won’t blame you.”

King Eberhart laughed in that manner.

But… what about this? Magical power circulation is a technique to counter demons. And it’s also a lost technology from Silvatoria. Using circulating ki to… neutralize and purify a body eroded this far by miasma—might that be possible?

+++

# **266 – Ancient Bloodline**

“Let’s begin the treatment immediately. Well then… I’ll be in your care.”

“Understood.”

Stepping forward as Princess Stephania’s gaze turned toward me, I bowed to King Eberhart and took his mutated hand… First, I needed to assess his condition.

“You mentioned there’s pain in the mutated area, correct?”

“Indeed.”

…The tissue was mutated, but life functions were still active.

I thought it might be sufficient to neutralize and purify the mutated parts… but circulating ki alone probably won’t be enough. It would be better to combine it with other methods. Release the magical power contaminated by miasma from the body. Then replenish the released magical power with new energy. And to prevent the released miasma from causing adverse effects… that’s when a blessing would be necessary.

“I’ll use the blessing and cursed melody from the start. Water magic and magic potions will depend on the condition. If there’s pain during treatment, I’ll use water magic or medicine to reduce it.”

When I explained my approach, everyone nodded. As Marlene made a prayer gesture, golden phosphorescence spread throughout the room. The blessing’s targets were the party members and King Eberhart.

“This is the Moon Goddess’s blessing… But this strength of blessing…”

King Eberhart murmured. Marlene had solid skills as a shrine maiden, and Claudia, the goddess herself, was present here. If one wanted something of higher quality than this, the only option would be to bring many shrine maidens from the Moon Temple.

Irmhild played the cursed melody on her lute, and Seraphina amplified its effects.

“…A cursed melody performer with spirit assistance. Indeed, this is an unprecedented method.”

King Eberhart laughed cheerfully. The effect of this cursed melody was to strengthen the listener’s vitality and enhance natural recovery abilities. We concentrated the effect, which would normally spread naturally, specifically on King Eberhart.

“Well then—let’s begin.”

I placed my hand on King Eberhart’s back and began circulating ki.

“What…?”

Instantly, King Eberhart’s eyes widened. That kind of reaction was expected.

Looking at King Eberhart’s internal magic power, I could see his brow furrow slightly. Due to contamination by miasma, the flow of magical power had become different from normal. Particularly in the mutated parts, it no longer seemed human.

I began organizing the flow of magical power from the boundary between the mutated and non-mutated areas. I refined magical power and sent it in.

I didn’t return excess magical power from King Eberhart back to me. Instead, I expelled it outside. Pitch-black miasma was released and scattered by the blessing. Unlike normal circulating ki, this consumed magical power, but that couldn’t be helped. In terms of imagery… it was similar to a blood transfusion.

“Is there any pain?”

“No… Though I do feel a kind of numbness.”

King Eberhart seemed to postpone his inquiries. The slightly relaxed atmosphere from earlier disappeared, replaced by a serious expression as he repeatedly clenched and unclenched his mutated right fist.

If I wasn’t causing him pain, I would gradually refine and strengthen the magical power further. I returned the disturbed flow of magical power to its normal state, and like expanding territory, I pushed back the contaminated areas with the circulated magical power.

“This, is…”

“O, oh…!”

King Eberhart and his aides let out astonished voices.

The mutated dragon scales began peeling off from the edges. Within the phosphorescence of the blessing, they disappeared into the void as if turning to dust. Beneath them was new skin.

Yes… Since demons can switch between different forms at will… this shouldn’t be irreversible either.

But it still wasn’t enough. To completely expel all the miasma that had seeped into the core of the contaminated area—

“Your Majesty. May I have permission to take up my magic staff?”

“If that’s necessary, then permission is granted.”

“Grace. Ouroboros.”

“Yes.”

The answer was simple. I just needed to increase the output. Grace brought out Ouroboros, wrapped in cloth, from the luggage she had entrusted to the maid. Taking it in hand, I said:

“Well then—”

Through Ouroboros, I enhanced the quality and quantity of magical power in the circulation.

Excess magical power overflowed from my body, tinting the room pale blue.

“Th-this magical power…!?”

The court magician’s eyes widened. It even absorbed and neutralized the leaking miasma. The proper flow of organized magical power… probably affected the physical body as well. King Eberhart’s mutated body was being restored to the form a human should have.

When an especially intense white light subsided—the figure that had been half-human, half-dragon had returned to human form.

“Unbelievable… such a thing…”

King Eberhart blinked as he gazed at his restored right hand. Looking at the mirror brought by a maid, his eyes widened even more.

“Since demons can transition between their forms quite freely. If we consider that as similar to magical spell formulas or magic manipulation methods, I thought that if we removed the cause, he might return to human form.”

“…I see. Indeed, I’ve heard they change forms as if transforming.”

“Is there any pain or discomfort?”

“No. Though I did have a throbbing pain all this time.”

When King Eberhart got up from the bed and stood, his aides let out emotionally charged voices.

But on my side, I was somewhat tired from consuming the enhanced magical power through circulation. I probably used magical power equivalent to multiple high-tier magics?

As I exhaled deeply, Ashley cast vitality recovery magic on me, and Rosemary brought her improved magic potion.

While receiving Ashley’s magic, I drank the magic potion in one go. Well, after a while the magic potion would take effect and my condition would return to normal.

“First, I must thank you. I’m grateful you purified my corrupted body.”

King Eberhart said quietly.

“Your words are too generous.”

Even though I removed King Eberhart’s miasma… this didn’t mean Silvatoria’s problems were solved.

“You, that was circulating ki, wasn’t it?”

“…Impossible. Why would someone from Verdugal…?”

At King Eberhart’s question, the court magician’s eyes widened.

Well, of course the conversation would go this way. I knew from when I first heard about King Eberhart’s condition that I would need to use circulating ki, so this was an expected development.

Crucially, King Eberhart’s complexion had improved considerably. With this, discussing Zadias probably wouldn’t be too burdensome.

If I were to explain why I can use circulating ki, I couldn’t avoid talking about Mother. There’s no point in discussing BFO matters here.

“I’ll explain the reason.”

“Indeed. But first…”

King Eberhart glanced at his sleeping attire and smiled wryly.

“I must make myself presentable. For the sake of decorum, would you mind waiting for a short while?”

“Hmm. I’ve taken up your time.”

We were shown to another room—what appeared to be a salon. While contacting the people at the marquis’s residence via communication device and waiting with everyone, King Eberhart soon arrived. Unlike his previous attire, this time he was in formal wear for receiving guests. King Eberhart settled into a chair and had the maids bring tea and sugar confections.

“Now, would you tell me your story?”

“First… I’d like to explain why I can use circulating ki.”

“First, you say. So it seems to be a complicated matter indeed. Regarding both my illness and its treatment, as well as the discussion here, shall we agree that neither side speaks of it to others?”

Perhaps sensing something from my and Princess Stephania’s demeanor, King Eberhart inquired. The reason King Eberhart’s illness was kept secret… was probably because the mutation caused by miasma might suggest connections with demons. When his condition was unstable, even releasing miasma might have been a risky state.

Similarly, the story about my mother’s origins isn’t something Verdugal would want made public either, not just Silvatoria. Verdugal is in the midst of fighting demon groups.

When I nodded, King Eberhart also nodded, then said:

“Indeed. Circulating ki itself existed in Silvatoria as a purification method against miasma. According to records, the number of users gradually decreased… and about a century ago, the last user died out.”

“Is that so…”

“Even though the techniques were barely passed down, those with the appropriate magical aptitude and those who could handle it satisfactorily simply couldn’t be trained. Those transmitting the technology seemed to have made efforts… but by the time they noticed, there were aspects where mixed blood had progressed significantly. It was unfortunate for the royal family, but this couldn’t be helped.”

…If someone from another country appeared possessing it, King Eberhart must have been imagining various possibilities. First, I bowed and introduced myself.

“My name is Theodore Gartner. My father is Henry Verdim Gartner, a noble of the Kingdom of Verdugal. Currently, I’ve received the position of Otherworld Ambassador from His Majesty Melvin and work in Termwills handling labyrinth-related matters.”

“The child of a noble from the Kingdom of Verdugal?”

“I’m an illegitimate child and have already left my family home to become independent, so I don’t have strong connections with the count’s household.”

“Hmm.”

King Eberhart tilted his teacup. Watching for when he set down the teacup, I broached the core matter.

“Do you recall the name Patricia, who was listed among the Sages’ Academy?”

“Patricia—of the ancient bloodline…! So, your mother was the Sealing Shrine Maiden!?”

King Eberhart’s eyes widened as he rose slightly from his chair.

Ancient bloodline and Sealing Shrine Maiden… I had thought he might have information I didn’t know about.

“I’m not familiar with the terms ancient bloodline or Sealing Shrine Maiden. My mother’s name was different from Patricia, and she never fully disclosed the circumstances… to either me or my father.”

“The end…?”

“My mother fought a demon called the King of Deathly Slumber, and that’s what caused her to lose her life.”

“Deathly Slumber… That was the demon that caused significant damage in Verdugal, wasn’t it?”

King Eberhart frowned at my words, then shook his head and sat back down.

“I won’t ask for details about the fight with demons now. It must be painful memories for you to recount.”

“Yes. Let’s return to the main topic.”

When I answered, King Eberhart closed his eyes.

“…Due to Zadias’s failure, I’m aware that talent left the academy. Yes… So the shrine maiden also fled our country. Changed her name… and went to Verdugal.”

A failure… It seems King Eberhart also had to acknowledge that Zadias’s actions were indeed a mistake.

At least externally, since it concerned his own future and the royal family’s prospects, he could recognize some legitimacy in Zadias’s claims. That’s probably why there was some aspect of requesting information disclosure from the Sages’ Academy, and it must have been difficult to condemn him for it.

But if asked what the actual situation was… given that he uses treatment as a pretext, Zadias’s magical research doesn’t seem to truly have that as its purpose. Even without circulating ki, the Silvatoria royal family has managed until now.

There are mountains of things I want to ask and must discuss.

Sheila and the others are currently heading toward the royal castle. We’ll have them look at King Melvin’s personal letter and evidence gems, and have Marquis Zilbolt and Elliot also be present to explain the circumstances so far.

+++

# **267 – Secret Talks at the Royal Castle**

“I now understand why you can use Circulating Ki. It was said that if there were any prospects for the future, they would likely come from magicians of the Ancient Bloodline.”

“…What is the Ancient Bloodline?”

“Legend says they are families descended from the magicians of Beriondora, much like the Silvatoria Royal Family.”

King Eberhart closed his eyes and began to explain.

“As the number of those who could use Circulating Ki decreased and several valuable Spell Formulas were scattered and lost, those with lineage connected to Beriondora were gathered to protect and pass these traditions down.”

It seemed somewhat understood that families close to Beriondora tended to produce excellent magicians. Therefore, marriages were arranged among these families… likely an attempt to revive the magician groups that fought against demons. Hence the term Ancient Bloodline. Aspiring magicians who admired them also gathered, eventually forming what would become the Sages’ Academy.

…This sounds similar to the Verdgar Royal Family.

In the battles against demons, magicians who could use circulation decreased in number, and techniques were lost. Or perhaps due to mixed bloodlines causing decline, they gathered those with similar backgrounds to increase bloodline purity. Those called elders would be the family heads of the Ancient Bloodline… that seems to be the case.

“What about the Sealing Shrine Maiden?”

“They say a special daughter from the Ancient Bloodline inherits the title… The detailed origins aren’t clear… and they currently have circumstances that prevent us from hearing their story. Volheim and others at the Sages’ Academy are researching ways to resolve the situation, but the results haven’t been promising.”

Volheim. The vice chancellor during the Sages’ Academy internal conflict… Given this, it seems he hasn’t reported to King Eberhart about pursuing magicians with the Memory Release Formula.

In any case, including matters about the Sealing Shrine Maiden, it seems we’ll have to ask the elders about those details. Let’s move on to the main topic.

“Actually… part of the reason we came to Silvatoria this time involves disturbances stemming from the Sages’ Academy internal conflict.”

Here, I bring up Princess Stephania’s reason for coming to Silvatoria. Perhaps sensing something suspicious, tension increases in King Eberhart’s expression.

“First… would you please read the personal letter from His Majesty Melvin?”

Princess Stephania presents King Melvin’s letter to King Eberhart. King Eberhart checks the wax seal and begins reading the letter. As he reads further, his expression grows severe.

Regarding the letter’s contents, first it writes about what has been understood so far concerning demons.

The objectives of the demon groups heading toward Verdgar, what was understood from deciphering Ancient Documents, and the hypothesis deduced from this – the possibility that there might be demons in Beriondora.

It also writes about incidents involving Zadias. The bandit disturbance, the attack on Gartner County, the blackmail against Marquis Zilbolt’s family as background, and that the identity of the blackmailer was a demon. Everything.

From King Eberhart’s perspective, the information that there might be demons in Beriondora would be shocking enough, but the part suggesting Zadias might be involved in the blackmail against Marquis Zilbolt’s family must be quite an impact.

If King Eberhart takes actions favoring Zadias’ side after this… well, we’ll have to make some decisive moves ourselves then.

“Is this… true?”

King Eberhart puts a hand to his forehead as if enduring a headache.

“There were many aspects where we couldn’t grasp the full picture of who was pulling the strings… so we were uncertain about how and to whom we should convey this information.”

“…I see. The envoy who came previously probably had this as their main topic too… If I were said to be bedridden in this situation, anyone would be cautious.”

King Eberhart seems to have grasped our movements and circumstances quite accurately.

“If necessary, I’ll undergo Magical Inquisition.”

I convey this, but King Eberhart shakes his head.

“Such measures would be far too shameless. It’s proper for us to verify the facts ourselves. In this case… it would be best to follow the strategy mentioned in the personal letter.”

The strategy in the personal letter… that would be using the plaster statue to issue notices about gathering information on Alvelinde within Silvatoria.

“Marquis Zilbolt is currently heading this way. Could you hear directly from the Marquis? Spirit Tephra is also accompanying us, which should help verify the story.”

“Accompanied by a High Spirit…”

King Eberhart shows a somewhat strained smile and calls a maid, instructing her to escort everyone to the inner chambers when Marquis Zilbolt arrives.

“Please grant your forgiveness for what Marquis Zilbolt has done.”

“…If that story is true, then as a lord it was unavoidable. Fundamentally… it’s my foolishness for allowing

sycophants

to run rampant while I lay ill.”

…Running rampant, huh. There’s probably someone responsible for reporting to King Eberhart… and that person likely has connections with Zadias. We’ll need to be cautious about the informant within the Royal Castle.

“Marquis Zilbolt has arrived,”

reports a lady-in-waiting.

“Hmm. Show him in here.”

As King Eberhart nods, Marquis Zilbolt, Elliot, and Tephra appear. They’re all wearing hoods. Sheila has accompanied them as escort.

Lavigne and Ignis should be in the carriage they rode to the castle, standing guard. They can’t exactly stroll around the Royal Castle, so they’re staying in the carriage.

Ambrum… is still playing the shadow clone role. He shows himself at windows dressed as Marquis Zilbolt, or transforms into Elliot to wait at the inn, being quite diligent about camouflage operations. Basically, he’s taking the role of disrupting location tracking.

Though he’ll also serve to warn Elmer and guide them to evacuate to the annex basement.

“Well come, Marquis Zilbolt. Spirit Tephra. And Sir Benedict. No, it’s Sir Elliot now, wasn’t it?”

While waiting for Marquis Zilbolt, I explained Elliot’s entire situation. Elliot, hearing his name, removes his mask and kneels. Tephra also removes her hood, revealing her face.

Ashley’s hair color has been restored with color remover. Comparing Elliot and observing Tephra, King Eberhart sighs.

“You’ve suffered hardships due to my foolishness.”

“Your words are too generous.”

Marquis Zilbolt and Elliot each respond to King Eberhart.

“I came along to testify to Marquis Zilbolt’s innocence but…”

Tephra tilts her head, looking somewhat uneasy.

“…I’ll believe you. I too am something of a magician. I wouldn’t mistake a spirit for something else, and I’ve heard stories about the High Spirit dwelling in Mt. Tephra.”

At King Eberhart’s words, Tephra shows a satisfied smile.

“These are the evidence items.”

I present the wooden box containing the plaster statue and Caex Gem. King Eberhart frowns upon seeing inside the box.

“…We’ll have to use these to shake up Zadias. We must summon him before he becomes suspicious and prepares his defenses.”

“We don’t know who might be informing him. There are parts that also need reporting to His Majesty Melvin, so if permitted, we’d like to be present at that meeting as well.”

I make the request. King Eberhart considers my words for a moment before asking.

“…I see. I’d heard Verdgar possessed a Demon Slayer… is it you?”

If I’m a magician who can use Circulating Ki, it’s natural he’d draw that conclusion.

“Yes.”

“…Then, I’ll swallow my pride and say this. I’d like to request your presence.”

“I’d like to ensure Her Highness Adriana’s safety as well,”

says Princess Stephania.

“Adriana?”

“It seems surveillance eyes are on her. She warned us to be cautious.”

“Understood. — Someone! Call Adriana here.”

At King Eberhart’s words, a lady-in-waiting bows and goes to fetch Princess Adriana. If it’s King Eberhart’s summons, even if there’s surveillance, they shouldn’t be able to stop her. Ensuring Princess Adriana’s safety is necessary.

Before long, Princess Adriana appears in the inner Royal Castle. She was said to be Princess Stephania’s friend… but her appearance is, how to say… fitting for the title of princess, with the aura of a sheltered young lady. Though her true nature is probably different.

“…Father… your appearance is–“

“Yes. It seems this treatment was successful.”

Princess Adriana’s eyes widen at King Eberhart’s appearance.

“That is most wonderful. Please forgive me for being unable to report my brother’s suspicious movements.”

“Fine. If I had noticed, he might have resorted to force.”

That’s right… King Eberhart was bedridden and unable to move, so if cornered, he might have assassinated King Eberhart, claimed it was illness, and purged those who knew the circumstances.

Princess Adriana was carrying secrets and was being watched as a rival for the throne, so there were parts where she couldn’t move freely.

“Steph… thank you.”

“No, Adriana. I’m glad you’re safe too.”

Princess Adriana turns to Princess Stephania, takes her hands, and they rejoice at their reunion.

“Zadias… isn’t in the Royal Castle?”

Meanwhile, King Eberhart, having received a report from a lady-in-waiting, frowns.

“He said he was heading to the Academy. That at the evening banquet welcoming Her Highness Stephania, he definitely wanted to show Her Highness Stephania something.”

“…I see. Since my treatment finished earlier than scheduled, tell him to return to the Royal Castle early to properly welcome Princess Stephania too.”

“Yes.”

They can’t tell him to return immediately because that would make Zadias suspicious.

…Something he wants to show Princess Stephania, huh. Unless he sensed danger and used it as an excuse to slip away… Is he planning to show some research results?

Considering his character – it might be his plan to show off something that demonstrates his martial prowess at the banquet as a return for my martial demonstration. It would also serve as a show of force to the nobles invited to the banquet.

In any case, events have been set in motion.

The enemy forces consist of Zadias and Chancellor Volheim. Then the Black Knights group. We’re assuming various possibilities including products of magical research and cooperating demons… well then.

+++

# **268 – In the Audience Chamber**

The design of the audience chamber in Silvatoria’s Royal Castle is said to be well-suited for protecting the assembled dignitaries.

Opening the large door at the front reveals a space as expansive as a dance hall. Directly opposite the entrance, a tiered structure rises, upon which sit the thrones of the King of Silvatoria and the Queen’s seat.

To the left and right of the hall are seats for the feudal lords and the robed nobility to occupy when attending audiences.

This is the designated location to receive Zadias. The reason lies in the ability to deploy powerful magical barrier walls around the frontal throne area and the noble seats on either side during an emergency.

The plan is to summon Zadias to the audience chamber, announce King Eberhart’s recovery there for the first time, and have the King formally receive the envoy from Verdgar anew. As it is an official occasion, the close aides chosen by King Eberhart himself will also attend to serve as witnesses.

We, too, will face him in the same unprotected area as Zadias.

“Theo, that…!”

“…What is it?”

Called by Grace, I looked out the castle window towards the direction of the Sages’ Academy… and saw something like a flying sailing ship approaching. A vessel flying Silvatoria’s national flag. That’s… something I haven’t even seen in BFO.

“…What is that?”

When I asked, King Eberhart frowned.

“A ship that flies through the air. It’s a project the Sages’ Academy began development on quite some time ago. I hadn’t been informed it was completed… They probably intend to announce it on this occasion, I suppose.”

…An airship. So this is part of the source of Zadias’s confidence.

Frankly speaking, in terms of aerial combat capabilities, Verdgar stands head and shoulders above other nations.

This is excluding my Aerial Combat Gear, of course… The reason lies in the existence of the Labyrinth. It provides a relatively stable supply of monster meat from Orcs and the like, enabling them to maintain forces like the Wyvern Corps.

Therefore, other nations inevitably have smaller Wyvern numbers compared to Verdgar.

From that perspective, considering the airship—a vessel capable of transporting numerous personnel, weapons, and supplies—it certainly has the potential to be a powerful weapon.

In BFO, it would probably be classified as one of Silvatoria’s secret weapons, right…? The fact that they’ve brought it out at this timing might mean word of the Aerial Combat Gear unveiled at the spring dinner party has reached them.

Anyway, for Zadias, this is tantamount to declaring he has no enemies left within the country, and it also serves to showcase Verdgar’s military assets.

“Excuse me,” I said, using Light Magic to create a telescopic lens and magnify the distant airship.

“Hoh.”

King Eberhart let out an impressed sound. Everyone peered curiously from behind me.

I observed the hull. The keel section seemed to be made of metal. From what I could see, the strength seemed adequate. It’s clearly built with full military deployment in mind.

On the deck were the Black Knights. At the helm stood Zadias, and beside him waited a magician clad in a robe. Unhealthily pale skin, sunken cheeks. A man with gray hair who looked nervous.

“This magician?”

“That would be Chancellor Volheim. He likely intends to come to the castle to report its completion as well.”

That answer was somewhat expected… Coming to the Royal Castle alongside Zadias, huh? Since it’s the airship’s unveiling, it’s only natural for the person in charge to attend.

“Since it’s an unveiling, they probably haven’t loaded any weapons onto the ship, right?”

Princess Adriana remarked. Indeed… I don’t see anything like a ballista.

“No… Please look here.”

Along the side of the hull, blue spherical objects were embedded in a row.

“These are?”

“We should probably consider them some kind of weapon. Look. There are also small windows near the spheres. I suspect it’s a mechanism to aim and fire magical projectiles from here.”

Considering their placement compared to Earth-side sailing ships, I think these are likely items serving an artillery-like purpose.

So, unable to obtain the magical technology possessed by the Ancient Bloodline, they were developing new weapons. While the extent of their power is unclear, if these are weapons involving magic tools, they probably operate using the marksman’s magical power or magic stones as a power source. That said, I don’t think they’d be that powerful…

“Well, isn’t that rather crude? The fact that they’re arriving on that thing means… the Black Knights are accompanying them. If they’re even carrying weapons… it’s not a situation that can be resolved simply by His Highness behaving himself.”

One of the close aides spoke in a flustered voice. King Eberhart placed a hand on his chin in thought, then asked me.

“Let me be direct. What do you think of that?”

“As a weapon… it’s probably excellent. However, if I were told to fight it here and now, I wouldn’t consider it much of a threat. Weapons of that magic tool type rely on magic stones for power, so their performance has inherent limitations.”

“Preposterous—! You’re… essentially saying you could take on a warship single-handedly.”

“Unless it can’t be shot down with magic around the 8th tier… then I might consider it a threat…”

“Wha—”

My words left the aide speechless, while King Eberhart gave a wry smile. Princess Stephania remained perfectly composed, and Sheila nodded as if it were only natural.

“…I suppose so. Judging by the magical power you exhibited when performing Circulating Ki… you could probably do even more than that?”

“Yes.”

When I nodded back, the aide’s expression twitched. Even so… for King Eberhart, Zadias is his own flesh and blood.

He frowned and made a pained face, but as if shaking off his hesitation, King Eberhart declared.

“Good. The plan remains unchanged. We will summon Zadias to the audience chamber and proceed as arranged. If the information from Verdgar is true, missing this chance would only lead to further tyranny. If Zadias and Volheim lead the production of more such ships under their direction, their foothold would become unshakable.”

Right. By revealing his hand, Zadias must be confident in his advantage. Dissenting feudal lords would likely be coerced into submission by force.
