For King Eberhart, such actions would be unacceptable given the current situation with the Demon’s suspicious movements. Moreover, with incidents like Beriondora’s and information suggesting Zadias’s connection to the Demon emerging.

“…I was unable to strongly condemn his mistakes. It’s natural to fear that my mutation might eventually befall him as well. But such a thing cannot serve as any excuse. Therefore, as King, I must verify the truth. If it is fact, Zadias’s actions are unforgivable, and I too will have no choice but to oppose him later.”

“Father…”

Princess Adriana called out to him with concern. King Eberhart smiled a lonely, wry smile.

“And if we are to confirm it, there is no other opportunity but now.”

For King Eberhart, this moment is the watershed—to make a decision or remain seated as he is.

That’s why we must verify the truth of the information we brought by observing Zadias’s reaction. Even if he understands logically, emotions are another matter.

I… cannot share King Eberhart’s concern for Zadias’s inner feelings like he does. Even if told that Zadias acted out of fear of mutation, it doesn’t sit right with me. If the reason truly was the fear of it happening to himself, he shouldn’t have tried to use research as a pretext.

Fundamentally, Elliot’s kidnapping and brainwashing, what he did to Marquis Zilbolt, what he attempted in Verdgar—not a single one of these can serve as an excuse. King Eberhart is right.

But I don’t intend to voice that now. King Eberhart also needs time to sort his emotions and make his decision. Everything will be confirmed from here on out.

The airship came to a stop, positioning its stern towards the castle. This suggests two things. Firstly, it increases the likelihood that those spheres are indeed weapons classified as projectile arms.

Since it’s an unveiling, they probably intend to explain the ship’s performance to some extent. In that case, parking with projectile weapons aimed at the castle, even if to display military might, would be rather clumsy.

The second point is… that Zadias hasn’t noticed the trap. If he had sensed it, he would likely have kept the weapons aimed at the castle while parked, given that no explanation has been provided yet.

As we waited in the antechamber leading to the audience chamber, Zadias, Volheim, and the Black Knights entered. Zadias and Volheim were unarmed, but the Black Knights, serving as the Crown Prince’s escort, appeared to be wearing swords.

“Ah, Your Highness Stephania, a pleasure to see you looking so well.”

Zadias offered a greeting with a composed smile.

“And to you, Your Highness Zadias.”

Princess Stephania responded with an elegant bow.

“My visit to His Majesty proceeded smoothly, so I am now to present greetings from my father in the audience chamber.”

“We were also asked by the Prime Minister to attend the envoy’s greeting session before the dinner. Thus, I have come here with the Chancellor of the Academy.”

“I see.”

Yes. So that’s why Zadias and his party will take their places in the seats on the left side of the audience chamber. The arrangement is for the Prime Minister, acting on behalf of the bedridden King, to receive the greetings and accept the official letter in the audience chamber. At least, that’s what Zadias has been told.

“How did the treatment go?”

“His Majesty expressed his gratitude to me. His condition… was beyond my expectations.”

Without mentioning specific results, Princess Stephania spoke quietly.

How he took that, Zadias showed a formally solemn expression and nodded.

“There’s nothing to be done. We too are at a loss and somewhat bewildered ourselves. Shall we change the subject? Did you see the ship outside?”

“Yes. Just now, from the castle window. As expected of the magical powerhouse Silvatoria is, you create amazing things.”

“Of course.”

Perhaps satisfied with Princess Stephania’s reply, Zadias smiled.

“If Your Highness is willing, I can take you aboard the ship later. The view of Silvatoria from the sky is exceptional.”

“That sounds lovely. If the opportunity arises—”

Just then, a trumpet sounded from deep within the audience chamber. The signal that the Prime Minister had arrived.

“Then, later.”

“Until then.”

Zadias crossed the antechamber and entered the left-side seats.

In harmony with the grandly played trumpet, the large front doors slowly opened. As the envoy, I followed a step behind Princess Stephania as we proceeded into the audience chamber.

On the left: Zadias, the Chancellor, and the Black Knights. On the right: the King’s close aides.

A soldier loudly recited words praising Silvatoria and King Eberhart, and the trumpet sounded once more. As that figure appeared from the passageway at the rear of the audience chamber, Zadias’s eyes widened and he let out a small, stunned voice.

“Wha…t?”

What Zadias saw there was—the robust, healthy figure of King Eberhart.

+++

# **269 – Crimson Black Crystal**

The envoy party bowed to King Eberhart according to proper etiquette.

“Well done. You have traveled far, Princess Stephania.”

King Eberhart spoke these words with a magnanimous gesture before seating himself on the throne.

As for Zadias… he seemed at a loss for words. After hesitating about what to say, he apparently decided to remain silent, perhaps remembering that this was the occasion for greetings between King Eberhart and the envoys. Volheim’s eyes were wide with surprise.

“I have come as the representative of my father, Melvin. Your Majesty Eberhart, I offer my sincere congratulations on your recovery. My father will surely rejoice when he hears the news.”

“Hmm… I must express my gratitude to you all once more. I hereby swear to repay the friendship and trust between our nations. And… while I was confined to my sickbed, I caused you all considerable trouble as well.”

King Eberhart looked around the audience chamber as he spoke, and his aides bowed in the manner of subordinates. A beat later, Zadias and the others followed suit.

“From now on, I must show myself before the people to reassure them. I must also devote more effort to governance that has been lacking. But first… Princess Stephania, I understand you bear a personal letter from the King of Verdugal.”

“Yes. Here it is.”

Princess Stephania respectfully produced the letter.

A civil official among the aides received the letter and handed it to King Eberhart. Zadias, who had been told nothing about any letter, leaned forward, wondering what was happening.

The content was the same as what had been delivered after the treatment. This was merely its formal presentation in an official setting.

King Eberhart read the letter thoroughly before nodding.

“…I have been fully informed of the details regarding the ruffian who ran amok in Termwills. We shall take appropriate measures on our end as well.”

King Eberhart nodded.

“Regarding that perpetrator, we have prepared a facial sketch and a plaster statue.”

Princess Stephania presented a wooden box containing the plaster statue. The civil official took out the statue and handed it to King Eberhart.

“Hmm. So this is the individual.”

Holding the plaster statue in one hand, King Eberhart furrowed his brow. He was making sure the face of the statue was easily visible to those assembled in the audience chamber. I could tell Zadias gasped. I knew from the start he was involved. So… what I should be watching here is Volheim’s reaction. Volheim’s eyes were also wide open, his gaze fixed on the plaster statue as a severe expression surfaced. This reaction… should be taken as that of an accomplice. In any case, because of what happened to Mother, I have no intention of letting him escape.

“It seems this individual boarded a ship from Silvatoria bound for Termwills with the aim of assassinating key figures. He is also said to be involved in an attempted assassination of a retainer of a noble house. We must proceed with arranging for his capture based on the facial sketch and plaster statue within our country and gather eyewitness reports. See to it immediately.”

“Yes, Your Majesty!”

The plaster statue was passed from King Eberhart to the civil official.

“Regarding this individual, there are eyewitness accounts suggesting he used miasma. If he is indeed a demon, this is an extremely grave matter.”

Hearing the word “demon,” the aides stirred.

“Who… Who is behind this…?”

I could even hear Zadias’s soft murmur. In his mind, he must be pondering who could have drawn this picture.

Was it Marquis Zilbolt or Benedict who betrayed him? If so, how were those two able to betray him? When were their restraints removed?

Or was it Princess Stephania before his eyes, or King Melvin behind her, who perceived it? If that’s the case, then why was he summoned here?

This is probably along the lines of what he’s thinking.

In any case, this leaves Zadias with no option to wait. If the manhunt progresses and information is gathered, sooner or later an eyewitness might appear.

More fundamentally, even without corroboration, if Marquis Zilbolt and Elliot are cooperating with King Eberhart, then most of Zadias’s schemes have been exposed. Therefore, if he simply goes with the flow, he won’t be granted any freedom of action in the future. No matter what excuse he uses, King Eberhart will place him under surveillance and detain him.

King Eberhart sent a brief glance toward Zadias as if to confirm his state, then lowered his eyes with a regretful expression. After a short pause, he raised his head. His expression no longer held any hesitation.

“Actually, I had already received an unofficial report. Regarding the attempted assassination of the noble house’s retainer, it is said to involve not a noble of the Verdugal Kingdom, but a noble of our own country. That individual is currently staying in Vinesdora. I have summoned him here as a witness. Marquis, step forward.”

Zadias’s eyes widened as he scanned the audience chamber. The witness—Marquis Zilbolt—entered boldly from the front. When he approached near us, Marquis Zilbolt knelt before King Eberhart.

“Fu, haha… hahaha!”

At that point, Zadias finally burst out laughing. The aides’ gazes gathered on Zadias, and King Eberhart spoke as if to reprimand him.

“Is something amusing?”

“Amusing? It’s more that… if I remain silent like this, unwarranted suspicion might fall upon me.”

It wasn’t resignation. Zadias spread his arms and stepped out from the left-hand seats into the audience chamber. The escort Black Knights and the Academy Headmaster followed, taking positions behind him.

…They still maintain some distance from us. We face each other across the great hall.

“Let me speak frankly, without fear of misunderstanding. I am acquainted with that perpetrator. However, I was introduced to him as an acquaintance of Marquis Zilbolt. Of course, I never dreamed he was dangerous, let alone that he might be a demon.”

Zadias brazenly declared such things.

He must have been taken by surprise, but he likely feels he holds the advantage. Conversely, if he were to obediently comply, he would only be at a disadvantage, and with the airship right there, now is the only time for Zadias’s side to act.

The reason he’s making such a defense… is because King Eberhart’s aides are present here. It’s the principle that logic and salves can be applied anywhere; before resorting to force, he probably intends to assert his own legitimacy.

If push comes to shove, he can pin the reason for their acquaintance on Marquis Zilbolt and make him shoulder all the blame. He can suppress any rebuttal backed by force. Even if it sounds absurd, he just needs to create a reason.

As for eyewitness accounts, since he was introduced by Marquis Zilbolt, it would be natural.

Truly… he refuses to know when he’s beaten.

“Then I must hear the details from both parties. Zadias and his attendants, as well as Marquis Zilbolt, shall remain at the Royal Castle.”

“Surely… Father, you don’t suspect me? I have devoted myself body and soul to the development of our country until now.”

Zadias spoke with gestures.

“It is true that our efforts fell just short in treating Your Majesty’s illness. However, we have achievements in other fields. Father, have you seen the ship outside? For the advancement of Silvatoria, we even created such a thing. To hear those words on this celebratory occasion where we intended to present it… is it not too much?”

“For the country… you say? Then summon Baron Silun and his brother, Lord Elliot.”

At King Eberhart’s words, two figures emerged from the depths of the audience chamber. The moment Zadias saw them, an expression of astonishment surfaced on his face.

The figures of Elliot wearing a mask and Ashley with her hair color restored. If Zadias, who knows Elliot’s true face, sees them, he will realize they are blood relatives.

Elliot removed his mask and knelt. There was no Gem on his forehead. At the sight of their appearances, a stir arose among the aides. In this case—the burn scars usually glimpsed through the gaps in the mask would prove that Elliot and Benedict are not different people. The burn scars Zadias had nominally used would come back to haunt him.

“This is the head of the Silun baronial house of Verdugal, Lady Ashley Rodias Silun. And the man we called Benedict is none other than her brother, Elliot Rodias Silun.”

“I merely took in a pitiful man who had lost his memory. A baronial house? Have you not simply brought a girl with a similar appearance?”

“Is that so? Then I shall demand an explanation for this as well.”

Saying this, King Eberhart took something out from his breast. It was—a Gem embedded in a stone slab.

“A Caex Gem… I believe it is called. This Gem—no, this magical creature—shall be examined by the Court Magicians and cross-referenced with documents. You said it was for the country? If you were pursuing talent that leaked from the Academy League, why was no report of the discovery made to me? And why was such a magical creature embedded in Lord Elliot’s forehead?”

Zadias remained expressionless and silent. Part of it was likely that he couldn’t gauge how much King Eberhart knew and thus had no way to respond.

“There are still more witnesses. The High Spirit who governs Mt. Tephra, which spreads across Marquis Zilbolt’s domain.”

At his words, Tephra also emerged from the back into the audience chamber. When she removed her hood, her flaming hair was revealed.

“It seems the demon… the Corrosion Princess Alvelinde used Curse Magic on the retainers of the Zilbolt marquis house and the Spirit Tephra, threatening them into obedience. If you claim the Marquis and the demon were cooperating, then why did his close associates and the spirit governing the volcano have to be taken hostage? Answer me.”

Questioned, Zadias closed his eyes.

“…If you have no answer, I cannot grant you freedom of action until everything is brought to light. Have the Black Knights discard their weapons and comply with my instructions.”

“…Hah.”

Zadias twisted the corner of his mouth.

“What is amusing?”

“I thought that even though you were corroded by miasma and your remaining life was short, you still had value as long as you could continue the ritual.”

“Let me be clear… you underestimate the demons. Each time the ritual was performed, each time I caught a glimpse of its nature, its terror beyond human comprehension literally seeped into my bones. But… what have you seen until now? What have you learned?”

“To say such a thing… One need only overcome such things and make them one’s own nourishment. Like this.”

Zadias spat out the words and raised his right hand. The Gems adorning the chests of the Black Knights’ armor shone, and something resembling miasma began to rise.

“Zadias… you…!”

“I believe I told you we were seeking means to overcome them. We have made the demons’ miasma our own. That’s not all. Starting with the Flight Technique, we have successfully formulated many of the techniques they use. Allow me to show you our research results—how we can slip through barriers and wield the secret arts of the demons.”

…So this is the reason for Zadias’s composure. The flying ship, soldiers who have obtained the demons’ Flight Technique. They might even be able to use Miasma Bullets and weaponized miasma.

“It is regrettable that it has come to this. You have grown old. You cannot even discern your own circumstances. I pity those present here as well… but this is a result you brought upon yourself.”

At his words, the Black Knights drew their swords. Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana rushed to protect King Eberhart.

—That should be enough.

This is also the reason I let him underestimate Princess Stephania’s combat strength. To bring him into an undeniable situation, obvious to all.

“Your Majesty Eberhart.”

“Yes?”

“Since fate has brought me here on this occasion, I request your sanction to strike down those who would dare raise their swords against Your Majesty.”

“…Handle it as you see fit. …My apologies. That is beyond our capabilities to handle.”

I received King Eberhart’s words. I had Grace hand me Ouroboros, and I passed her the axe she had been levitating disguised as luggage. Grace, who had been standing quietly with her eyes closed without saying a word until now, opened her eyelids—the color of her eyes was already red.

Barrier Walls deployed across the front and sides of the audience chamber. Simultaneously, blessings from Marlene and Claudia enveloped us.

Not yet—I won’t advance. The signal to begin will be after the aides have evacuated. King Eberhart and Princess Adriana… will be protected within this audience chamber by the double barrier of the Barrier Walls and Princess Stephania’s Defense Field.

As I raised Ouroboros and heightened my magical power, Volheim, noticing this, spoke.

“Could it be… Magical Power Circulation? I see, so you were the one who cured the King’s illness!”

“…You said you came from Verdugal, didn’t you? You… could it be, are you Patricia’s son?”

Zadias laughed cheerfully and spoke to me.

“Now, of all times… What will you do by asking that?”

“To raise your staff against me, who should rightfully be your master. Even now, I could forget that discourtesy and take you into my service in Patricia’s place?”

I’ve humored this farce until now to create a stage to strike him down, but… I’ve had enough of this guy.

“Shut up already. You are unpleasant.”

I bared my fangs in a smile toward Zadias. Instead of the suppressed emotions, excess magical power scattered as Spark Light around my body. Zadias’s eyes widened for a moment, but the next instant, he too laughed.

“Kuku. Is that your answer? Then I shall ask you the same question again after cutting off your limbs.”

In Zadias and Volheim’s hands were crimson-black crystals. The miasma rising from Zadias’s crystal enveloped his entire body, and his form began to change before our eyes. The crystal in Volheim’s hand—lengthened and transformed into something like a Khakkhara.

“Zadias, I’m releasing that from the ship.”

“Do it. Volheim.”

Along with his words, a great vibration assaulted the castle.

“Theodore-sama…! A giant Golem from the ship…!”

“Yeah, I see it.”

I nodded at Ashley’s voice. I could see two giant metal Golems—one black and one white—flying out from the airship.

Ignis, who had been waiting, crashed into the white one. I had positioned Caduceus, Lavigne, and Ignis outside to prevent escape from the audience chamber… but Caduceus and Lavigne would have a hard time holding them off due to compatibility issues.

The black Golem ignored Ignis, smashed through pillars, shattered walls, and came flying into the audience chamber. But it seems Zadias and the others have no intention of fleeing either.

That makes sense. Even if they retreated, they don’t control the Knight Order. They would simply be pursued for high treason. If Zadias doesn’t win here, his plans will come to nothing.

“…Grace. Can I leave the black one to you?”

“Then I shall entrust the white one to Lady Marie.”

Without any show of effort, Grace stepped forward, holding an axe in each hand.

“…Understood. I’ll take Zadias and Volheim. Everyone, please handle the Black Knights.”

“Yes, Theodore-sama.”

Ashley deployed a Defense Field with her back to the throne, constructing a defensive position. The Dullahan summoned by Marlene made its appearance.

“I have a debt to settle for this wound with the Black Knight Captain. That one is mine.”

Elliot took a step forward. A man among the Black Knights, clad in armor with particularly intricate decorations, raised his longsword in response as if answering the challenge. Flames erupted from its hilt.

Behind him stood Zadias… transformed into a half-human, half-dragon being. He bore some resemblance to King Eberhart’s mutated form, but was far more sinister—a dragon-man with red and black coloration.

So the crystal was a magic tool for Demonification. Their so-called breakthrough wasn’t about removing miasma, but controlling it.

In that case, perhaps the Caex Gem’s purpose wasn’t merely for domination, but to enhance one’s own power after undergoing Demonification.

I wondered about the difference between this transformation and Volheim’s… Was it due to the Silvatoria royal family’s constitution or traits? Or was Zadias’s crystal specially made?

But well, I could verify the answers later. This seemed far more refined than that Half-Demon from before. If they’ve chosen Demonification, then I’ll crush them without holding back.

+++

# **270 – Turmoil in the Magical Kingdom**

“Benedict… you bastard. Have you forgotten the debt you owe for being taken in by His Highness?”

One of the Black Knights spat venomously as Elliot stepped forward, but the Black Knight captain silenced him with a gesture.

“Captain Ragnar…”

“He seems to have business with me. You all follow His Highness’s will.”

“Yes, sir!”

Elliot and Ragnar faced each other from a distance. Ragnar narrowed his eyes and smiled.

“I won’t speak of debts.”

“I didn’t think you would prioritize personal grudges.”

“It’s nothing of the sort. In the end, I simply stick with His Highness because I enjoy fighting. Though my subordinates admire me, the Vice-Commander is better at commanding group battles. And besides… I thought it would be interesting to see how much you’ve grown since then.”

Ragnar twisted the corner of his mouth happily as he said this and took a stance with his blazing longsword.

“I see…”

In response, Elliot… directed his cold gaze and ice rapier toward Ragnar. Then—from the side, a tsunami of frigid air came rushing in.

As if it were a signal. They stepped in from both sides simultaneously. Both kicked off the ground and closed the distance. In midair, ice and fire swords clashed, producing a sound like evaporation.

The audience chamber was covered in ice. While continuing their deadlock in the air, Ragnar laughed.

“This wide-range cooling magic is your sister’s! And you can fight in midair too? You’re full of surprises!”

“You’re a flame magic user. This magic shouldn’t affect you much.”

“That’s right. Entertain me, Benedict!”

“That is not my name!”

“Ah, that’s true!”

“Freeze…!”

A large Magic Circle shone in Ashley’s upraised hand. The Magic Circle converged into a pure white sphere of cold air, which she slammed into the ground. From that single point, the entire audience chamber began freezing over. Ice covered the floor, and from it, ice pillars shot up everywhere, piercing through to the ceiling. 7th Class Water Magic: Icicle Palace. A base defense magic that seals a wide area with ice. It was a spell with long duration that continuously transformed the effective range into a world of extreme cold.

“An ice practitioner! Quite skilled!”

“We can break the barrier with our miasma technique if we’re not interrupted! First, scatter the nuisances and crush that silver-haired girl maintaining the Defense Field!”

The Black Knights had identified King Eberhart and Princess Adriana as their targets. That was the command given by their master, Zadias.

King Eberhart had to be killed, and Zadias had to declare his succession to the throne. How to handle Princess Adriana and Princess Stephania wasn’t yet certain… at best, they would be confined or taken hostage, otherwise they would likely be killed as well.

But to achieve these objectives, they had to destroy the barrier spread throughout the audience chamber. To destroy the barrier, they ultimately had to eliminate the practitioner constructing the Defense Field who stood in their way.

So in the end, this was—the form of combat they excelled at.

The Black Knights formed ranks and simultaneously fired miasma bullets at Ashley in the heart of their defensive position. However—ice walls and ice pillars formed, blocking most of the miasma bullets.

“A blessing! The miasma bullets weaken at longer distances!”

“Deal with it using normal magic!”

Even if they changed their attack methods, the attenuation from the Defense Field still occurred. Ashley and the others in the defensive position effortlessly blocked the projectiles.

In return, lightning strikes, ice shotguns, light bows and arrows, sound bullets, and more came raining back at them.

Exchanging arrows at long range was ultimately just a warm-up. Neither side took damage thanks to the miasma shields, but—Ashley’s Icicle Palace remained active. Meanwhile, the temperature in the audience chamber continued to drop. Their breath turned white.

“So their aim is to freeze us with delayed combat…!”

“But wouldn’t they suffer in low temperatures too?”

“I doubt they’re unprepared.”

That Black Knight’s intuition was correct. With Tephra’s blessing active, the Icicle Palace that should affect both sides worked exclusively to the Black Knights’ disadvantage.

Then perhaps they could break through the defensive position with golems—but when they scanned the area, a chilling scene came into view.

—A woman fighting evenly with a giant golem, and the figure of a massive knight.

Frankly speaking, those fighting the golems were monsters. If caught in the crossfire, they would be crushed along with their armor regardless of whose attack it was. They could only be seen as exceptionally unfavorable opponents for the Black Knights. Since they were perfectly contained, there was nothing to be done, but the same went for the other side.

“…We’ll have to charge in, accepting the casualties. If we charge with miasma at full power, we can suppress the Defense Field’s effects to some extent.”

“Four of you charge in. The rest follow from slightly behind and provide covering fire. We’ll draw the enemy rearguard’s barrage! Charge in and crush them!”

“Yes, sir!”

Seeing that long-range attacks were getting them nowhere, just as the Black Knights advanced, Sheila and Dullahan emerged from the defensive position as if in response. But if they left the defensive position, that was exactly what the Black Knights wanted. The Black Knights fired miasma bullets while Sheila and Dullahan weaved through the gaps in the barrage. Both sides charged at ferocious speeds.

“Step aside, you beast-woman!”

A lightning-wrapped sword swung downward. Sheila leaped diagonally upward as if to avoid it.

The Black Knights tracked her with their eyes, trying to predict her trajectory to slam miasma bullets into her.

But with a right-angle turn that was natural for Sheila but seemed like mockery to the Black Knights, she crossed right before their eyes. The miasma bullets fired by three of them pierced uselessly through empty space.

As they reacted to Sheila’s movement and tried to follow her with their eyes—sticky threads showered down upon them. She wasn’t even looking in their direction. She fired them from diagonally behind with precise trajectories.

“Guh!?”

The Black Knight whose vision was obscured struggled to remove the threads stuck to his face, but they weren’t something that could be dealt with so easily. His left hand that touched them also got stuck, making the situation uncontrollable.

“Dodge it!”

“That’s impossible.”

Another man shouted to his comrade, but with his vision blocked and his left hand immobilized, there was no way he could react to Sheila and Dullahan’s movements. Covering fire risked friendly fire. Sheila’s matter-of-fact voice echoed, and the next moment, the hind leg of Dullahan’s steed kicked the Black Knight in the back of the head, sending him tumbling down. Even protected by his helmet, it couldn’t block the impact entirely.

“One down.”

“Don’t mock us!”

Enraged at the sight of their comrade falling with his eyes rolled back, they fired miasma bullets, but they couldn’t get a clear aim on Sheila who moved away in irregular patterns. Using ice pillars as shields, she would circle behind them and then fly out in completely different directions.

“What kind of movement is that!?”

“Verdgar’s Flight Technique!”

“Don’t force your aim! Roughly is fine! Fire across an area!”

“Do you think we’ll let you?”

As the rearguard tried to perform suppression fire with miasma bullets on Sheila, Irmhild’s light arrow grazed through their midst. When Seraphina’s Cursed Melody Amplification spread a high, clear sound, the Flight Technique was disrupted, causing the Black Knights to nearly fall for a moment.

Though they quickly recovered, the vanguard’s situation had already shifted by then. Saucers came flying in rapid succession—two, then three. They blocked with swords and deflected with shields, but then Sheila, who had vanished, circled around from the side and kicked a helmet flying.

“Guh!”

Perhaps because the Black Knights understood that Sheila would target gaps in their armor, they kept their sides closed and halted in midair, trying not to show openings. The logic was probably that they only needed to be wary of the threads. Swords wrapped in Fighting Spirit could be blocked with Fighting Spirit, allowing them to turn it into a contest of Sword Arts. Besides, Sheila couldn’t maintain the same movements forever. Her Vitality was limited, and using magic tools consumed Magical Power.

But—the kicked Black Knight had stopped moving. Dullahan’s massive sword approached without a sound and mercilessly swept through. Perhaps because it was enhanced by miasma, it didn’t bisect him, but it hit with enough force to crush him along with his armor, sending him flying.

He seemed to barely maintain consciousness, but of course he couldn’t avoid the mass of sound fired from Seraphina’s horn either. The Resonance Bullet shook his skull right through his helmet. It destroyed his eardrums. It disturbed his vestibular system and reaped his consciousness.

“Did you think you were safe just because you’re protected by armor?”

“That makes two.”

“You bastaaaaaard!”

Ignoring Sheila and Dullahan, one of them desperately squeezed out all his miasma, wrapped it around his body, and forcibly charged into the defensive position. The remaining vanguard was frantically trying to track the movements of the Saucers dancing around, Sheila’s circular trajectories, and Dullahan’s location, leaving no room for counterattacks.

But the Black Knight who charged into the defensive position—that was as far as he got.

“Too bad. Farewell.”

Claudia’s Teleportation Magic activated from the side. He was transported to the first basement hall of the labyrinth where the fully-equipped Verdgar Knight Order was waiting. One Black Knight against the Verdgar Knight Order who had experience fighting Half-Demons. The difference in combat power was insurmountable.

“What was that just now!”

The watching Black Knights raised bewildered voices. One of their comrades had vanished from the spot.

Annihilation? Teleportation? At any rate, it meant that even solo forced breakthroughs weren’t permitted. The moment the last vanguard was distracted by his comrade’s disappearance, sticky threads were pasted to his back, and through the threads, Marlene’s Lightning Strike reaped his consciousness, sending him falling down.

Then Sheila and the others turned toward the rearguard. They raised their swords to meet them, but they didn’t come straight on. They scattered left and right.

Before they knew it—the number of opponents had increased. Sheila, Irmhild, Dullahan. Countless Saucers dancing everywhere. The ice statues created by Ashley and Lavigne were covered by illusions created by Marlene. They traced circular dances as if to surround the remaining Black Knights.

“Th-this can’t be…! What are these people…?”

“Why… are we so helpless…?”

Meanwhile, the temperature continued to drop. It was no longer just cold—but had transformed into pain, an extremely low-temperature hell. Even the sensation of gripping their swords was being stolen away. The sounds they heard became jumbled, distant and near… Even knowing they were illusions, they could no longer distinguish between real and fake. The Black Knights could only gaze at the scene before them, shuddering at their own situation.

“Let’s go.”

As if taking Ashley’s area magic as a signal, Grace charged into the black golem. Her opponent had a massive frame surpassing Ignis. Precisely because of that, Grace’s movements were several times faster.

Moving at arrow-like speed that left no shadow, Grace easily slipped into its guard. Using her momentum as she passed by, she slammed her axe into an unarmored part.

“This is—”

A sensation unlike anything she’d felt before. It sank in only as much as the force of her strike, then the golem’s body itself pushed Grace’s axe back with absurd elasticity.

She was knocked backward. There, the black golem’s straight punch roared as it approached. Grace met it head-on. When she struck it aside by slamming her axe from the side, the golem’s arm bent like a giant tree flexing. But that was only momentary. It just flexed, then returned to its original shape with added momentum.

The problem wasn’t the armor it wore, but what lay beneath. The black golem’s body itself possessed extraordinary elasticity, making it impervious to both slash attacks and strikes. That was its characteristic. The armor on its arms, legs, and body wasn’t for defense, but for offense. They were nothing more than blunt instruments to tear apart and crush opponents.

It flexed its arm to build momentum, then unleashed attacks as if the flexing giant tree had become a whip.

She intercepted with her Fighting Spirit-wrapped axe. Undaunted by the ridiculous difference in size, she knocked aside each of the golem’s blows, slipped through, and delivered Fighting Spirit-infused slash attacks. But even those didn’t work.

“…I see. The Magic Kingdom’s golems have quite unusual abilities.”

Grace frowned slightly, looking somewhat displeased.

Meanwhile, the white golem—was putting on quite a show against Ignis and Rosemary.

It didn’t possess the extreme elasticity of the black golem. But attacks didn’t penetrate. Even when they hit, there was no response.

Ignis’s War Hammer roared as it struck through the white golem’s flank. But then a pale blue wave of light ran across its entire body—soon that light gathered in its fist and was fired as a magic bullet.

The various magics Rosemary fired to support Ignis yielded similar results. The moment they touched the white golem’s armor, they were absorbed as if sucked in, replaced by waves of light running across the armor surface, then converted into counterattacking light bullets.

“Absorbing magic and impact—. Converting it into magical power and transforming it into attacks… I see. Quite efficient.”

Rosemary maintained some distance from the white golem, evading the magic bullets while observing the golems.

Both were probably created with the assumption of suppressing the Silvatoria Knight Order and magicians. Using overwhelming defensive capabilities as a shield, they would trample and annihilate with mass. Making them impervious to both magic and strikes.

With Theodore as an exception—it would be difficult for anyone but Grace or Ignis to properly face them.

The white golem and black golem. Should they switch opponents? No, they should each continue as they are.

Just as Rosemary finished that calculation, the white golem that had broken through Ignis attempted a body slam. Leaping back, she extended a magic thread to Ignis. Pulled by the connected Ignis, she changed trajectory and escaped danger.

The white golem crashed into the wall. It converted that impact into magical power. It fired a magic bullet aimed at Ignis. Ignis shattered the magic bullet head-on with his War Hammer.

The clash between Ignis and the white golem. Merely crossing weapons was equivalent to letting the white golem prepare its next shot. The magic bullets fired incessantly at Rosemary. It lowered the power of each shot and fired them from its fingertips. Deflecting them all was difficult. Ignis moved into the line of fire to become his master’s shield, shooting them down with his hammer and fists.

But those were forced movements. While Ignis’s movements were restricted, the white golem’s fist caught him.

The power wasn’t that great. Because it was converting its own strikes. But magic bullets from point-blank range were different. A direct hit. Ignis was forced to step back. There was nothing wrong with Ignis himself, but… she had no intention of testing how durable the Doll was.

Rosemary frowned with displeasure. Using Puppet Strings was probably inadvisable too. Because the moment they touched, they would excessively drain her magical power.

The Black Golem charging toward Grace—crouched deeply as if gathering momentum, then launched itself forward using elastic force like a bouncing ball. Even when Grace deflected it with her axe, it flew straight toward her like a rebounding sphere. It spun its body, tearing through the air with its armor. It didn’t matter if she dodged. Just as it shattered one of Ashley’s ice pillars, Grace released her axe. The chain wrapped in fighting spirit coiled around the Black Golem’s body, and when Grace pulled, their movements reached a stalemate.

“Don’t think you can hold back Luvanche and Spaela alone forever! I’ll crush you all soon and offer those clever little girls as blood sacrifices!”

Zadias roared as he assessed the battle situation.

“Hmph…”

Rosemary scoffed at his words.

Indeed. Zadias’ judgment that the situation was favorable based on the Golem’s fighting style—was correct in one sense.

Grace facing the Black Golem… even with regenerative abilities, couldn’t match a pureblood vampire. So even one direct hit would tip the scales heavily in the Golem’s favor.

What about the White Golem and Ignis? In terms of strength and armor… basic comparisons would favor Ignis. However, Rosemary, who appeared to be its master, was a mere human. The only question was how to break through Ignis and attack Rosemary waiting behind it.

But. Even so, the expression beneath Rosemary’s feathered fan remained unchanged.

“—What a nuisance. Isn’t that right, Grace?”

“Absolutely. Opponents that can’t be dealt with using an axe… I despise them.”

While handling the Black Golem’s chain attacks resembling a storm with just one axe wrapped in fighting spirit—Grace also showed a faint smile. Her crimson glowing eyes and fangs peeking from the corners of her mouth.

“But their power source… appears to be perfectly ordinary magical power.”

“They’re not even living beings to begin with. What does it matter?”

Saying this, Grace and Rosemary briefly exchanged glances and laughed.

The chain entangled with the Black Golem. And the magic threads connected to Ignis. Changes occurred in each.

The chain absorbed magical power, while the magic threads supplied it.

With incomparable explosive speed, Ignis stepped forward. It hooked its claws into the armor and lifted the White Golem’s massive body using the momentum.

“That’s right—. If they’re not living beings. If it’s not blood, it doesn’t matter—but even so, I truly despise it.”

Right nearby. While continuously parrying the Black Golem’s attacks, Grace spoke. Contrary to her words, she felt a violent impulse welling up inside herself. Her lips formed a ferocious, splitting smile.

Through the chain wrapped in fighting spirit. A pale light was drawn from the Black Golem toward Grace’s hand.

Energy Drain. Stealing the magical power that served as the Golem’s energy source, absorbing and assimilating it as Grace’s own magical power—. One of the vampire’s fundamental abilities. Enhanced by her Moonlit Dress, she could use it anytime.

The reason she normally didn’t show this ability… was simply because she hated it. And because she had no need to use it. That was all there was to it.

Seeing this, Rosemary laughed.

“Conversion creates significant losses and is inefficient. Even my enhancements to Ignis are like that. Now—. I wonder how much power this Golem can withstand?”

While still holding the White Golem overhead. Without any warning, destructive power was unleashed. Rosemary’s Pile Bunker, charged with all her magical power, was fired at maximum output.

A deafening roar and explosive wind. The pile shot out with tremendous force slammed into the White Golem’s abdomen.

Absorption—couldn’t keep up. Piercing through the magical conversion armor, boring a hole through the Golem’s main body and spreading cracks. The explosive wind magic released inside further widened the cracks. As the Pile Bunker was withdrawn, Ignis’s War Hammer coming from the side caught the Golem.

A distinctly different, dull sound compared to before. Cracks spread rapidly from the pierced hole—and the White Golem shattered in two from the torso.

“Fufu, ahaha! Aha-ha-ha—!”

Meanwhile, the fate of the Black Golem that had its magical power drained was equally miserable. The elasticity it maintained by consuming magical power was lost, and whether it extended its right hand or left hand, Grace’s axe—accompanied by roaring laughter—chopped them to pieces, scattering fragments.

Pulling her other axe back to hand and stepping forward. A jump. The axe wrapped in fighting spirit left behind black lightning-like afterimages as it cleaved the Black Golem from head to waist in a bamboo-splitter motion.

It didn’t end. Grace didn’t stop there.

Her feelings toward Theodore and Lisa. Her emotions toward Zadias and the Black Knights. The self-loathing from being forced to use Energy Drain. All these fueled Grace’s destructive impulses.

Almost simultaneously, she grabbed the shattered arm of the White Golem dancing through the air and, using centrifugal force, hurled it outside the audience chamber.

Where it landed—was the airship. The crew remaining aboard had moored it alongside the audience chamber, ready to retreat or fire at a moment’s notice.

They didn’t even have time to fire. The White Golem smashed through the airship’s side and crashed inside. Following that, beams of light from the White Golem’s still barely functioning arms pierced through the airship from within.

Whether that—caused any fatal damage to the airship. As if sinking to the ocean floor. The airship began descending—at a slow pace—toward the castle’s courtyard.

——The gleam of ice and the afterglow of flames intertwined and clashed. Neither yielding, they struck sword against sword. The disadvantage of mass due to using a rapier was compensated for with enveloping ice.

Ice spears and fireballs fired at close range while swords clashed. Evaporated ice turned to mist, and from the mist, ice shotgun pellets were fired, which Ragnar extinguished by enveloping himself in flame armor. Their respective specialty techniques interfered with each other, preventing either from becoming decisive.

Ragnar blocked Elliot’s slash attacks with a Miasma Wall. As he flowed with the attack to reposition himself and showed a stance to strike, Elliot fired water blades toward his back.

“Tch!”

Intercepted with a Flame Sword. But unlike ice, water blades couldn’t be completely blocked. They caught Ragnar’s helmet.

Speaking of Elliot, using Ashley’s created ice pillars as footholds, he flew sideways before creating distance and turning back around.

Ragnar tore off his helmet. Fighting Elliot with the helmet’s visor would limit his vision. That’s why his reaction to the water blades was delayed.

“Is this payback?”

Ragnar bared his teeth, pointed at his own face with his thumb, and looked toward Elliot.

The wound Elliot inflicted on Ragnar was aimed at roughly the same location—though not exactly—as the burn scar on Elliot’s face. It had slipped through the helmet’s gap, leaving a cut on his cheek.

“I merely thought I could take your right eye through the helmet’s gap. If I couldn’t finish you, it’s meaningless.”

“Kuku! I like you! Not finishing me off was the right choice!”

Ragnar laughed, then stepped forward with a longsword in his right hand and a flame whip in his left. Elliot enveloped his entire body in ice armor to counter the whip’s irregular trajectory.

In aerial combat, the advantage likely lay with the more experienced Ragnar. However, Ashley had erected numerous ice pillars as obstacles, preventing him from utilizing his mobility effectively.

In contrast, Elliot’s movements were reflexive—repeating minute jumps while controlling Levitation from shield to shield. Since he moved while killing inertia, obstacles didn’t bother him much.

As a result, the advantage-disadvantage gap wasn’t that significant, and they fought while rapidly changing locations—in the air, on the ground—neither particular about their battlefield.

Crossing swords as they passed each other, clashing Miasma Shields against ice shields. Forcefully kicking each other away, striking when off-balance. Bouncing away to disengage. Turning around for slashes and thrusts. Flames and ice blades grazing cheeks. The flame whip approaching from unexpected directions, while Elliot’s widely dispersed ice thorns entangled it. Their magics interfered with each other, exploding into steam.

“This won’t get us anywhere!”

The extreme temperature difference between heat and cold. Shattering ice blocks. Scattering sparks. Swords growling as they sought to take each other’s heads. Parrying, clashing, pounding each other with magic at close range.

When both were repelled, Ragnar deployed a Magic Circle. A giant sphere of fire swelled above his head. In response, Elliot also deployed a Magic Circle.

Ragnar’s magic completed a moment faster. He unleashed the great fireball forward. Elliot’s ice blocks, fired slightly later, collided head-on.

A momentary stalemate, then one side prevailed. Ragnar’s magic won due to its momentum. Shattering the ice and scattering explosive winds in the fireball’s path. The blast flames and ice shotgun pellets swallowed Elliot as he crossed his arms to defend.

Ragnar charged through the explosion. Swinging his blazing longsword as if to behead Elliot.

A hard impact. When he completed the swing, an ice helmet went flying through the air.

“Wrong—!?”

What remained was just a shell. Only the ice armor Elliot had been wearing. Elliot had shed the armor from the back and escaped, now charging from Ragnar’s left side with wind-like speed. The rapier carried not ice, but fighting spirit—!

“Tch!”

Thrusting his left palm toward the incoming rapier, he created a Miasma Barrier. Elliot’s rapier, wrapped in blessing and fighting spirit, pierced through the barrier and skewered Ragnar’s left palm.

As if he’d anticipated this, Ragnar clenched his already-impaled left hand and raised the sword in his right. If Elliot dodged, he’d follow up with a Miasma Slash. At this distance. With his weapon trapped and in his flesh body, Elliot had no way to avoid it—!

“Got you!”

But Elliot stepped forward instead. Taking the base of Ragnar’s descending blade—with his shoulder—killing the slash’s force, stopping the blade with bone. Completely disregarding everything, he released his rapier and grabbed the wounded palm with his bare right hand.

“Rotten Blood!”

“Gah!?”

From the wound on his left hand. An indescribable numbness and something like terror spread throughout his body. An intense interference that allowed no resistance. He couldn’t even swing his longsword, let alone hold it properly.

“A reverse healing—spell…? Kuku, for a technique used by a magic knight known for purity, that’s pretty filthy…”

“It’s a spell formula my sister taught me. I won’t permit mockery.”

A massive block of ice formed around Elliot’s clenched right fist. He’d released his rapier when using Rotten Blood. Indeed—against armored opponents, this was more reasonable than slashes or thrusts. Especially since his opponent was poisoned—.

The ice fist was unleashed. Smashing through Ragnar’s chest, the shattered ice fragments striking his face along with the impact. That was all—Ragnar’s consciousness faded to black as he plummeted downward.

+++

# **271 – Obsession and Guidance**

“…Go! Bring Eberhart before me. Kill anyone who resists! But Stephania and that magician brat are my prey! Don’t lay a hand on them!”

Perhaps his hearing had improved through demonification. Zadias seemed to have heard my voice, as he irritably gave orders to the Black Knights.

“Yes, sir!”

Following Zadias’s command, the Black Knights headed toward the defensive positions. As instructed, they appeared to be ignoring me as I approached Zadias.

The two Golems were Grace and Rosemary. The Black Knights were Ashley and the others. And Elliot was dealing with the Black Knight commander.

I had recalled Caduceus to the throne room to standby as reinforcements. Zadias… wasn’t leaving any guards behind, it seemed.

I took some distance and faced the two. The crystals Zadias had been holding appeared to have all been absorbed by him. His solar plexus glowed with a reddish-black light. Was that the core?

Miasma extended long from Zadias’s right hand, forming into a sword. So he could weaponize miasma too.

Converting magical power to miasma… switching between positive and negative, then manipulating the spell formula to transform… that much was fine. Would he revert if the core was destroyed? Or was he like demons, unable to stop unless killed?

When I fully crouched down, Volheim frowned.

“He’s going to charge. Magic from magical power circulation can’t gain range.”

“…He’s just a moldy relic of the past after all. He appears lightly armored. One solid hit should end the fight.”

So he knew about the properties of magical power circulation. But that was irrelevant. If he thought he could fight from a distance or capture me alive… he could try.

Activating Mirage Body—I stepped forward with full force.

Foot level. Directly ahead. Eye level. Moving along the shortest path toward Zadias with three trajectories alongside two illusions.

“What?!”

“This is—”

Simultaneously controlling Levitation and Air Blast mid-air. Accelerating further in the air. I plunged into his guard in one motion.

Zadias swung down with a Bamboo Splitter from above. He sliced through the eye-level and direct-ahead illusions, but I had already stepped inside the sword’s trajectory. I scooped up the groaning Ouroboros from below. The tip of the rebounding staff smashed into Zadias’s chin.

Just before impact, he leaped backward on his own. His reaction speed was decent.

“Oh…”

Glancing around, I saw Volheim’s eyes wide open. As if regaining his senses after a moment’s delay, he tried to create distance. I pursued. As he deployed a miasma barrier wall, I slammed Ouroboros into it. The magical power enveloping Ouroboros clashed with Volheim’s miasma, scattering sparks.

“Tch!”

Zadias, having regained his posture, rebounded and charged from behind.

“Nemea!”

I deployed a thin Shield on my back. Reading the attack type and angle. Without even turning around, Nemea filled with circulated magical power intercepted Zadias’s miasma sword with her claws. While forcefully pushing back Volheim in front, I controlled Nemea to intercept Zadias behind me. Spark Light flashed, and the sound of clashing blades echoed.

“Th-this guy…?!”

Beyond the miasma barrier wall, Volheim’s Magic Circle deployed.

To crush it at the outset. While pinning him with Ouroboros, I struck with a palm strike imbued with magical shock.

“Gah?!”

The Magic Circle scattered, and Volheim was sent flying backward. Using Nemea’s claws that had blocked the miasma sword, I diverted the force as if parrying, causing Zadias’s body to flounder. Maintaining the momentum, I shifted form and slammed Ouroboros into his flank.

“Guu?!”

It was more than enough power to rupture internal organs in a human, yet he seemed relatively unfazed. Perhaps because he was in dragon form, his surface durability might approach Zevion’s.

Capella’s hind legs shot out in front of me, kicking Zadias in the chest before closing the distance with her back still turned to Volheim.

“You bastard!”

Zadias closed in as if chasing. I knocked down the incoming miasma bullets with Ouroboros. Nemea leaped as if pouncing on Volheim approaching from behind, swinging down her claws. Volheim blocked it with his khakkhara. The fact he could withstand Nemea’s strength suggested Enhancement through miasma. While his appearance hadn’t changed much, his interior clearly had.

Blocking the descending miasma sword with Ouroboros, I unleashed a kick with a compact motion meant only for contact. That was sufficient as an attack origin. The moment my sole touched his abdomen, I struck with magical shock, shifted form, and disengaged. I knew from Capella’s signal that he’d deployed a Magic Circle behind me. The instant I leaped sideways, a Fireball pierced where I’d been, catching Zadias. Ignoring Zadias caught in the blast, I immediately reversed direction and leaped at Volheim.

Perhaps affected by the shock strike through the miasma barrier wall, Volheim met me with his khakkhara. Did he have Staff Martial Arts training? Ouroboros and the khakkhara clashed, and he tried to entangle and lift it. I deployed a Shield to block the khakkhara’s upward rebound direction. Kicked up at the astonished Volheim’s chin.

“Gwaaah?!”

Zadias charged from behind through the blast. Using Volheim’s reclining body as a stepping stone, I leaped upward as if running up.

“Wh…?!”

Zadias swung his sword, but I wasn’t there. I had already taken position above both of them.

One, two, three. Simultaneously deploying Magic Circles. Sixth-Tier Earth Magic Solid Hammer multiple activation.

“Smash!”

Chunks of rock poured down toward the two at ferocious speed. The first shot hit Volheim directly, who hadn’t recovered his posture from where I’d run up. Though he blocked with his khakkhara, he crashed down toward the floor.

Second shot. Zadias roared and slashed down the rock chunk head-on. Third shot. This time it caught Volheim stuck to the floor. He seemed to try blocking with his khakkhara again, but it shattered along with the khakkhara.

The split second shot still lived on as a Technique.

“O—oooooh?!”

The rock chunk split into two pieces hit the weaponless Volheim directly. Enough power to crush him to pieces.

“Vo-Volheim…!”

As the dust cleared—Volheim didn’t get up again. His eyes were rolled back—was this because his demonification was shallow? Miasma rose from the shattered khakkhara and Volheim’s own body.

So the miasma was draining. He’d revert even if the crystal broke. Seems he had some countermeasures prepared. Ignoring the stunned Zadias, I landed, applied a Sealing Technique, solidified it with Earth Magic, and rolled him aside.

Rotten as he was, he was still the Sages’ Academy director. He probably had High-Tier Magic in reserve… but I couldn’t let him use it here. I had to crush him as a priority.

“You… bastard…”

Zadias’s voice trembled.

“I’ll give you a warning. If you expel the crystals from your body now, release the transformation, and surrender, I’ll guarantee your life.”

I could have restored Volheim by knocking him out with Solid Hammer. But what about Zadias? Judging from the durability I’d glimpsed during our warm-up, any stronger magic would become an issue of excessive force before even considering holding back.

I wouldn’t feel any pain over whatever happened to him, but I did want him to spill information.

“If holding back halfway just gives you a chance to counterattack, I’ll finish you off properly, whether you’re the Crown Prince or not. With Volheim here, I have enough mouths to talk.”

“That’s my line! I thought about capturing you alive, but that’s over now! I’ll behead you and show Stephania!”

“Funny joke. You can’t even see the battle situation.”

One by one, Black Knights fell. Zadias finally noticed and looked around at the situation, but upon seeing the Golems, he shook his head.

“Don’t think you can hold off Levanche and Spaera alone forever! I’ll crush you soon and offer those clever little girls as a blood sacrifice!”

…Is that so.

Without answering, I floated up to Zadias’s eye level.

“There are techniques I can’t use with subordinates nearby…! I’ll show you—show you that! That you—brats like you—can’t possibly be Verdgar’s Demon Slayer! Such nonsense can’t be real!”

He screamed as if convincing himself. As he crouched and concentrated power, his solar plexus flickered reddish-black. Responding, miasma rose from his entire body.

“Goaaaaaaaah!”

A roar. While scattering lightning widely from his entire body, he charged with ferocious momentum. I deployed a Shield diagonally, deflecting Zadias’s trajectory as if firing him backward.

“Useless.”

Deploying a Magic Circle. Lightning Magic Fifth-Tier Lightning Veil. I also wrapped myself in lightning and confronted him. I stood ready to receive close combat unchanged. Catching the uncontrolled lightning strikes, I placed them under my control and mastered them.

Blocking the sword of Zadias, who circled and charged, with Ouroboros. Deflecting and countering with Ouroboros. Blocking, blocking. Both his strength and reaction speed had increased from before. But so what?

The miasma sword wrapped in lightning grazed right past my face. Flowing, parrying, I struck with a shock strike through the Shield. Showing no reaction, Zadias pushed forward.

But it wasn’t nearly enough. Strength, durability, reaction speed—none of it mattered.

Killing intent. Technique. Tactics. Everything was lacking.

Entangling the sword, I used his own strength to flip him upward. Smashed Ouroboros into his wide-open face. The opposite end. Flipped up and cracked his jaw.

Refining magical power while activating Mirage Body. The deception of clones. Using movement and trajectory to confuse, then wielding the staff, his fast reaction speed worked against him as he was sucked into the attacks.

Zadias’s face was battered left and right. Mixing strong and weak attacks, further blending shock strikes among them, accumulating damage internally while ignoring his surface durability.

Beaten down repeatedly by Ouroboros, Zadias was sent flying backward. Coughing, he wiped blood trickling from the corner of his mouth.

“Such nonsense…! Why can’t I lay a hand on a mere human?! One strike… one strike should be enough…!”

That’s when it happened. An explosive sound and the noise of something hard shattering echoed. The white and black Golems were almost simultaneously crushed.

Grace grabbed the white Golem’s upper half and, using centrifugal force, slammed it into the airship at cannonball-like speed.

Shattering the airship, a brilliant light exploded inside. The airship slowly sank. Elliot had defeated the Black Knight commander… Ashley and the others had completely wiped out the Black Knights. The last Black Knight fell, frozen in ice.

“You—bastard! You bastard, you bastard!”

Enraged by the sight, Zadias rose up with miasma and came at me.

Another fierce clash. Even now, he hadn’t given up. While crossing blades, miasma converged in his mouth. A scene I’d seen with BFO too. It reminded me of a dragon’s breath.

If so, he’d probably release the accumulated miasma from his mouth. That wouldn’t be a miasma bullet, but rather what should be called a miasma cannon in terms of power.

But—something felt off. That gaze. That killing intent. For a Technique meant to decide the match—.

He took my strike directly in his flank without even avoiding it. The next moment, Zadias opened his mouth wide, showing a stance as if to unleash miasma like a dragon’s breath.

I deployed a Magic Circle. But then Zadias turned completely in the wrong direction. Where his gaze landed—was King Eberhart.

A crimson, massive destruction ray illuminated the throne room, piercing through and shattering the Royal Castle.

“Ha—hahahahah!”

Ignoring me, he probably thought it’d be fine if he pierced through the barrier walls and defensive positions to take King Eberhart’s life. Or perhaps—he calculated that this would shake me.

“Hihahaha! Hahahaha—ha…?”

Zadias’s foolish, roaring laughter stopped. Once the crimson flash was fully released, his vision would recover. Where his gaze fell, only blue sky stretched out.

Short-range Teleportation Magic Compact Leap. While maintaining contact, changing direction and teleporting. In short, I made him waste his shot into the sky.

He couldn’t land such a big move on me. So if he aimed it at someone else, he thought I’d either protect the target or he could achieve his objective… that’s what Zadias had calculated.

Unable to comprehend, Zadias froze. An enormous opening. Point-blank range close enough to spark. Controlling the excess magical power enveloping my body, I took a palm strike stance at my hip.

“You’re done.”

Coordinating the movement of all my joints with the palm strike release. Gathering the circulating magical power running in a spiral pattern to a single point. Releasing a magical shockwave aimed at his solar plexus.

One of the bare-handed Combat Skills. A fusion of Spiral Palm Break, Gardinis’s shock strike method, and external magical power manipulation techniques.

Destructive power unimaginable from such a small motion was born. A visible magical shockwave pierced through from Zadias’s back side. A thin shockwave bundled like thread. Only shock propagation. It didn’t make a hole. Zadias, clutching his solar plexus, writhed in agony.

Fragments of red crystal spilled from between his fingers. Meanwhile—on my withdrawn hand, unused, excess magical power remained.

…Leftover, huh? I’d intended to use it all in one strike, but my control is still immature. Needs practice.

But—could I fire about one more worth of magic immediately?

“Ga, gu, gaaah…”

Miasma leaked from all over Zadias’s body.

When I deployed a Magic Circle, Zadias stretched his trembling hand forward as if to stop me.

“Finishing blow… I’m already… surrender—”

“Can’t trust you. Until the miasma fully drains—you can’t release the transformation, and you can still manipulate miasma, right?”

Saying that, I activated magic. Simultaneously with activation, I flew using Nemea and Capella’s strength.

Sixth-Tier Wind Magic Vortex Drive.

“Gah?!”

Wrapped in a barrier wall of gale force, I held Ouroboros like a spear and thrust into Zadias’s abdomen.

Ouroboros’s voice of delight. Zadias’s scream. Accelerating further.

Left and right, ignoring inertia, making sharp turns, breaking through walls while holding Zadias, piercing through ice pillars, gouging the floor, ascending together to near the ceiling.

“Get crushed.”

Drawing an arc, falling straight down. Smashing through the floor, slamming him into the lower level. Crunching sounds as he embedded into the floor, where I canceled the magic.

Zadias lay with limbs splayed, eyes rolled back, tongue out, twitching and convulsing. Like King Eberhart’s transformation, he seemed to be gradually reverting to human from the extremities, but—

Well… since he had durability on par with Zevion during transformation, he should barely be alive even like this. Though all four limbs were bent in strange directions, I mustn’t forget to apply a Magic Seal.

+++

# **272 – Liberation of the Academy Alliance**

“Theodore-sama!”

After dragging Zadias to the audience chamber, everyone rushed over. First, we needed to assess the current situation and ensure everyone’s safety.

“Is everyone injured?”

“I’m fine.”

“I’m alright too. Ignis is also unharmed.”

Grace and Rosemary, who had dealt with the Golem, reported no issues.

“Sheila?”

“Yeah, no problems. Irmhild and Seraphina are also unhurt.”

“Those of us in the rearguard aren’t injured either.”

As Ashley said this, Marlene nodded repeatedly.

“However, Brother Elliot sustained a minor shoulder injury. But he used Healing Magic on himself… and says it’s nothing serious.”

“Elliot-san, are you okay?”

“Yes, there’s no need to worry about me.”

Elliot smiled while lightly touching his torn shoulder area.

Though it feels strange for me to say this, he truly embodied the principle of “letting the enemy cut your flesh while you break their bones” at the end. Even knowing he couldn’t cut through the core, taking the blow with his bone must have been incredibly painful. Well, it seems only a faint scar remains. His skill with Healing Magic appears quite proficient.

Anyway, it seems our companions are fine. Next is securing the area. I went around applying Magic Seals to the fallen Black Knights. As usual, I packaged them up by binding them with Light Bind and hardening them with Earth Magic. I checked the headcount to ensure no one had escaped in the confusion. After I finished packaging them, Elliot used Clear Blood on the Black Knights’ leader—Ragnar, who was still breathing.

“I too… had my life spared by Ragnar once before. With this, I’ve repaid that debt.”

Elliot said. Well… I suppose this settles Elliot’s personal grudge.

The crashed Airship… is surrounded by soldiers. The crew seems to have surrendered quietly. Given that there’s no commotion, it appears no Black Knights remain there either.

Meanwhile, I checked the Communication Device. A report came from Mercedes of the Verdgar Knight Order, confirming they had successfully captured the dispatched Black Knights. I should properly inform them that we’ve defeated Zadias as well.

“For now, there seems to be no cause for concern. Are you injured?”

“Hmm. Nothing serious. …I ended up burdening you with dealing with my own family’s failures. My apologies, Theodore-dono. I thank you.”

After glancing at the still-unconscious Zadias, King Eberhart spoke.

“Not at all. He was someone I had my own deep history with.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana also bowed quietly and expressed their gratitude.

“Thank you. We’re unharmed as well.”

“I thank you, Theodore-sama. But… this is the power of an ancient Battle Mage… It’s even more fearsome than I’d heard.”

Princess Adriana said this while surveying the audience chamber.

Now that the battle was over and I looked around, I realized I might have been a bit too flashy. Well, I was quite furious with Zadias.

“I’ll take responsibility and repair the destroyed areas with Magic Construction.”

“I appreciate the offer… but I believe the traces of destruction should remain as a warning, kept visible to the public for as long as possible.”

“Is that so? However, there’s also the risk of collapse. At least let me reinforce the structurally weakened areas.”

When I responded, King Eberhart smiled wryly and nodded. Seraphina smiled, realizing work had come her way.

“Hmm. But with this, the matter is settled, I suppose. This should also clear Marquis Zilbolt’s tarnished name.”

When Tephra said this while gazing around the audience chamber, Marquis Zilbolt gave a wry smile.

“I hope it turns out that way. But what about the remnants?”

“I believe we’ve captured the main members of the Black Knights. The remaining cleanup should be handled by the Sages’ Academy.”

Elliot checked the faces of the Black Knights.

“Indeed. With Zadias and Volheim’s schemes exposed and both defeated, no one should dare to openly resist. I won’t allow any further confusion. Regarding Marquis Zilbolt’s honor, I shall declare his integrity before the nobles myself.”

In response to King Eberhart’s words, Marquis Zilbolt responded with a subordinate’s bow. Just then, his aides returned.

“Your Majesty! Are you injured?!”

“As you can see. Zadias’s right to the throne is hereby revoked, effective immediately, and he is disinherited. Mobilize the Knight Order and offer surrender terms for the cleanup of the Sages’ Academy. Thoroughly re-examine all personnel relationships within and outside the castle, and arrest all accomplices without exception.”

“Yes, sir!”

King Eberhart issued orders to the aides who had rushed over.

The biggest problem has been eliminated… but Silvatoria seems likely to become quite busy. The issue with the Sages’ Academy elders also remains.

“I should head to the Sages’ Academy as well. Since I can use Miasma, there’s no guarantee someone won’t try to escape by air or destroy evidence. We need to ensure the elders’ safety.”

We know Marquis Zilbolt, as well as Elmer and his group, are innocent. So it was decided they would serve as escorts for King Eberhart, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana until the Sages’ Academy matter is resolved and the situation stabilizes. Elmer’s group has plenty of personnel, making it just right.

By the time we finished minimally reinforcing the Royal Castle’s damage, the Magic Knight Order and soldiers had been organized. Riding military horses with them toward the Sages’ Academy, Claudia spoke to me.

“May I have a moment?”

“Hmm? What is it?”

“In large cities like this, there are Moon Temples of considerable size, right? I think they can be treated like enclaves where my power reaches within each region.”

“Ah, similar to how ritual grounds are for Tephra?”

Indeed, it wouldn’t be wrong to say Claudia is the master of the Moon Temples.

“Yes. If I visit once and arrange things a bit, they can reliably serve as bases for teleportation. Unlike creating stone monuments, there’s no worry about being moved to the labyrinth side.”

I see… That’s convenient. I had been thinking Silvatoria might face various dangers due to its proximity to Beriondora, but with this, I should be able to rush over if anything happens.

“The issue would be the means of communication, I suppose.”

“What about having the shrine maidens offer prayers for salvation from demons when major incidents involving demons occur…?”

“Can you detect that?”

“Yes. No problem.”

…Hmm. So that would mean the goddess herself comes rushing when prayed to, I suppose.

Anyway, that would solve various problems. Even without detailed exchanges via Communication Device, it would suffice if they could communicate the most critical points. For emergency evacuations, they could just flee to the Moon Temple.

In that case, I should visit the Moon Temple later, and have King Eberhart issue a notification to the shrine maidens.

While we were talking, we arrived in front of the Sages’ Academy grounds. First, the king’s envoy stepped forward.

“W-what is this about!? We saw a flash of light from the Royal Castle earlier—what happened?!”

The gate guard asked the envoy with a somewhat confused expression.

“I come as a representative of His Majesty Eberhart. Zadias and Volheim have staged a rebellion and have been apprehended. All soldiers, knights, and magicians within the Sages’ Academy are to discard their weapons, surrender, and follow instructions. Defying the king’s command will be considered aiding high treason without room for excuse. Conversely, even those who sided with Zadias will receive reduced sentences if they surrender quietly.”

Upon hearing “high treason,” the gate guard’s face turned pale.

“U-understood.”

The guard placed his weapon on the spot.

“That helps. Now please assist by helping to explain the situation to everyone within the grounds as well.”

“Y-yes, sir!”

The guard stood rigidly at attention in response to the envoy’s words. We proceeded into the grounds with the Knight Order.

People who emerged from various facilities wondering what was happening also obediently followed the soldiers’ instructions upon hearing the envoy’s words.

Between Zadias and Volheim’s defeat, the severity of the high treason charge, and trust in King Eberhart’s character who promised reduced sentences, it was almost disappointingly straightforward.

And then—we reached the towering giant Tower. Black Knights appeared immediately. All of them are armed. Well, given they originally aimed to usurp the throne and likely witnessed the Miasma cannon’s flash in the sky from the Royal Castle where the Airship headed, it’s not surprising they’re on high alert.

“What in the world… is this about?”

“I come as a representative of His Majesty Eberhart.”

The envoy repeated the same words verbatim.

“His Highness staged a rebellion… and lost?”

The Black Knight’s eyes widened.

“It’s the truth. Respond only by whether you will discard all arms or not. Any other action—even consulting about whether to surrender—will be considered intent to rebel. Or else… will you fight the entire national army with those Miasma-emitting weapons? Choose of your own will.”

The envoy stated impassively. The Black Knights froze, unable to even exchange glances at his words. But… when one person discarded his weapon and removed his Armor, the others followed suit.

Having witnessed the Miasma cannon being fired before this situation probably plays a part in making them believe the story.

“Good. Are the elders safe?”

“Yes… They’re in the Tower’s basement.”

As the Black Knight answered with a bowed head, he was taken away by the soldiers. …With this, Zadias’s faction should be crushed. First, I need to restore the elders’ memories.

# **273 – In the Underground of the Tower**

The core of the Sages’ Academy was a massive stone tower.

Pushing open the door and stepping inside, the entrance hall came into view. Straight ahead was a staircase leading upward, while circular corridors extended to the left and right, following the outer perimeter.

Soldiers rushed up the stairs and dispersed along the left and right corridors. Given the tower’s immense size, if hostages had been taken and a siege situation had occurred, it would have become quite troublesome.

“By order of His Majesty Eberhart, to prioritize the safety of the elders, I have been instructed to guide you to the section where the elders are being held,” said the messenger from King Eberhart, turning to face us.

“You’ll guide us?”

“Yes. We’ve selected those familiar with the tower’s interior from among the surrendered individuals and extracted information from them. There should be few delays. While it may take some time to secure the entire tower…”

…I see.

“Understood. Once we locate the elders, I’d like to remain on guard duty in the basement until the tower is secured.”

“That would be helpful. Depending on the situation, healing might be necessary…”

Indeed. Since we’re the ones who treated King Eberhart, having us stay in the basement would be convenient as we could handle both escort and healing duties.

Just then, a messenger soldier came running up. The soldier whispered something to the messenger before hurriedly running off again.

“It seems we’ve obtained information about the path to the basement. Let me guide you,” the messenger said, then began walking ahead to lead the way. We followed behind.

After ascending the stairs and proceeding straight ahead, a large door came into view. Touching the sphere on the wall caused the door to open automatically in response to magical power. …This kind of mechanism really gives you the feeling of a major magic nation.

Stepping through the door—we found ourselves in a grand library built in the tower’s central section. Desks and chairs for research were placed in the center of the room, while bookshelves lined the inner walls of the cylindrical room. It was open to the upper floors, with balcony seating installed at what appeared to be the second and third floor levels. The structure seemed to be similar up to about the fifth floor.

“This is quite… intriguing,” Rosemary murmured while looking around the grand library. Given time and permission, Rosemary would probably want to scour through the books here.

The messenger looked around the grand library and said, “They mentioned there’s a door here that leads down to the basement…”

“Let’s search for it.”

Even though Zadias and his group had used this as their base, there would likely be people coming and going in the grand library. While Zadias apparently claimed to be protecting the elders whose memories were sealed, I doubt he would make security too lax. There should be a hidden door leading to the basement at least. Releasing Caduceus, I began carefully examining the library’s back areas for any suspicious spots… and soon discovered what appeared to be a hidden door seam in the wall behind one bookshelf.

“…Found it.”

“Already?”

The messenger’s eyes widened.

“Mathius is good at this sort of thing.”

“Well, that’s…”

Sheila’s words left me somewhat at a loss for a response.

Given my history of creating various things like underground passages and hidden doors, it’s hard to deny. Grace is smiling too since she knows I found Mother’s hidden room.

“…I think there might be some mechanism in this bookshelf.”

Regaining my composure, we all went to the bookshelf.

Pushing or pulling a specific book would be the classic approach, right? As we divided up tasks and began manipulating the books—pushing, pulling, tilting them—Marlene, standing on her toes, pushed a book that seemed to be the right one. There was a sound like a latch releasing, and the bookshelf opened inward. Beyond it was a staircase leading downward.

“Thank you.”

Marlene nodded at my words and showed an untroubled smile.

“Shall we go then?”

We descended the spiraling, winding staircase. …People who knew Mother are ahead. Just thinking that made me feel slightly unsettled.

At the bottom of the stairs was a sturdy iron door. …A dungeon cell, perhaps.

“I don’t sense… any magical power.”

Holding my hand near the keyhole to check for any magical presence. Compared to the building’s overall aesthetic, the iron door felt somewhat newer. It seems the door itself was added later. Probably to keep things out of sight, either Zadias or Volheim must have renovated the basement.

It’s irritating to think Zadias made this. I’d like to smash it open, but there might be traps, and if those traps were the kind that harm those imprisoned inside to protect secrets, it would be unbearable to watch. Though my emotions are somewhat agitated, I should proceed carefully here.

Sheila took out her Thieves Guild tools and began carefully examining the keyhole. I created a magical light to make her work area more visible.

“No traps. I’ll pick the lock.”

Sheila inserted a wire-like tool into the keyhole and began the unlocking process.

Is it really just for confinement? Well, if their memories are sealed, they probably can’t use any magic at all.

“It’s open.”

As Sheila stepped away, the door swung inward.

“Thank you, Sheila.”

“Mhm.”

“You’re quite skilled…”

The messenger, who had been watching, spoke in an impressed tone.

“We explore labyrinths in Termwills, you see.”

“Ah. So you’re accustomed to exploration.”

“That’s right.”

Stepping into the dungeon cell. …The atmosphere was much brighter and more spacious than the impression the word “dungeon” conveys. It was well-lit by magic tools.

There was a hall-like open space, with round tables, chairs, and even a water-creating magic tool—enough space to relax somewhat.

Rather than a dungeon, it would be more appropriate to call it a large-scale house arrest.

“If they’re here… it doesn’t look like they were treated harshly.”
