“That might be true. Their memories are only sealed, after all.”

Claudia sighed with some relief, while Ashley nodded with a bright smile.

Since they were made unable to remember, torture would be pointless, and considering their goal was to eventually restore memories and extract information, there shouldn’t be any reason for excessively rough treatment. By claiming they had taken care of them without violence until now, they probably had in mind the possibility of winning them over after their memories were restored.

King Eberhart also said he couldn’t speak with the elders due to circumstances, but Zadias might have claimed it was for therapeutic isolation or something similar.

“If they’d resorted to violence, even their excuses wouldn’t hold water.”

Finding a corridor at the end of the hall. Proceeding further, I saw wooden doors lined up.

…Probably the elders’ private rooms, I suppose. Starting with the nearest one, I knocked and called out to check if anyone was inside.

“Is anyone in there?”

“…Yes.”

A reply came. A woman’s voice. The sound of a lock being opened from inside was heard, and the private room’s door opened.

Was the iron door the only thing serving the confinement function?

The person who showed her face was a young woman. She didn’t have the aura of an elder… but since they’re of the Ancient Bloodline, she might be a family member of an elder.

“You’re not the usual woman, are you? Are you newly arrived?”

“…No, that’s not it. I’ll explain the situation, but first, could everyone here gather in the hall over there? Would that be alright?”

“Yes. Understood.”

“…Ah, before that, I’d like to ask about your circumstances a bit.”

I want to understand what they’ve been told and how they comprehend their own situation. I’d like to avoid a situation where distrust arises after gathering everyone.

“Is it something I can answer?”

“Just what you know, just what you can answer is fine. Do you know why you’re here?”

“Um. There was a failure in a magic experiment, they said. All of us lost our memories in the accident, and in Silvatoria, they’re searching for a way to restore our memories… They said they want to research treatment methods for that purpose.”

…I see.

“There was a locked door at the entrance—do you know anything about that?”

“Honestly, it doesn’t quite make sense to me… but they said we’re important people and there’s danger of being targeted… to prevent intruders from entering…”

As she said that, the woman’s expression clouded.

“Ah, no. We have absolutely no intention of causing harm. Whether you stay here or leave is entirely your choice.”

“…Yes, that’s right.”

After looking at our group, the woman nodded. Well, given our apparent age range, we don’t look particularly intimidating. They might be wondering what kind of group we are.

After asking a few more questions, it seemed that while under escort—or rather, surveillance—they were allowed to take walks within the Sages’ Academy grounds.

Well, you could say they were just deceiving people who had lost their memories, that they were only after the magic these people possessed… but this situation is infinitely better than being treated harshly.

But anyway, I understand the circumstances now. Let’s divide up tasks, call out to people in the rooms, and have them gather in the hall.

But that means… even if we brought the magician who was on Elliot’s ship, we couldn’t mix him in here. Is he imprisoned somewhere else?

“Here you are.”

Just then, the messenger soldier from earlier came running up, out of breath.

“What’s the matter?”

When the messenger asked, the messenger soldier saluted while catching his breath and answered.

“They’ve discovered a magician-like man on the upper floor who appears to be under Subjugation Magic.”

“…Probably someone related to the people here. Elliot, do you remember the face of the magician who was on the ship?”

“I think I’d recognize him if I saw him. We fought together against the Black Knights.”

I see… If he still had his memories because he escaped from the Academy, he could have fought the Black Knights, and by placing him under Subjugation Magic, they could force him to work for Zadias.

“…Please bring him here. Be sure to treat him with respect.”

“Understood.”

The messenger soldier turned on his heel and ran back up the spiral staircase.

Now then. Back to the task of guiding the Ancient Bloodline magicians. Though it’s just knocking on doors, calling out, and having them come to the hall. Everyone is relatively cooperative, so it doesn’t take much effort. They don’t even seem suspicious… probably because they’ve lost their memories and have been here all along.

“Is this everyone?”

“Yes, that should be all.”

Just as the guiding was completed, soldiers returned from above bringing a man wearing a robe. A pattern indicating Subjugation Magic was visible on his neck.

“Long time no see. Do you remember meeting on the ship?”

When Elliot spoke to him, the man’s eyes widened. It seems this is indeed the person in question.

“You… from that time. You’re alive?”

“Yes. I’m glad we’re both safe. We’ve come to free you.”

“I see…”

The man sighed as if looking up at the heavens.

“Please wait a bit longer for the Subjugation Magic to be removed.”

“…Ah. I’ve waited for years. A little more patience is nothing.”

When I spoke to him, the man narrowed his eyes and smiled.

Good… Now then, let’s begin. Turning to face the magicians with lost memories gathered in the hall, I took a deep breath before beginning.

“Please listen without being startled. Actually, I know the Spell Formula to restore memories. I’m going to restore everyone’s memories now.”

When I said this, a stir arose among them—they had been watching to see what would happen.

“Is that… really true?”

The woman who had first spoken asked.

“Yes. I understand it’s a sudden story and you must feel anxious… The reason I can use this magic might be better explained after your memories are restored. Of course, if you insist on an explanation first, I’ll answer to the best of my ability.”

When I said this, they looked at each other. Eventually, the woman from earlier stepped forward and said.

“…We know almost nothing about the outside world. So… we have no way of knowing what’s right and what’s wrong. If you say this is how it is, we have no choice but to believe you.”

…I suppose so.

They’ll obediently listen to what we say, but they must still feel anxious inside.

“But all of us have always wanted to regain our memories. So your story makes us both happy and anxious. If possible… could you start with me?”

Saying this, she stared intently at me.

“…Understood. Please sit in that chair and make yourself comfortable.”

After we looked at each other for a moment, I answered, and she nodded.

Holding my hand over her head as she sat with closed eyes, I took one deep breath and deployed the Magic Circle.

The magic that Mother and another magician protected to the end. As the Spell Formula took effect, another Magic Circle automatically appeared in front of the woman’s forehead.

Memory sealing through magic, and unlocking. When the Magic Circle I deployed shone particularly brightly, the woman’s Magic Circle showed behavior as if rotating and disassembling from the center. The other Magic Circle completely broke apart and disappeared. My Spell Formula completed almost simultaneously.

“…How is it?”

I asked. As everyone watched with bated breath—the woman slowly opened her eyes, looked up at my face, and showed an expression as if about to cry. Then she hugged me.

“Ah… I can tell from your eye color and features. You—you’re Patricia’s child, aren’t you?”

+++

# **274 – Magicians of the Ancient Bloodline**

Someone who knows about Mother…

I had thought there might be someone.

“…I think that’s probably right.”

“Probably?”

Still holding me, the person asks in a gentle voice.

“Mother went by the name Lisa.”

“I see… So she didn’t tell you about the old days.”

When I nod, she slowly pulls away. As she does, a hint of sadness briefly crosses her expression. It seems she sensed something foreboding in my words and Mother’s absence.

“I’m Valentina. I grew up with your mother like sisters. I was the younger one.”

Sisters… So that’s why she recognized me immediately despite my different hair color, since she was close with Mother. I take a deep breath and calm my heart.

“My name is Theodore. I had the opportunity to learn Mother’s spell formula and the other formula Her Highness Adriana had received from the academic alliance magician, so I came to return everyone’s memories. The issue you were concerned about has been resolved. The mastermind behind the incident has been defeated.”

“…I believe you. I’d like to hear more details, but everyone else is waiting too.”

Valentina stands up and addresses the Ancient Bloodline magicians whose memories haven’t returned yet.

“What this boy says is true. My memories have returned as well.”

Everyone’s gaze turns toward us, and one of them asks Valentina.

“About that mastermind you mentioned earlier?”

“You’ll understand once your memories return. I think explaining the circumstances now would only cause confusion.”

“…Understood.”

The man seemed satisfied with that.

“Then let’s proceed with restoring them in order.”

“In that case, I think it would be best to start with that person over there.”

Valentina indicates an elderly man with long white hair and a white beard. There are several people who carry the air of elders… and he’s one of them.

“Hmm. Me, is it?”

The old man rises with deliberate movements.

“Isn’t this person related to Theo? Their… eye colors are similar, you see.”

At Grace’s words, I look at the old man. …Indeed, they might be similar.

“That’s one reason too. He should also be familiar with the memory restoration magic.”

I see… If he entrusted the spell formulas to Mother and another magician, it makes sense that there would be someone who originally knew the complete form of the formula from the beginning.

If that’s the case, then by restoring his memories first, we can split up and restore everyone else’s memories from then on.

“I leave it in your hands.”

The old man, looking straight into my eyes, said quietly with a smile.

“Yes.”

I nod and proceed to use the Memory Release Formula as before. I deploy the Magic Circle and place my hand over his forehead. When the formula completes, the old man quietly opens his eyes.

“First… let me express my gratitude. My foggy head has cleared.”

Then he looks at my face and says.

“I see. Indeed, you resemble Patricia. Did you get your hair color from your father?”

“No. It’s actually the same color as Mother’s. I’ve just dyed it for disguise purposes… I’ll return it to normal once the situation stabilizes.”

“Is that so…”

After scrutinizing my face intently, the old man closes his eyes.

“You said your name was Theodore, didn’t you? I am Siegmund. Whether I have the right to call myself this or not, I suppose I would be your grandfather.”

“…Yes.”

…Grandfather. Even being told that, I can’t quite feel the reality of it.

“There’s one thing I wanted to ask. Why was Mother chosen to be the one sent out? Was it because she was the Sealing Shrine Maiden?”

When I ask this, Old Sigmund looks slightly surprised, but quickly regains his composure and answers.

“Well, we didn’t just send out the main candidates; we sent out several people. That one over there is one of them too.”

Old Sigmund points to the magician who had been under Subjugation Magic. The magician bows slightly at being mentioned.

Spreading them out would make it easier to escape, I suppose.

“As for Patricia, the reasons were the importance of her being the Sealing Shrine Maiden, her magical skills being sufficient to entrust with part of the technique, and trust that she wouldn’t betray us… But simply sealing memories wasn’t enough. The vice chancellor at the time was seeking someone of the Wilcloud family bloodline. He probably wanted to give symbolic meaning to the disclosure of technology through an engagement with the Wilcloud family.”

In other words, merely sealing memories was insufficient to protect her from Volheim. They needed to protect both the secret technique and the Sealing Shrine Maiden.

“Let me confirm something from our side as well. You said the mastermind had been defeated?”

“Yes. Both of the central figures involved in the academic alliance’s internal conflict.”

Since there are still those whose memories haven’t returned, I don’t mention Zadias or Volheim by name. But they should understand from that.

“…I see. We both likely have many things we want to say and ask, but let’s first complete what needs to be done.”

“Understood.”

The two of us split up and begin applying the memory release spell formulas.

“You have remarkably precise magic control for someone your age.”

“As expected of Lady Patricia’s son.”

As memories are restored, people offer words along with their self-introductions. Since there’s a line waiting, I can’t have long conversations with each person individually… but piecing together what I hear gradually, it seems the ones called elders are seven senior magicians.

The Ancient Bloodline is comprised of seven families, and the family heads have traditionally been called elders. Among them, my grandfather Old Sigmund’s family, the Wilclouds, apparently serve as the central figures among the seven families. And Valentina too is apparently someone from one of the elder families.

“May I have a moment?”

The king’s messenger approaches, looking somewhat apologetic.

“What is it?”

“His Majesty instructed us to assist you, but we haven’t been told the details. Does His Majesty know about this matter?”

“Yes. I received permission from His Majesty Eberhart and Her Highness Adriana.”

Both were present in the audience chamber, and it was the perfect opportunity to explain the situation. Both were quite surprised, but they also ended up requesting that I look after the elders.

“I see. Even though we can provide healing… I was somewhat wondering why you people were accompanying us… Now I understand. This matter… I will need to report to His Majesty…”

“Then could I ask you to handle that? I still have things to discuss here.”

“Understood. I have no intention of interfering with a family reunion either. Consider this part of the treatment process, and I’ll leave it in your hands here. I need to command the soldiers upstairs. I’ll leave a few soldiers here, so if anything comes up, please use them as messengers.”

“Yes.”

The messenger leaves the scene in my care and returns upstairs to command the soldiers. The magician who is Elliot’s acquaintance also went with the messenger, as he needed to have his Subjugation Magic removed.

After restoring everyone’s memories, we moved from the underground hall to the great library to continue our conversation. Once seated, Old Sigmund asks.

“Now that everyone’s memories have returned… first, could you tell us about Patricia?”

Old Sigmund, Valentina, and everyone else turn their attention toward me. Right. This is probably what they’re most concerned about too. It’s definitely not good news, but… I have to convey it properly.

I return a small smile to Grace and the others who are looking at me with concern, then begin speaking.

“This is what I know… Mother went to Termwills in the Kingdom of Verdugal and apparently worked as an adventurer there while delving into the Boundary Labyrinth.”

“The Boundary Labyrinth, huh… She was exceptionally talented in magic, but she sometimes had health issues. She probably thought that if she defeated monsters in the labyrinth and gained power, she could compensate for that.”

Probably… that’s right. I nod at Old Sigmund’s words and continue.

“She apparently attended Peresford Academy too. That’s where Mother met my father. Henry Verdim Gartner, a noble of Verdugal.”

“Count Gartner…”

“That would be the previous Count Gartner, I suppose?”

“Most likely.”

…I can’t avoid mentioning House Broderick either.

“There were apparently various complications regarding marriage talks between the previous Count and House Broderick… I haven’t heard the detailed story, but in the end, Father and Mother never married. So I’m considered the Count’s illegitimate child.”

When I say this, Old Sigmund frowns. …Well, this probably isn’t pleasant news for Old Sigmund either.

Perhaps noticing my gaze, Old Sigmund sighs.

“…I understand. Patricia was using a false name and didn’t reveal her identity. That’s my responsibility too. I can’t say much about that matter.”

I bow slightly at Old Sigmund’s words and continue.

“Mother fought a demon that attacked Verdugal six winters ago… She defeated it, but fell ill due to that battle—”

When I get that far, everyone makes pained expressions. I probably don’t need to say what comes next.

The Ancient Bloodline magicians. They’re all people who knew Mother… While I’m happy to have met them, thinking about what comes next also weighs on my heart. Because I absolutely have to convey this news.

“I see… We sent her out to protect her, and yet… in the end, we survived while Patricia never returned…”

Old Sigmund shakes his head.

For a while, silence dominates the room, but eventually Valentina speaks quietly.

“But… you came to us.”

Then Valentina looks straight at me.

“You, Patricia’s child and no one else, came to help us. That makes me happy. Patricia would surely…”

“…Yes, I think Mother would be pleased.”

That’s the kind of person Mother was. There’s no doubt about that. I answer with a small smile, and Valentina also smiles while wiping tears from her cheeks.

“Mother wasn’t disliked or driven out by those around her. If you say it was to protect her… then I’m glad I came here too.”

If these are people who would listen so seriously and think so carefully about Mother, then that makes me happy too.

“There’s just one thing I want to make clear. I remember the days I spent living with Mother as happy ones. Mother seemed happy too.”

“I see… So Patricia was happy.”

At my words, Old Sigmund smiles somewhat sadly.

“This place may not be that kind of place for you… but thank you for returning to us, my grandson.”

“…Yes. Grandfather.”

I take the hand he extends.

Grandfather, huh. It’s still a somewhat unfamiliar word. But this word too… will probably become more natural to say eventually.

+++

# **275 – The Sealed Shrine Maiden**

The Sages’ Academy apparently also serves as a living space for the magicians who belong to it. For the members of the seven families led by the elders, it’s practically like their own home, which is why Valentina brought us tea.

“Please tell me about my mother.”

“…Hmm.”

Old Sigmund nodded.

“Where should I begin? When speaking of Patricia, our own stories inevitably come up as well.”

When I nodded at his words, Old Sigmund continued after saying “Well then” as a preface.

“We are said to be the descendants of the seven sages who served the magic kingdom of Beriondora. Though the bloodline has thinned since Silvatoria was founded. Still, there’s no doubt that our ancestors were among the Seven Sages.”

So that’s why there are seven elders representing seven families. The group of magicians who sealed the demon lord in the Termwills Labyrinth might have been them too.

“But… when Beriondora later fell, the family heads died in the battle against the demons, and the inheritance of several precious magics was lost. The bloodlines remained, but there were problems with passing down the techniques.”

One of the elders spoke.

“…Like teleportation magic and magical power circulation?”

At my words, Old Sigmund gave a wry smile.

“Hmm. Theodore. You were in Verdugal, weren’t you? Given that you knew about the Sealing Shrine Maiden, you seem quite familiar with our internal affairs…”

“About the Sealing Shrine Maiden, His Majesty Eberhart said that when he learned of my origins. As for teleportation magic… a demon I defeated before said it was a lost magic.”

A magician who had been sipping tea choked on his words at that.

“Y-you defeated a demon?”

“Verdugal is currently engaged in covert combat with demon groups. It involves labyrinths and Beriondora.”

“Just what have you been doing…? I’d like to hear about that too, but it would derail the conversation. Let me first tell you about us. Regarding teleportation magic, while the family head who could use it lost their life, it wasn’t completely lost.”

“I see. So you secretly passed it down.”

And that was inherited by my mother? But wait…

“It’s slightly different to say we passed down teleportation magic. We found the research materials of the user and were trying to analyze and study them to restore the spell formula. We didn’t know if a user would appear due to the relationship between magical aptitude and learning difficulty… but the seven families promoted marriages among ourselves, trying to return to the ancient sages. We believed it would bear fruit eventually.”

“And my mother might have been able to become a user?”

“That’s right. And Patricia responded to that. But the user’s research materials were from before the spell formula was completed. Patricia was trying to improve and research the spell formula, thinking she could make the revived teleportation magic more efficient.”

So even after leaving Silvatoria, my mother continued her research. The Sages’ Academy wasn’t just aiming for the return of magical power circulation users, but also the revival of other techniques, I suppose.

“However… if teleportation magic were to fall into the hands of demons, you can easily imagine what would happen, can’t you? Therefore, while it could be a powerful weapon, we positioned spell formulas that must never fall into demon hands as secret arts, keeping them hidden while still passing them down.”

If teleportation magic fell into demon hands… barrier-type seals would become meaningless, indeed.

So that’s where their secretive nature comes from. They wouldn’t reveal secrets even to the crown prince. It wasn’t just paranoia that ambitious power-seekers might ally with demons, and so on.

Superhuman power and long lifespans. Being able to approach demons… would be attractive to those seeking domination or immortality.

“What about the Sealing Shrine Maiden?”

“This is a tradition that has continued since the time of Beriondora… but while the ritual procedures remain, their original meaning isn’t clear.”

“Perhaps due to battles with demons and disturbances like what Zadias caused in the past causing them to be lost…”

“It might also be because too much time has passed… but yes, that’s about right.”

Old Sigmund said this to me with a somewhat awkward expression.

Hmm. Verdugal had similar things happen in its past too. Claudia being bound to the labyrinth is one example, and a previous Verdugal king turning the mines into a labyrinth is another.

Claudia had a distant look in her eyes. She might have been remembering old times.

“Anyway, the most magically talented daughter from our seven families is chosen to inherit the title. After undergoing the ritual, she becomes a shrine maiden protecting the four directions… or so it’s said. The seal… probably refers to the ancient demons pacified by the royal family. It really makes you think… our connection with them runs deep.”

“We must select the Sealing Shrine Maiden and complete the ritual soon. Before the next full moon night…”

“The young ladies of the Wilcloud family have often become the shrine maiden through the generations…. Patricia was such a brilliant magician.”

When one person said this, the elders nodded… and the atmosphere suddenly relaxed as they continued talking about my mother.

“…But aside from her magical talent, she was a gentle, good-natured girl.”

“That’s right. Though I had my doubts about the strange magic tools she sometimes made.”

“She was using the crystal paperweight in my study as reference for those. She was quite fond of it.”

“Ah… that skull-shaped one?”

“Yes.”

Well, this is probably just normal conversation about my mother.

…Hmm. It must be similar to the staff Auria had. Now I know where it originated from, but I’ll refrain from probing deeper.

“Now then. You said something quite concerning earlier.”

“Ah, about defeating the demon?”

“Yes. Including that, I’d like to hear your story. What have you been doing?”

“Understood.”

Well now… where should I begin? It’s difficult for me to explain everything from start to finish. I don’t understand the cause of my memories of past life myself, so I can’t explain it.

That said, I plan to tell them to some extent. I should explain the current situation first.

“First, about the present. I serve as the Otherworld Ambassador in the Kingdom of Verdugal, a position directly under His Majesty Melvin, working on labyrinth-related matters…. I have obligations and things I must do, so regardless of future exchanges, I want to make it clear that I will definitely return to Verdugal.”

If I mentioned being able to use magical power circulation before explaining this, it would likely become complicated. I should make my stance clear first. I’ve already shown King Eberhart my magical power circulation, so hiding it here would be meaningless.

“…Hmm. If you were a free person, we’d want you to remain with the Wilcloud family. But well, we’re in your debt for your help. We’d like to accommodate your wishes.”

Old Sigmund said.

“Thank you. Now then… about when I went to Termwills. The matter is already resolved, but there was a period when I didn’t get along well with my stepmother and her son. So… I learned magic through self-study and used being able to use chantless magic as leverage to negotiate with my father.”

Well, I’ll avoid mentioning the content of my self-study.

“Chantless. Indeed, immature magicians occasionally have magical outbursts due to emotions…”

Valentina nodded.

“That’s right. I used that as my reason. I said I wanted to learn more magic and attend Peresford Academy, so I went to Termwills.”

I met Ashley along the way, there was the Cardiff kidnapping incident where I met Sheila… lots of things happened. I’ll explain the circumstances from the kidnapping incident up to when I fought Linette in some detail.

“—And so when the overeager police stormed the Cardiff mansion, the demon who had infiltrated was exposed. This was probably my first battle with a demon.”

“First, you say?”

“No… I’ve had several battles with demon groups since then.”

“Why you? Well, considering Patricia, I can understand the sentiment somewhat…”

Old Sigmund furrowed his brow.

“Because I can fight demons. I can use magical power circulation.”

“…What!?”

After a few moments, almost everyone from the academy present, starting with the elders, either widened their eyes or rose from their seats.

“I-is that true!?”

“Yes. Let me show you.”

As I circulated and heightened my magical power, the elders’ faces lit up with joy.

“O-oh…! This is…!”

“Our goal has been achieved too…!”

“…And using this circulation, the new flight technique, the Moon Goddess’s Blessing, and the magic my mother left me, I’ve defeated demons several times with everyone.”

“…I no longer know where to begin asking questions.”

Old Sigmund gave a wry smile while touching his forehead.

“To think magical power circulation would revive away from our hands. How ironic.”

“Theodore-kun. Are you… returning to Verdugal?”

“As I said earlier. I have obligations to everyone and work that I started myself. As for magical power circulation… well, I might be able to cooperate in some ways.”

“…I see. Well, that makes sense.”

At my response, one of the elders looked somewhat dejected.

“But you said ‘regardless of exchanges,’ right? We don’t know Theodore-kun’s situation or Verdugal’s situation. We should proceed calmly so everyone can be satisfied, don’t you think?”

When Valentina said this to the elders, Sigmund nodded.

“The problems have piled up because we’ve been asleep until now… but since we made Patricia bear a difficult role, we can’t make unreasonable demands of her memento. But, yes indeed. The demons appearing in Verdugal seem deeply connected to Beriondora too, so it might be good to approach His Majesty about offering technical cooperation with Theodore and Verdugal.”

“I see.”

“That’s certainly true.”

The elders nodded as if convinced.

Technical cooperation? Well, that would probably be classified as something that can be shared rather than secret arts, but would that include airships and the creation methods of those golems? Are those part of the Sages’ Academy’s technology too?

+++

# **276 – Technical Exchange**

“At any rate, now that I’ve recovered, I must pay my respects at the Royal Castle. But before that, Theodore. Could you introduce your companions in a bit more detail?”

“Of course. Well—”

We had only briefly exchanged names during the memory restoration process.

After all, we came directly to the academy alliance after fighting Zadias, so we’re still dressed in combat dresses and equipped with weapons. They probably still have questions about what kind of gathering this is.

During the introductions, they didn’t react to Rosemary or Marlene’s names… probably because the memory seal was placed on the elders before their names became known in Silvatoria.

So as I introduced everyone… the consecutive titles of “fiancée” and “bride sent from the royal family” made everyone’s expressions shift from puzzled to strained smiles, which was quite something to behold.

When we got to Sheila and Irmhild, the “fiancée” titles finally stopped, and Old Sigmund seemed somewhat relieved.

“…Indeed… if you have achievements like defeating demons, I suppose that makes sense.”

“Grace has been living with my mother since I was born… so she might know stories from before I can remember.”

“Oh ho. That interests me. I’d like to hear those stories once things have settled down.”

At Old Sigmund’s words, Grace quietly bowed and placed her hand over her chest with a smile. Old Sigmund closed his eyes when he noticed her ring.

“That ring…?”

“It was made by my mother.”

“This ring has protected me until today. It’s very precious to me.”

“A seal ring. That’s originally a technique passed down from shrine maiden to shrine maiden through generations. Patricia adapted it to weaken her own constitution. If it’s protecting Lady Grace, then it’s best to continue cherishing it.”

“Thank you.”

Grace placed her hand over the ring and nodded. Then—at that moment, the messenger returned.

“Was I interrupting?”

“Not at all. We were just finishing up our conversation.”

When I answered, the messenger’s expression relaxed.

“Is that so? We’ve confirmed the surrender of everyone in the tower up to the upper levels. Therefore… we’d like to speak with the members of the seven families as well, so we’d appreciate if you could accompany us to the Royal Castle. Of course, if anyone is feeling unwell, we can reschedule.”

“Hmm. That’s quite timely. I shall go to the Royal Castle myself.”

“Lord Sigmund. I shall accompany you as well.”

When Old Sigmund stood up, Valentina followed.

“…It was probably that Volheim fellow. My study was ransacked.”

Several minutes later. Old Sigmund emerged from his room with a grim expression, having finished his preparations.

He wore a robe and carried a magic staff, looking quite dignified and fitting for his title of elder.

“Was anything taken?”

Asked Valentina. She too had changed, now wearing a white robe with embroidery and carrying a magic staff.

“No. When I sealed my memories, I moved all truly important materials and catalysts to the treasure room with a magical lock. They just overturned some books. To enter the treasure room, my memories had to be restored first.”

Old Sigmund grinned.

So ultimately, neither Zadias nor Volheim could enter the treasure room. The Volheim faction magicians must have worked hard in their own way, since they developed techniques like miasma techniques from their research.

“Then, shall we go?”

Urged by the messenger, we headed to the Royal Castle by carriage.

When we arrived at the Royal Castle, they stared wide-eyed at the airship lying in the courtyard and the rubble from the destroyed walls.

“What happened here?”

“Zadias attempted to take His Majesty Eberhart’s life, and while we subdued him… well, let’s just say these are the aftereffects of that battle…”

Some parts were destroyed by Zadias and his golems, but I also broke through walls and floors. I can’t say I don’t feel somewhat responsible.

“Zadias underwent demonification, so it was unavoidable.”

When Sheila said this, Marlene nodded repeatedly. Old Sigmund’s mouth twitched.

“It seems he was colluding with demons… and had established techniques for manipulating miasma.”

“He brought out a giant golem, and we fought it in the audience chamber.”

Added Ashley and Rosemary.

“Deplorable… Even though he should carry the blood of the Beriondora royal family, who are said to have bravely fought demons… he’s fallen as low as one can go.”

“But if you defeated the demonified Zadias and a giant golem, then this situation makes sense.”

“Indeed. It seems Theodore and his companions possess power beyond what we imagined.”

“Well… compared to the demons I’ve fought before, he was practically a downgraded version.”

When I shared my thoughts, Old Sigmund gave a wry smile.

“Are demons… things that humans transform into like that?”

“From what I saw of His Majesty Eberhart’s mutation due to miasma erosion, it just seemed like he thought of controlling it. But somehow, I feel the fundamental nature is different.”

When Irmhilt tilted her head and voiced her question, Claudia answered.

“…There’s a passage in oral tradition that says ‘humans are not demons’… What you saw of Zadias might be better described as a failed attempt to bring humans closer to demons. If that’s the case, there are records in the literature.”

A failed attempt. So the completed version would be a true demon, I suppose.

That raises the question of what the difference is between a failed attempt transformed from a human and the completed version. It seemed much closer to a real demon than the half-demons created by Gardinis and the Duoveris Cult.

As we talked, we proceeded deeper into the Royal Castle. When we were shown to the VIP room, King Eberhart, Princess Adriana and Princess Stephania, along with their escort Marquis Zilbolt and others were waiting.

“Your Majesty.”

“Lord Sigmund. Are you sure it’s alright for you to be moving about already?”

“Originally, I merely sealed my own memories. Since we used the proper procedure to undo the magic, I’m perfectly healthy.”

“…Right. That was the case.”

King Eberhart smiled self-deprecatingly.

“At any rate, I must apologize for allowing that man’s rampage.”

“…At this point, saying that won’t change anything. Let the royal family and academy alliance join as one and devote our strength to repelling the demon threat.”

“…You would… say that to me?”

“It seems Her Highness Adriana sheltered Selblum.”

Selblum. Probably the magician who, like my mother, was given one half of the memory liberation spell formula.

Princess Adriana closed her eyes.

“That person said that the day would come when Silvatoria would return to the right path.”

“…I cannot betray that person’s trust.”

When King Eberhart spoke, Princess Adriana nodded.

“Now then… I’d like to discuss what comes next.”

“Indeed. We also have matters to discuss regarding Verdgar and Theodore.”

“Oh ho…”

“Hmm. Technical cooperation, then?”

When Old Sigmund mentioned sending academy alliance members to Verdgar, King Eberhart responded with a serious expression.

“About that, I’d like to add something from my side as well. The collapse of the Black Knights represents a decrease in military strength. I cannot make any firm commitments here, but to compensate for that, I’m thinking of asking Verdgar if we could introduce aerial combat equipment here as well.”

For example, flight through miasma techniques… Unless they plan to control people with Caex Gems like Zadias did, it sounds too problematic to be formally adopted.

“Then this would be more of a technical exchange than technical cooperation.”

King Eberhart smiled wryly. He thought for a moment longer before raising his head.

“We owe Verdgar an unrepayable debt. I suppose I have no choice but to go to Termwills myself and request an audience with Lord Melvin.”

So it would be a summit meeting. Well… it’s a discussion where both sides stand to gain much. Cooperating against demons should be beneficial for everyone.

“One more thing. It seems we can use the power of the Moon Goddess and Moon Temple to enable transfer magic between Termwills and Vinesdora. If it’s not too much trouble, why not use that when heading to Termwills?”

“What…?”

King Eberhart’s eyes widened. I also informed him that with the prayers of the Moon Temple shrine maidens, we can detect crisis situations here. Though I needed to add that we can’t use transfer magic too frequently.

“The Moon Temple. Hmm… That’s reassuring news. I’ll have a notice sent to the shrine maidens accordingly.”

“Your Majesty. May we accompany you to Termwills as well?”

“Lord Sigmund. I would also like to accompany you.”

Said Valentina. So both of them would be going to Termwills.

“Very well. For Lord Sigmund, this would also be his first meeting with his grandson. But… we still haven’t properly welcomed Princess Stephania as a nation. This brings disgrace to our country. It might not be appropriate for me to call it a victory celebration, but we have prepared a banquet and there’s the matter of rewards. Let’s proceed with preparations for Termwills gradually. That should allow the situation to stabilize.”

A banquet. Now that he mentioned it, that was the official reason we came to the Royal Castle.

King Eberhart going to Termwills… well, I should contact them through the communication device.

Is there anything else I should discuss? Probably matters related to the Beriondora investigation.

This could lead to stirring up trouble, so we should proceed with extreme caution. It’s definitely not something to undertake in the current situation, before we’ve emerged from the confusion. It would be better to have thorough discussions between Verdgar and Silvatoria first.

+++

# **277 – The Old Magician and the Airship**

The matter regarding Beriondora would be discussed another day—with King Melvin also present, so the discussions at the royal castle were temporarily concluded for now.

Before the banquet, I wanted to visit the Moon Temple and make some preparations on our end as well.

“Can I take this off now?”

Tephra asked while pinching her hood. Since we were going out into the city, I had invited her along as she seemed bored.

“Hmm. Well, I think it should be fine?”

The city was currently bustling with soldiers moving about hurriedly. Even if remnants of the Crown Prince’s faction were hiding among them, they likely wouldn’t be foolish enough to target someone deliberately drawing attention.

“That’s good.”

When Tephra revealed her face, Old Sigmund and Valentina froze for a moment.

“The Spirit of Mt. Tephra, I see.”

“My grandson certainly has wide connections.”

Given this reaction, I couldn’t help but wonder how they would react after hearing about Claudia once we returned to Termwills.

Old Sigmund, having reached a spot where the courtyard was visible, turned his gaze toward the crashed airship.

“I’m somewhat interested in that. I shall inspect the interior of the ship before the banquet.”

“Is that so? Well, after visiting the Moon Temple, I’ll stop by the ship as well.”

“Indeed. Until later, then.”

“Take care, Theodore-kun.”

“Yes. Please remain somewhat vigilant yourselves. I’ll leave a Familiar for your personal security.”

“Thank you.”

Valentina smiled and nodded.

Leaving Caduceus there, we parted ways with Old Sigmund and Valentina for the time being, and we boarded a carriage heading toward the Moon Temple located in the city. Princess Stephania volunteered to guide us.

We hadn’t been able to do any sightseeing because Zadias was around. From Princess Stephania’s perspective, if she missed this chance, she might not know when she’d get another opportunity for free time.

Thus, both Princess Stephania and Tephra were in rather high spirits.

“It’s been a long time since I’ve been able to leisurely see the city of Vinesdora like this.”

“I am also looking forward to the banquet.”

“Indeed.”

The two of them seemed to be hitting it off quite well.

“Sister, won’t today’s banquet be quite trying for you?”

Rosemary said.

Come to think of it, Zadias had been obstructing marriage proposals for Princess Stephania. Now that Zadias was gone, there would likely be many nobles seeking engagement with Princess Stephania…

“Ah, that should be fine. His Majesty Eberhart has kindly indicated that he isn’t hosting the soirée with that intention.”

“Hmm? While it involves you, Sister, perhaps he’s also being considerate of Theodore’s background as well?”

Rosemary seemed to be pondering while opening and closing her feathered fan.

“Is it related to the Sages’ Academy?”

Ashley inquired.

The Sages’ Academy seems to maintain a certain distance from royalty and nobility. It’s unclear how much information about Zadias will become public due to this incident, but the story of treating King Eberhart and the Academy elders will likely be shared… and if so, naturally, some people might try to get closer.

“That’s right. From King Eberhart’s perspective, he probably can’t explain the details. In that case, it makes sense to take measures to maintain distance from the start. I’m sure he doesn’t want the domestic nobility complicating the situation.”

Claudia closed her eyes and gave a wry smile before adding.

“However, while there might be some political intent, perhaps he also genuinely wants it to be a welcoming occasion? If the guest of honor becomes weary despite King Eberhart’s efforts to entertain, it would defeat the purpose.”

“The feudal lords will probably be somewhat dissatisfied, though.”

While we were having such conversations, we arrived at the Moon Temple. Inside the walls was a garden, with a stone-paved path leading to the temple.

The Moon Temple in Vinesdora was quite sizable, but not as peculiar a building as the one in Termwills. It could be described as a typical temple with rows of pillars.

“This will only take a moment.”

Claudia stepped onto the temple grounds after alighting from the carriage. A Magic Circle glowed at her feet, and from there, a band of light raced along the outer perimeter of the grounds. A band of light returned from the opposite direction and merged with the Magic Circle deployed at Claudia’s feet.

It seemed to be as quick as her words suggested. Perhaps having seen the light from within the grounds, a Shrine Maiden appeared with a puzzled expression, but Claudia, standing still, directed a gentle smile toward her. By that time, Claudia’s Technique was already complete.

The Shrine Maiden looked slightly bewildered but bowed to Claudia and returned inside.

Afterward, we toured the city of Vinesdora by carriage and then returned to the royal castle. In the courtyard, Old Sigmund still seemed to be examining the airship.

“Grandfather.”

“Oh. You’re back?”

When I peeked my face into the still-tilted airship, Old Sigmund and Valentina looked up.

“It seemed like you were investigating something. Is there anything I can assist with?”

“No, no. We were just observing Volheim’s handiwork, which was shaped based on the materials we left behind.”

“His Majesty seems to be considering whether the airship technology can be introduced to Verdgar.”

Ah. So he really does intend to bring airship technology to Verdgar. That’s why he was checking the interior to see if there were any parts corresponding to secret arts.

It seems the memory Seals and hiding materials in the Treasure Room weren’t fully prepared. Lower priority items were probably postponed. If Demons were to seize the airship… it wouldn’t be a desirable situation, but it’s probably because it’s unrelated to the Barrier.

But… Zadias had been boasting about the completion of the airship as his own achievement. In the end, it seems Volheim and the others merely inherited the research of the elders.

“Though it might be odd for me to say this since I broke it… can it be repaired?”

Grace asked, sounding somewhat apologetic.

“What’s this? So it was you, Lady Grace?”

Old Sigmund patted the completely immobilized upper body of the white Golem.

“I threw it from the audience chamber.”

“Another bold feat… The ship sank because one of its three heart components was shot through from the inside, disrupting the balance, I’d reckon. The ship tilted, the crew panicked and fled, resulting in a loss of maintenance and the crash. If a Golem gets thrown in, that’s likely to happen.”

He laughed cheerfully as he said this.

“So if we replace that heart component…?”

“Indeed. If we replace it and do some minor repairs to the exterior, I think we can get it moving. While I’d like to bring a completed product to Verdgar as a sample… well, we didn’t build this, so perhaps we shouldn’t worry too much about it.”

“I’ve checked it over generally… but it seems no techniques resembling secret arts are used in the ship.”

“That’s right. However, the problem lies here.”

He tapped what appeared to be a cannon firing mechanism with his Staff. Rows of crystal ball-like objects engraved with patterns were lined up. Touching these and sending Magical Power would probably activate them.

“I thought it was a Magic Tool that fires Magical Power projectiles.”

“Indeed. Your assessment is correct. As for its purpose… this seems more for Monsters on the ground or… otherwise, aimed at humans. Its shape isn’t very weapon-like, which is also not good. Until it becomes widely known, it could be used for Surprise Attacks.”

“Probably. Even with a Surprise Attack, this likely wouldn’t work on Demons.”

It seems the angle can be adjusted somewhat… but whether one could hit a Demon through this viewing port… well, I think it’s impossible.

“Therefore, even if we repair the airship, it would be better to remove this. I don’t think disseminating its manufacturing method would lead to good results.”

I share that opinion. For long-range attacks, loading existing equipment would suffice… and for anti-Demon Equipment, rather than thinking about defeating a Demon with it alone, it would be better to explore other methods.

For example—something that affects a wide area and is difficult to Dodge.

Effects like attenuating Miasma or disrupting control would be desirable. Ideally, Equipment that makes the enemy reluctant to actively target the airship. If we could establish a method like accompanying it with the Wyvern Corps, intimidating the Demons, and then defeating them in group combat… if such a form is established, the enemy would likely hesitate to attack recklessly.

“Zadias and Volheim seemed solely focused on controlling and utilizing Miasma, but if the research has progressed to some extent, we might be able to create Equipment for countering Demons from that. Though I think anything half-baked would be tough against High-ranking Demons.”

“Certainly. I suppose I must review the materials those fellows left behind…”

If we’re going to take this ship as a sample to Verdgar… for now, let’s use Wood Magic to patch the holes in the hull.

+++

# **278 – Feast and Honor**

We temporarily patched the holes in the airship and then moved together to the royal castle’s guest room to wait for the banquet.

Though there was still time before it started, the conversation naturally continued about the airship.

“Those Golems you fought were originally developed as armor for magic knights and magicians,” Old Sigmund explained.

“Is that so?”

Indeed, shields equipped with magical power conversion armor seemed quite useful…

“The size directly correlates with absorption capacity. When miniaturized, the performance becomes rather limited. Improving efficiency was the challenge.”

“In that sense, using them as Golem armor might have been quite logical,” Valentina remarked.

It seemed they had chosen to leverage the strengths rather than solve the problems regarding Golems.

“Then perhaps we could even build the airship’s hull entirely from conversion armor. Converting absorbed energy into propulsion, for instance. That would achieve both defense power and mobility.”

“That might be reasonable, but production would be the issue. After all, it’s not something ordinary blacksmiths can make. It requires spell formulas to create… and the larger the scale, the more difficult the magic control becomes.”

“Magic control is my specialty. If you could teach me the production process and spell formulas, I’ll take charge of it.”

“That’s reckless… or so I’d normally say, but in your case…” Old Sigmund smiled wryly.

Just then, a knock sounded at the door.

“Come in,” I answered, and a maid entered, bowing respectfully.

“The banquet preparations are complete.”

“Then let us proceed.”

The banquet was held in the dance hall located in one wing of the royal castle.

They had apparently brought in tables and arranged dishes upon them. The musicians were already prepared, playing gentle melodies.

We were seated at a balcony overlooking the hall. King Eberhart and Princess Adriana’s seats were there, along with Elliot’s, Marquis Zilbolt’s, and those of his retainers.

Being the guests of honor, we were visible to everyone but difficult to approach. King Eberhart seemed to have chosen this location deliberately. While one could greet Princess Stephania after climbing the stairs, it was right in front of King Eberhart’s position, making careless conversation impossible.

“We’re seated here too, so you understand what His Majesty Eberhart intends,” Old Sigmund said.

“Basically, ‘stay out of it,’ I suppose?”

“Something like that.”

“We don’t know how they’ll announce Zadias’s situation, but… there was a disturbance during the day, the banquet is being held despite his absence, and the opposing elders are appearing in public. With my elder sister present too. Those with limited information would hesitate, while those in the know would understand the approach,” Rosemary said, fluttering her feather fan with a shiver.

“If they stick their necks out carelessly, they’ll be accused of trying to probe the royal family’s internal affairs. Normally there might be complaints, but today is clearly not ordinary times.”

“Especially with His Majesty Eberhart present too,” Claudia added with closed eyes, prompting a wry smile from Princess Stephania.

Any noble without that much perception wouldn’t last long. Since Princess Stephania’s visit was rather sudden, few regional lords attended. Most attendees were court nobles… Well, today’s events would likely spread throughout Silvatoria soon enough.

Ashley and Marlene were both listening intently to the conversation. As a lord, Ashley probably found much of it educational.

The banquet attendees began entering the dance hall. The nobles glanced toward Princess Stephania on the balcony, but only bowed from afar—none approached.

Once everyone had gathered, the musicians changed their tune. In response, King Eberhart and Princess Adriana appeared. The nobles stirred slightly—it had been a while since King Eberhart appeared in public.

King Eberhart smiled in our direction before having Princess Adriana stand a step behind him as he approached the balcony’s edge. He then surveyed all present and spread his arms wide.

“My people, thank you for gathering today. I fell ill and could not appear before you for many days. I’m sure this caused you anxiety, but worry no more.”

King Eberhart paused and looked toward us.

“Princess Stephania from Verdugal, concerned about my condition, visited with skilled healing magicians. My recovery is entirely thanks to their efforts.”

As King Eberhart spoke, Princess Stephania stood, gathered her skirt, and curtsied, prompting applause.

“Furthermore, as you can see, Elder Sigmund of the Academy has also recovered from illness and attends this banquet. This too is thanks to those brought by Princess Stephania. Through their actions, I dare say the dark clouds casting shadows over our kingdom have been dispelled.”

Dark clouds casting shadows… Well, that metaphorically refers to Zadias and Volheim. For those in the know, King Eberhart’s stance is clear—he’s publicly declaring his extremely poor opinion of Zadias and his faction.

“And Marquis Zilbolt.”

“Yes, Your Majesty.”

“You endured much hardship while I lay ill.”

“Your Majesty. Such undeserved words.”

Marquis Zilbolt knelt in a vassal’s bow.

“Your wife and child were also ill, were they not? Some who don’t know the circumstances might criticize the path the dark clouds forced you to take. But Marquis. I know you are innocent. I know your integrity. Henceforth, I shall not permit any groundless slander against you.”

“I shall strive to prove worthy of Your Majesty’s trust and bring no shame to the kingdom’s nobility.”

So he compared being taken hostage to illness. They couldn’t publicly reveal Zadias’s actions directly, but the metaphor sufficed. This would lead to rumors that Zadias and Volheim had poisoned King Eberhart, the elders, and Marquis Zilbolt’s family.

Some might speculate this led to his downfall and disinheritance. The king and elder recovered. Despite the crown prince’s downfall, Marquis Zilbolt—who belonged to the crown prince’s faction—had his honor publicly declared.

They might connect the castle’s destruction and airship incident in some way… but the truth would be concealed to protect the kingdom and royal family’s honor.

“And one more thing. Regarding the renowned Sir Benedict of our Magic Knight Order, there’s something I must tell you all.”

Following Marquis Zilbolt, Elliot knelt.

“This man is Elliot Rodias Siln, a noble of Verdugal. Having regained his lost memories, it’s only proper he be returned to Verdugal. Sir Elliot. Raise your head.”

“Yes.”

“You served well as my sword until today. Your loyalty and valor—I shan’t forget them, even after you depart these lands.”

“Your gracious words. I shall never forget the kindness Your Majesty has shown me. Though I return to Verdugal, should danger threaten you, I will surely come running.”

“Good. And regarding this healing, those with particularly remarkable achievements shall receive rewards. I’ll speak with them later.”

King Eberhart narrowed his eyes and nodded before turning back to the attendees.

“I celebrate the friendship with the Kingdom of Verdugal and wish for our mutual prosperity. And to welcome Princess Stephania, who has visited our kingdom, I have prepared this banquet. Everyone, tonight, drink deeply from your cups, dance and sing, and celebrate to your hearts’ content.”

Cheers praising King Eberhart, Silvatoria, and Verdugal resounded.

King Eberhart raised a hand in response to the applause and cheers before returning to his seat. The musicians began playing lively music, and dishes were brought out one after another.

Sheila and Irmhild seemed particularly interested in the musicians’ performance. Well, it might inspire them in some ways.

“Theodore-dono. I apologize for not mentioning your name publicly. Normally, I should have announced it and explained the rewards in more detail,” King Eberhart said upon returning.

“No, thank you for your consideration,” I replied with a wry smile.

They concealed the information because I’m a Demon Slayer.

“I considered several rewards for you, but I’m not fully aware of your circumstances. I thought something matching your wishes would please you more. If you have any desires, speak them freely.”

Asked this, I thought for a moment before answering.

“Then… something to prepare for fighting demons.”

“Excellent. Then I shall open the treasure room. You may choose from among its contents.”

…The Magic Kingdom’s treasure room. I wonder what we’ll find there.

+++

# **279 – Magic Bullet**

The nobles seemed to be watching our situation while talking among themselves, but none of them approached us too deeply. Well, there’s nothing we can do about being the subject of various rumors. After all, Tephra is here, and this is also after the incident with Zadias.

Perhaps it would have been improper to skip formal greetings entirely, as the main figures did come to greet us. However, none of them tried to initiate any particular conversation, and the banquet concluded without any major troubles.

From our perspective, we enjoyed the food and music, and King Eberhart successfully demonstrated his recovery to everyone in the royal castle and, by extension, to the feudal lords. For the nobles who couldn’t take advantage of this precious opportunity, it must have been a disappointing outcome… Well, the timing was bad, and it’s none of our concern anyway.

After the banquet ended, King Eberhart called out to us.

“You all must be busy people. You likely have many duties to attend to starting tomorrow, so why not take your time afterward to select your rewards? I’ve already spoken with the treasure room manager. As long as it’s not something exceptionally valuable, there shouldn’t be any issues.”

“Thank you very much.”

…And so, right after the banquet, we were shown inside the treasure room.

“Exceptionally valuable” apparently refers to items essential to Silvatoria. That said, such items were stored even deeper within the treasure room.

“This way, please.”

We were led to the treasure room by the manager in charge. Similar to Termwills, there was also a catalog, with items organized by category.

“So, what kind of things are you looking for?”

Many items had apparently been donated to the royal castle from the Sages’ Academy, and Old Sigmund was accompanying us in an advisory role.

“We currently have enough weapons and armor for now… I was hoping for items that could enhance our abilities or broaden our tactical options.”

The catalog contained brief descriptions and origins. We all went through it with the feeling of literally browsing a catalog, and it seemed each of us found something of interest, as questions started flying about various items.

“What about this?”

“Gauntlets of Thunder… Well, they’re exactly as the name suggests. They deliver a lightning strike to whatever you touch. Like ordinary magic tools, they can be activated at will, and I’ve heard their power is quite considerable.”

Lightning, huh. Sheila might have taken a liking to that tactic she used in coordination with Marlene, where they electrified the sticky threads.

Restricting movement with sticky threads, and directly linking it to attack with lightning strikes. Both the sticky threads and the paralysis from lightning complement Sheila, who prioritizes speed in various ways. The fact that it’s a strong weapon against enemies in metal armor is probably another advantage for Sheila, who focuses on slash attacks.

“Mmm. If there’s nothing else, I’ll take this.”

Though tentative, Sheila made her decision.

“I’m curious about these Reciprocating Gems,” said Irmhild.

“Those, huh. They return to their paired stone even if you throw them. Since they float back, they don’t return at very high speed… They were developed with the idea of retrieving launched objects. There was talk of using them for projectile weapons, but the cost became prohibitive, so they ended up shelved.”

Irmhild has an eye for good items too. Their intended use would be as a pure enhancement for her giant arrows. Given the nature of using spears as arrow ammunition, until now she couldn’t carry many and had to create situations where she could land a sure hit, but with these, she could use them more freely.

The fact that they don’t return as fast as Ouroboros… means there will be a gap between shots, but there are advantages too. It would be dangerous and troublesome if the spears returned to her hand at high speed. Anyway, since she fights while leaping around, it shouldn’t be a problem.

Since they’re in gem form, if we take them back to the workshop and have Viola process them, they should be able to be incorporated into Irmhild’s equipment without difficulty.

“How about this for me?” said Seraphina.

What Seraphina chose was a transverse flute. It was said that playing it summons a spirit beast that protects the owner… If the horn is for offense, then this one is for defense, I suppose.

“What kind of spirit beast is this?”

“Something like a semi-transparent wolf’s head. It flies around and bites opponents.”

I see. It seems capable of handling aerial combat too… Since Seraphina often pairs with Irmhild due to her characteristics, it should also be suitable as an escort role.

Well then… Sheila, Irmhild, and Seraphina have probably decided on these.

“This Aura Amplifying Bracelet seems interesting to me,” said Grace.

“Enhancing destructive power, I assume?”

“Yes.”

At my words, Grace showed a smile.

Grace’s choice is straightforward. She intends to further develop her strengths and aim for increased attack power.

The catalog also mentions it can focus and emit fighting spirit, but for Grace, that’s probably just a bonus. Well, having an easily usable shooting technique added to her repertoire might be convenient in various ways.

“I’m interested in this grimoire,” said Ashley.

“A grimoire of healing magic, huh. It was on loan from the Academy for King Eberhart’s treatment… But, well, I suppose it’s fine.”

“Then, once I’ve learned it, I’ll return it.”

“It’s fine. It’s not a secret technique. It’s the kind of thing that’s more beneficial the more it spreads.”

Like Grace, Ashley seems to have chosen to enhance her strengths.

“What kind of magic is recorded in the healing grimoire?” I asked.

Old Sigmund answered while making a gesture as if recalling. “A Barrier of Regeneration, I believe, and things like launching healing magic that normally requires contact over a distance.”

That sounds useful. It should complement Ashley well in various ways, as she constructs defensive positions.

As we progressed through the catalog, Marlene pointed her finger.

“Marlene, that one?”

She nodded repeatedly. What Marlene indicated was a magical creature in the shape of a bird.

“…Could it serve as a substitute for a familiar?” said Rosemary.

At Rosemary’s words, Old Sigmund nodded. “That’s right. If you properly form a contract, that should be possible.”

A bird familiar, huh. It’s orthodox, but bird familiars are actually useful for reconnaissance, tailing, and such. While only magicians can utilize familiars, if the party as a whole possesses more of them, the options available increase. It’s probably good for Marlene to have one too. You can’t always get what you want with a summoning ritual.

“What about Marie?”

“As for me… the magic bag that appeared earlier seems nice. I’d like it if it’s a convenient size for carrying around.”

“That one has a protective ability that prevents items inside from breaking, but the weight and size of items don’t change when placed inside. It’s been passed down since Beriondora’s time. It can hold a considerable amount, but not an unlimited quantity. The size is about what you can hang from your waist. Living creatures cannot enter.”

“…I see. I thought it might be just right for carrying medicines.”

…That would mean she could keep things like the magical flames she used when we were inside the book readily available. Potions are one thing, but carrying glass bottles or flasks around regularly is inconvenient. Potions are manageable, but dangerous substances are even more so.

Being a magic bag, it’s certainly convenient, but Rosemary could probably make even more effective use of it by performing impromptu mixing on the spot or using prepared chemicals. Of course, it would also be useful during exploration.

“As for me… due to the nature of having magic on standby for activation, I can’t participate much in combat, so something defensive seems good. This Staff of Shadow Thorns looks nice,” said Claudia.

It seems to be a self-defense tool for magicians, where thorns extend from the staff to entangle opponents.

Hmm. So she wants something that can restrain movement while she uses teleportation magic on opponents. Hmm. Everyone is deciding quite easily.

“This is…” I followed the description in the catalog that caught my eye.

“Magic Bullet… It says it’s a weapon for users of magical power circulation…”

“This one has also been passed down since Beriondora’s time… It’s a weapon that hasn’t had a user for a long time. It seems to be a magical creature created for users of magical power circulation, who are weak at shooting battles, to deal with distant enemies. Well, the literature says it can be used without problems in close combat too.”

According to the catalog, it could probably be considered the same type of weapon as Marlene’s Saucer or Luceriage’s Dancing Sword. Though it’s single-shot.

It appears to be a weapon that launches a sphere filled with circulating magical power at tremendous speed to pierce through enemies—a literal living bullet, it seems. It’s also written as having an evil eye, so apparently it has an eye.

The bullet’s trajectory can be controlled by the user’s will… Hmm. I didn’t originally intend to engage in shooting battles, but it seems usable both for closing distance with opponents and for increasing options in close combat.

“Equipment suited for magical power circulation tends to have a magical creature feel to it, doesn’t it?” said Grace.

“Yeah. Normal materials break easily, you see. With magical creatures, you can probably enhance them as an extension of circulating ki.”

The Chimera Coat can also be incorporated into the circulation.

“Hmm. Your staff is quite interesting too… From the looks of it, it seems specialized for circulation.”

“It’s an item I received as a reward previously. It’s quite versatile, so I find it very useful. I’ll try it out a bit, and if there are no problems, I’ll go with this one.”

And so, each of us received the actual items to examine them.

The Magic Bullet was a black sphere about the size of a clenched fist. When I channeled circulating magical power into it—a single eye opened, and bat-like wings sprouted.

When it took off from my palm, it flew around me happily. The catalog mentioned that during a charge, it closes its eye and folds its wings to become a complete bullet… But normally, it takes this form.

+++

# **280 – Nostalgia**

The Magic Bullet flew around me for a while, but seemed to show interest in Caduceus, Ouroboros, and Nemea and Capella inside the Chimera Coat. It flew close to its fellow magical creatures and blinked its eyes.

Caduceus, who had taken the form of a cat, followed the Magic Bullet with his eyes. Ouroboros purred, while Nemea and Capella poked their heads out and appeared to exchange greetings with the Magic Bullet.

I’m not sure if it’s because they’re all magical creatures with a sense of camaraderie, or because they’re all my companions… but well, it doesn’t seem to be a problem.

As for what Marlene received… it was a bird with metallic-feathered wings. More than just a bird, this was a raptor. A falcon.

When Marlene held the falcon in her hands and channeled magical power to awaken it, it spread its wings and flew around the Treasure Room. Though it seemed a bit cramped, it circled around once before returning to Marlene and landing on the floor. This one also seemed fine. After greeting Marlene, it appeared to join the circle of magical creatures to exchange greetings.

“We should give these children names too,” Grace said.

“…Hmm. How about Balor for the Magic Bullet?”

I thought of it because of the magic bullet connection and association with a single eye. Naming it directly after Taslam also seemed like a good idea.

When I gave it the name, the Magic Bullet—Balor—blinked its eyelids and fluttered around.

“Do you like it?”

“I wonder…?”

I didn’t have an answer to Sheila’s question…

“As for the bird… I’ll need to name it when I make the familiar contract later.”

When I said this, Marlene smiled and nodded slightly.

Everyone had received their respective treasures, and those who could test them out were doing so. Testing Balor… wouldn’t be possible here.

…So when I asked King Eberhart about it, he said I could try it out in the courtyard.

In exchange, since battle mage weapons are rare and he wanted to see it, King Eberhart, Princess Stephania, Princess Adriana, Valentina, and Elliot also came to the courtyard.

“Have you decided on your reward?” Elliot asked.

“Yes. We’re about to test it out, and if there are no problems, that should settle it. What about you, Elliot—”

Elliot was wearing Mithril Silver armor covering his shoulders and chest area.

“I received magical armor. …For someone like me returning to my homeland, this is such excessive consideration…”

“Good. Consider it a parting gift. Superior weapons and armor should be handled by those worthy of them. Leaving them on display is like letting grain rot.”

King Eberhart laughed. Apparently, Marquis Zilbolt also received a magical staff as a reward. Well… we didn’t specifically ask for weapons or armor.

Now then. With everyone gathered, let’s begin.

“There’s a possibility that fragments might scatter when the target is shot down, so please allow me to take precautions.”

“Very well.”

For now, deploying a Defense Field should suffice.

“Then—I’ll begin.”

Placing Balor on my palm, I circulated my ki. I fed magical power to Balor, or rather, had it accumulate power… charging it with energy.

When it was wrapped in a pale spark, I released the Magic Bullet.

“Go—”

With my voice, Balor curled up as if folding its wings and closed its eyes—or so I thought, but the next moment it flew off at an absurd speed from the initial velocity.

A Light Arrow shot straight up into the night sky. Higher and higher without end. While it’s wrapped in my magical power, a pseudo-connection is created. It’s like having a second familiar, though limited.

However, when it becomes a bullet, even with the magical connection, its eyes are closed so its vision is blocked. By controlling it from my side, I can manipulate its trajectory. Therefore—my line-of-sight distance would essentially become the effective range, I suppose.

Of course, if Caduceus is present, the range should extend further. Depending on the situation, it might even be possible to shoot targets from a distance without the magician themselves appearing at all.

Controlling its movements. The Light Bullet drew a large arc, leaving complex trails of light in the night darkness as I wished.

“Wow…”

“This is…”

Next should be its power, right? I brought it back to a close distance and launched an ice block with Water Magic. Balor easily shattered it to pieces.

It shattered the fragments further. Two, three times.

“Return.”

While controlling its movements, I pulled it back to my hand. When it reached my palm, Balor—which had been spinning like a drill—spread its wings and stopped moving. Despite having executed a Charge, it didn’t have a single scratch. It has the sturdiness befitting a weapon.

“It’s amazing. It would probably pierce through shields and armor easily.”

“Hmm… Impressive power.”

When Princess Adriana and King Eberhart spoke admiringly, Old Sigmund also nodded.

“To bring out this level of performance on your first attempt… It seems it can also serve as a Magic Slave.”

“I see. So it can become a mobile artillery platform too.”

Magic Slave. It’s a shooting technique where you keep a spell hovering in advance, allowing you to cast magic from there as needed.

Normally, it’s a technique that battle mages shouldn’t be able to use… but Balor can cast magic from its side. In that case, Balor’s field of vision could probably be used for aiming.

Since it can only handle as much as the charged magical power allows, I probably can’t be greedy wanting both charging and artillery functions, but having more options is welcome regardless.

“What do you think?”

“It’s good. I’ve decided on this one.”

While it fills the gap in long-range and shooting combat, it also seems like it will demonstrate power in close combat, which is its original forte.

“Hmm. That’s excellent. Will it be useful?”

“I think if I control the charge in close combat while simultaneously engaging in hand-to-hand combat, I might be able to fully utilize both my own abilities and the magic bullet’s. The rest is just practice.”

At my words, King Eberhart and the others widened their eyes in surprise. However, King Eberhart cleared his throat once and straightened his posture.

“Nnn. Well… it might be possible for you. I hope this magic bullet will protect you and your companions.”

“Thank you.”

“The night has grown quite late… Princess Stephania, will you be returning to your lodgings?”

“Yes. We’ve been using the inn and Marquis Zilbolt’s villa as bases for various preparations, so we need to clean up afterward,” said Princess Stephania.

…We can’t leave until we properly restore things like the hidden passage we dug under the inn.

“I see. We will also proceed with preparations to head to Termwills.”

“Yes. Oh, that’s right. I’d like to take a short stroll around the Sages’ Academy grounds—would that be alright?”

When I asked, King Eberhart’s face broke into a smile.

“You need not hesitate with me. This is your mother’s hometown, after all.”

And so, we restored the hidden door we’d made in the inn room to its original state, filled in the underground passage directly beneath the inn… and the next day arrived. We completed what needed to be done before returning and finished our departure preparations. King Eberhart and Old Sigmund still seemed busy, but we had relatively more free time.

So we decided to head to the academy together—to Silvatoria, or rather, the Sages’ Academy that could be called my mother’s family home—to take a somewhat leisurely look around.

Even though we can come and go with Teleportation Magic, we can’t be that casual about it. We might not have free time the next time we come.

“It’s a nice place. Here,” I murmured while strolling along the walking path within the Sages’ Academy grounds.

“Right?” Valentina smiled.

If the matter with Zadias were resolved, it would be a peaceful, green space where you could feel calm. There’s a pond in the small forest within the grounds, and they’ve even built a gazebo. It’s quiet with good sunlight… a relaxing place.

“Shall we have tea here?”

Rosemary took a tea set out from her Magic Bag. The bag itself is only large enough to attach to a belt at her waist.

“That’s convenient.”

“I think so too. It’s a good item.”

Since the bag itself is modest in size, it doesn’t get in the way of various things.

And so, we all drank tea and relaxed. Ashley made hot water for us.

“Speaking of which… Lady Lisa said she likes it because the lakeshore in the county resembles the place where she grew up a little.”

Grace narrowed her eyes at the view from the gazebo. Her gaze—seemed to be looking somewhere far away.

“That’s… right. Indeed, this area might resemble my mother’s home.”

“Patricia said she wanted to build a wooden house in a forest like this and live there.”

Valentina laughed softly.

“Ah. So that’s why Lady Lisa…”

Ashley closed her eyes.

Yeah. That house was also my mother’s childhood dream.

“—It’s in Gartner County, that house. They used Wood Magic to create a giant tree and hollowed out the inside to make a home.”

“I’d like to see that once.”

“Since you’re also heading to Termwills, Valentina, I think you’ll have opportunities to extend your trip to the county.”

“That’s right. Definitely.”

“It’s a good place. It somewhat resembles my birthplace too.”

“I like that house too,” said Irmhild and Seraphina.

Irmhild’s hometown… the Labyrinth Village. Peaceful with a nearby forest… it might indeed be similar. Claudia smiled somewhat awkwardly and tilted her teacup.

…Tomorrow, or the day after. King Eberhart’s departure preparations and the airship renovation work should be completed. Then we’ll probably depart for Termwills.

So for now, in this place. Let’s rest our wings and relax as much as possible.

Thank you for always reading my work!

+++

# **281 – Journey on the Airship**

The airship’s renovation work seemed to be progressing rapidly, with elders from the Sages’ Academy having come to oversee it.

The magic cannons had been removed, and the magic tools for levitation had been reinstalled – by the next morning, the airship was already floating beside the Royal Castle again, showing how quickly the work had been completed.

While it was good that the airship’s renovation finished early, teleporting the entire ship at once presented some difficulties.

Claudia’s magical power consumption would be substantial, but that could be covered with Circulating Ki. The real problem was that making something as large as an airship disappear and reappear would inevitably attract attention. Since we wanted to keep the existence of Teleportation Magic as secret as possible, having too many witnesses would be problematic.

In that case, it might be better to first send King Eberhart and the others to Termwills via Teleportation Magic, with the airship following afterward by air route. With that in mind, I headed to the Royal Castle to explain. After being led deep into the castle, I met with King Eberhart.

“—While it’s possible to send the entire ship to Termwills using Teleportation Magic, it would inevitably draw attention. Therefore, having the ship travel normally might be preferable.”

After my explanation about the teleportation magic, King Eberhart showed a thoughtful expression before looking up and speaking.

“Hmm… Indeed. However, rather than sending the ship alone to Termwills later, I believe it would be better for me to board it and travel there myself. The fact that this is being delivered as part of Silvatoria’s national policy is important.”

I see. Perhaps King Eberhart wants to demonstrate Silvatoria’s friendly stance toward Verdgar both domestically and internationally by personally delivering the ship.

Given the incident with Zadias, Silvatoria’s internal situation couldn’t be called stable. It wouldn’t be surprising if the upper echelons of Verdgar had some skepticism toward Silvatoria.

While the airship is only part of the overall technological exchange, it’s certainly the most visible part. Being symbolic, he probably wants to handle it personally.

“Understood. Then we’ll also board the ship and accompany you as escorts.”

“That’s reassuring… but you could return first via teleportation magic if you prefer?”

“No. We’d also like to visit Her Highness Stephania along the way, and the Moon Temple in Marquis Fobrester’s territory.”

“The Moon Temple… For teleportation magic preparations?”

“Yes.”

Princess Stephania’s territory is located further north by land from Marquis Fobrester’s territory. When returning from Vinesdora to Termwills, it can serve as a relay point, allowing us to stop by the Moon Temple and create a situation where we can teleport to various places.

We want to establish a situation where we can respond even if demons appear in places other than Termwills.

“Very well. Then let us embark on this journey through the skies by airship together. My travel preparations are complete. We can depart today once the luggage is loaded.”

King Eberhart said this with a pleased expression.

“Understood. Our luggage is packed in the Dragon Palanquin, so we can move anytime once it’s loaded onto the airship.”
