Those boarding the airship include us, Princess Stephania, Elliot, and Tephra. From the Silvatoria side, Marquis Zilbolt and Elmer. King Eberhart, Princess Adriana, Old Sigmund, and as his assistant, Valentina. Additionally, there are King Eberhart’s royal guards and servants, plus a few crew members for operating the ship.

Princess Adriana is scheduled to remain with the Verdgar side even after King Eberhart returns from Termwills, serving as a goodwill ambassador to Verdgar as King Eberhart’s representative.

We loaded the Dragon Palanquin onto the airship and divided the work of carrying the luggage to the cabins. While working, something occurred to me and I asked Elliot.

“Elliot-san, are you sure you don’t want to use teleportation magic?”

I thought he might want to reach the Barony of Silun as quickly as possible. However, at Elliot’s own request, he decided to board the airship as an escort.

“Yes. As a former magic knight of Silvatoria, I wish to protect His Majesty Eberhart during his journey. Especially since Ashley and her fiancé Theodore-dono will also be accompanying us.”

Saying this, Elliot smiled quietly.

He’s either very dutiful or has a strong sense of responsibility.

“Theo, they say we’re departing soon.”

Grace, who had come down from the deck carrying luggage, called out to me.

“Ah. Understood.”

It’s time to say goodbye to Vinesdora for a while. I decided to go to the deck to take in the view.

We temporarily paused moving and organizing the luggage and went together to the deck. Old Sigmund was at the helm, with Valentina assisting him.

“Oh, Theodore. Perfect timing – we’re about to depart now.”

He said this with a smile.

“Yes. This is my first time traveling by airship, so I’m looking forward to it.”

“Hmm.”

The ropes mooring the airship were untied.

When Old Sigmund touched the crystal ball resting on the pedestal beside the helm, the airship gradually began to gain altitude. As the magic tools at the rear of the hull activated, the sails caught the tailwind, and the airship began moving toward Verdgar.

Since this was my first experience flying through the sky on something other than myself, whether wyvern or hippogriff, I found myself crowding toward the edge of the deck. Stopping myself with my hand, I asked Valentina.

“…Is there no concern about tilting due to weight?”

The wyverns also serve as escorts for the unarmed airship during the journey. The thought of the airship capsizing from the weight of its escorts was too awful to contemplate.

“That’s fine. The three power sources are designed to maintain balance.”

Valentina answered my concern.

“…Then it should be okay. Alright, you all.”

When I gave permission, the Lindwurm cried out. Following its voice, the wyverns stretched their necks with keen interest, looking down at the city from the deck.

…Yeah. Seems I was worrying unnecessarily. Despite the strong wind hitting the mast, the deck itself is wind-free – various wind magic controls and balance maintenance seem to be employed in the airship beyond what meets the eye.

The airship advanced as if gliding through the sky. The people seeing off King Eberhart gradually grew smaller. The city where Mother was born and raised receded into the distance. The sky was blue—and the mountain range stretching into the distance was beautiful.

“Is the direction correct?”

“Yes. We’ll continue like this and cross the sea from the port.”

While looking at a compass and map, Valentina was speaking with Old Sigmund. We’re first heading for Princess Stephania’s territory. Apparently, we’ll follow the same route as the Dragon Palanquin over the main roads. If we don’t use established routes, the possibility of encountering monsters increases.

After crossing the sea and reaching Princess Stephania’s territory, we’ll proceed by land heading south. We plan to stop by Marquis Fobrester’s territory before heading to Termwills.

“Then let’s continue along this route for a while.”

“I’ll inform you when we reach the branching point.”

“Hmm. Now then… Theodore. Might I have a moment?”

Called by Old Sigmund, I went over to him.

“Along the way, I thought I’d explain about the airship. I mentioned this briefly before – while this ship was made by that Zadias fellow, we were also involved in its development. If you intend to be involved in airship construction, you must learn about ships.”

“Yes. It would probably be good for everyone to hear this too. Having everyone know how to operate the ship would be insurance in case of emergencies.”

“Hmm.”

So we gathered everyone to listen. Once everyone was assembled, Old Sigmund nodded and began talking about the airship.

“Well, operating it isn’t particularly difficult. Turn the helm to change direction. Use the crystal ball on the right to adjust the ship’s altitude. Use the crystal ball on the left to change the ship’s speed.”

Turning the helm sends wind from the magic tools in that direction, and the sails catch the wind to change the ship’s course. Ascending and descending… meaning controlling the output of the three levitation magic tools is done with the right crystal ball.

The left crystal ball adjusts wind strength—essentially, it’s the crystal ball that controls speed.

Though it can’t compare to an airplane, it moves at considerable speed compared to a sailing ship. Since it’s pushing forward something levitated by magic rather than flying by lift, it doesn’t seem like it would stall and crash…

Unlike a real ship, there’s little shaking. The stable behavior makes me feel it’s truly a product of the Magic Kingdom. The three core units levitate the ship… working in coordination to maintain balance. This seems to be the essence of the airship.

“Speaking of which, when we discussed armor, we also talked about propulsion. Do you have any good ideas?”

“I have several… but they should probably match the airship’s core units. I can’t say for sure without testing.”

Since it levitates and doesn’t stall, it seems quite flexible.

+++

# **282 – On the Blue Sea**

I gripped the helm and checked the compass. Confirming the ship’s heading against the needle’s direction, I gazed out over the blue ocean ahead.

The translucent azure under the sunlight, the light reflecting off the sea surface… The blue of the ocean seen from above was beautiful.

“How is it? What are your thoughts on piloting the ship?”

King Eberhart, who had come up to the deck, asked me. Old Sigmund was with him.

“I’m getting quite used to it.”

Piloting the airship was indeed simple. Though it was a sailing ship, the horizontal sails received a steady tailwind, so it required little handling. The crew’s burden was light.

The natural wind was a southerly. Our destination, Verdgar, was also to the south—a headwind. If this were a normal ship, we would need to use fore-and-aft sails to advance against the wind.

Since fore-and-aft sails don’t allow you to sail directly into the wind, you would need to zigzag while carefully checking your direction… but the Magic Tool attached to the bow mitigated the headwind, and the Magic Tool at the stern sent wind from back to front, making that maneuver unnecessary. Thus, piloting was easy, and the crew’s burden was light—that’s how it worked.

On the other hand, there were probably issues unique to airships. First, the bottleneck in operation was how to secure the ship’s power.

The fuel was, of course, Magical Power. A Magician needed to replenish the Magical Power in the airship’s core and Magic Tools.

It might be possible to sail in an energy-saving mode by not using the wind-controlling Magic Tools. In that case, the sailing techniques of a normal sailing ship would be required.

In this instance, since multiple Magicians were aboard the airship, there was no worry on that front, but to operate an airship… considering relief personnel and such, multiple Magicians needed to be aboard.

“However, piloting this completed airship, I can’t help but think… there are many blind spots.”

“That’s true. We must be vigilant on the ground side as well… but as it is now, there are too many unseen areas.”

Because of its ship-like shape, there were many blind spots. The area below the hull was completely invisible to the crew. It wasn’t as if there were no methods, like utilizing Familiars or using Light Magic.

Right now, we had the Lindwurm flying alongside to guard the blind spots. Saphir the Hippogriff was flying around the airship with Elliot. It seemed she would sulk if Elliot didn’t pay attention to her.

“Zadias seemed to intend to use this for combat, but aside from transport capacity, there is room for reconsideration,” King Eberhart said.

Indeed. I should compile the things I learned on this journey as points for improvement. Well, that aside.

“Changing the subject a bit, may I ask for details about the current situation and future treatment of Zadias and Volheim?”

Since we were on the topic of Zadias, I wanted to confirm the present circumstances and what was to come.

“Those two have been placed under Subjugation Magic, forbidden from using Magic, and imprisoned. We plan to extract information from them periodically, but we believe there is virtually no risk of escape.”

“…What do you mean?”

“It means they paid a high price for meddling with Miasma using those red crystals.”

According to King Eberhart… it seemed the Miasma hadn’t completely dissipated, and they could no longer control it, so their limbs and such had been eroded. Due to the Miasma Erosion, Healing Magic that should affect the body hardly worked, and they couldn’t recover from fractures; they were writhing in agony from the double intense pain of Erosion and fractures.

Not only Zadias, but Volheim was the same. That guy lost consciousness early on, but his bones were cracked all over from the Solid Hammer, and the Miasma Erosion was doubling the pain. It was said that escape was practically impossible for both of them.

“Speaking from experience with Miasma Erosion… even natural healing of injuries slows down. They will likely suffer in excruciating pain for a considerable period.”

“That is… rather extreme, one might say.”

“It’s the retribution for meddling with Miasma. You need not trouble yourself over it. If it were a concern, I would have discussed it with you, but there was no need.”

…Indeed. With Circulating Ki, I probably could have drawn out the Miasma… but King Eberhart didn’t bring that up to me.

“Then the issue would be external assistance, I suppose.”

“To prevent that, we’ve been quite careful in selecting the jailers and guards and setting up the system,” King Eberhart said with a wry smile at Old Sigmund’s words.

“In that case… all that’s left is to extract information, I suppose.”

“Indeed. We are also investigating what they were up to through other means. As part of your reward from the other day, we opened the Treasure Room and are having the catalog and items cross-checked. They might have taken something out, and their purpose might become clear from that.”

I see. Various pieces of information would likely come out eventually. I could just fly to Vinesdora periodically to ask for updates.

“It’s about time to switch. You should relax in the cabin as well. We should reach Princess Stephania’s territory by the next shift.”

“Thank you.”

After having Old Sigmund take over the helm, Elliot and Saphir came down to the deck.

“Shift change?”

“Yes. Elliot-san, you’ve been on guard duty for quite a long time too; aren’t you tired? How about going to the cabin for some tea?”

“That sounds good. But, there’s something I’d like to talk about a little.”

What could it be? It didn’t seem like the kind of thing to discuss over tea in the cabin.

“That’s fine. If you’d prefer not in the cabin, how about over there on the deck?”

I pointed to the edge of the deck, and Elliot nodded. The two of us moved there and talked while looking out at the sea.

“Is this about Ashley, by any chance?”

“Yes,” Elliot said with a wry smile, but then his expression turned serious as he asked, “That child was trying very hard to become a proper lord, wasn’t she? Talking with her, I got that impression.”

“…Yes, that’s right. Not just Magic study and training, but also studying to be a lord, giving instructions for the Barony of Silun—she’s working hard on various things.”

“I see.”

Saying that, Elliot closed his eyes.

“Is something the matter?”

When I asked, Elliot seemed a little hesitant about what to say, but eventually spoke.

“Actually, I’m worried that my return to the Barony of Silun might cause some disturbance. Since Ashley has succeeded as the head of the Silun Baron family, she should continue as the lord. It wouldn’t be right for the family headship to be handed over to me just because I’ve returned now.”

…That’s certainly true.

For example, if a second son inherited the headship due to a temporary health issue, and then later the elder brother recovered and the headship returned to him—without very special circumstances, that normally wouldn’t happen.

There was a time when the Silun Barony’s retainers caused some problematic behavior… but it’s stable now, and even that didn’t become a major issue. Ashley has no faults as a lord.

So, what Elliot is worried about is whether the surrounding people might try to push him forward. If Ashley herself offered to hand over the headship, citing her young age… that might very well go through.

In short, if many retainers wanted Elliot to become lord, they might pressure Ashley to relinquish the headship.

While it’s about Ashley, this is also a matter of Elliot’s own position.

“In other words, Elliot-san, you want to support Ashley as the lord.”

“Yes. After our parents passed away… while I was gone, Ashley worked very hard. I don’t want to waste her efforts. If the headship came to me just because I returned, wouldn’t that be pitiful for Ashley? But… if being the lord is a burden for Ashley… that was originally a responsibility I should have borne. Even if that were the case, it feels presumptuous to say so. It would be insulting.”

…Yeah, that’s right. Telling her, “If you don’t want to be lord, I’ll do it, so you can step down”—that could be taken as an insult to Ashley’s resolve.

“Have you talked to Ashley about this?”

“…No, not yet.”

It must indeed be difficult for Elliot to bring up. The reason he started talking to me about it was probably because he first wanted to know how Ashley was doing. He also seemed unsure whether he should consult her or not.

But… Elliot’s desire to support Ashley must undoubtedly be genuine. If he himself wanted to be lord, he would have approached Ashley directly about handing over the headship, not talked to me.

“In that case, let’s talk with Ashley present too. We should confirm her intentions.”

But surely… Ashley’s answer is already decided, I think. Ashley didn’t stand up with half-hearted resolve either. I’ve seen and know that. She probably wouldn’t misunderstand Elliot’s words either.

Elliot, who had been hesitating whether to bring it up or not—seemed to make up his mind after looking at my expression and nodded quietly.

+++

# **283 – Circumstances of the Baronial Family**

“Ashley, may I have a moment?”

I called out to Ashley as I headed toward the cabin with Elliot.

“What is it?”

“I need to talk about the Barony of Silun.”

When Elliot said this, Ashley nodded with a serious expression.

“Elliot-san is a bit worried. About whether there might be some disturbance related to the family succession when he returns. That’s why I thought it necessary to discuss this now.”

“Indeed… that’s true. Until now, I thought such matters were unrelated to the Silun baronial family.”

If we were to discuss the matter of the Barony of Silun’s lord from a detached perspective, many would likely welcome Elliot becoming the lord. He is the legitimate firstborn son and rightful heir. It would be perfectly natural for him to become the lord.

However, we must also consider that Ashley and the Barony of Silun have some unique aspects. It seems that after treating an injured adventurer near the labyrinth entrance some time ago, her popularity among adventurers has increased… and they appear quite favorable toward the Silun baronial family.

Word spread from Termwills, and the adventurers coming to the Barony of Silun seem quite cooperative, likely due to their favorable impression of Ashley.

The forest near the Barony of Silun is somewhat challenging with a fair number of monsters. The continued cooperation of adventurers is essential there, and it aligns well with the Barony of Silun’s policies.

From the perspective of rebuilding the Marquisate of Broderick, Verdgar would likely want to support the stability of the Barony of Silun as well.

First, I should hear Ashley’s thoughts. We decided to continue our discussion on the deck with all three of us.

“I believe my return will cause some ripples in the Barony of Silun. However, if we discuss it and unify our intentions, there won’t be any wavering later on, and the retainers probably won’t say anything reckless. That’s precisely why I want to clearly hear Ashley’s thoughts.”

Wavering… Indeed, if voices saying Elliot would be more suitable spread, they would likely reach Ashley’s ears too.

If Ashley lacked confidence or resolve at that time, such voices might grow louder. The same would apply if Elliot became the lord. The adventurers in the territory would voice their desire for Ashley to remain as lord. If that happened, those who would try to champion Ashley might appear… perhaps.

There’s no guarantee that my engagement to her… wouldn’t appear attractive to such people. While some might argue she should yield the family headship to Elliot because she’s engaged… others could view it as advantageous for the barony since I’m a direct vassal of the king. Those aspects would be evaluated and interpreted differently depending on one’s position.

Well… I won’t let anyone try to use Ashley because of her engagement to me, though.

“I… was deeply depressed after Father and Mother passed away and Elliot-oniisama didn’t return. I was afraid of the outside world.”

Ashley closed her eyes at Elliot’s words and placed a hand over her heart.

“Lady Lisa encouraged me, I met Theodore-sama… and then I saw many things and met many people. Lady Marie’s thorough way of maintaining resolve, Lady Claudia-sama’s way of living… Seeing those things, I wanted to be a lord who could stand shoulder to shoulder with those people. I don’t intend to bend that way of living now. I wouldn’t be able to face them anymore.”

Ashley looked directly into Elliot’s eyes as she said this.

She was born a noble and became the lord. Even if the circumstances weren’t what she wished for… after hearing Mother’s story, she’s striving to become worthy of being a lord. That’s why I want to affirm the path Ashley is trying to walk and offer my support as well.

“…I understand.”

Elliot smiled with a relieved expression.

“I’m sure I’m still lacking in many ways now… and probably causing worry for Elliot-oniisama and everyone in the Barony of Silun. But please, will you believe in me?”

“Of course. For me, confirming Ashley’s feelings about being the lord was all I needed. I was worried that because I’m an inadequate brother, I might have imposed a burden on you.”

“Not at all. Now, being able to remain as lord is also my support. I’m happy that you’ve returned too.”

Ashley smiled.

“Thank you, Ashley.”

…Yeah. Ashley and Elliot should be fine now. Even though they’re siblings, they’ve been separated for a long time, so having a proper discussion and ensuring mutual understanding is important. This way, they won’t harbor distrust later on.

“Based on our current discussion, let’s also consult with His Majesty Melvin.”

Now that I’ve confirmed both their thoughts, I can offer my support too. Since this concerns the lordship, I’d like to hear King Melvin’s opinion as well.

While Elliot’s position within Verdgar still has some uncertainties… with his level of ability, he’ll likely be welcomed with generous treatment from Verdgar.

“Thank you, Theodore-sama.”

“Mm. Well then, shall we return to the cabin and relax for a bit?”

“That sounds good. I’m just starting to get the hang of the card game.”

Elliot smiled as he said this.

We caught sight of Princess Stephania’s territory around dusk that day. Perfect timing. We’ll probably stay in Princess Stephania’s territory today and then head south tomorrow after stopping by the Moon Temple and such.

I also made a promise to create a hidden room in Princess Stephania’s castle. I should probably do that tonight.

Princess Stephania’s territory, like the Marquisate of Fobrester, is a port town facing the sea. Her castle sits on a small hill a short distance from the town. Apparently, it was originally an expanded fortress, giving it quite a formidable impression.

“If we approach directly with the airship, it might cause confusion, so I’ll go ahead on a wyvern to explain.”

Princess Stephania will ride one of the wyverns to inform her territory’s retainers.

“Then I’ll escort you.”

“Fufu. Thank you. Mm. I’m looking forward to seeing everyone’s faces when they see the airship.”

Princess Stephania seems to be in quite high spirits. She’s a troublesome person in a different way than Rosemary.

“We’ll also let them know we’re here, so it’ll be a double surprise, I suppose.”

…That would be Princess Adriana. Somehow, these two seem like partners in mischief… but I won’t delve deeper.

With stirrups and saddle attached to the wyvern, Princess Stephania takes off from the deck. I also mount Lindwurm and fly alongside her.

We fly over the sea, and as we approach near the port, we see wyverns taking off from the castle and heading toward us.

“This is—Your Highness Stephania…!”

The knights riding the wyverns immediately salute upon recognizing Princess Stephania.

“Good work on your duties. That flying ship belongs to Silvatoria. His Majesty Eberhart and Her Highness Adriana are also aboard. Please welcome them properly without any discourtesy.”

“Y-yes, ma’am!”

The knights’ eyes widen for a moment, but they quickly return the salute and begin to turn their wyverns. However, Princess Stephania stops one of the knights.

“Could you please tell the people gathered at the port that there’s nothing to worry about?”

“Understood.”

The addressed knight spurs his wyvern and heads straight toward the people gathered at the port.

We fly behind the knight heading toward the castle and land in the spacious grounds within the castle premises.

“Your Highness…!”

An elderly knight in full armor comes running up with a panicked expression.

“I’m back, Georg.”

Princess Stephania smiles toward the elderly knight—Georg.

“You’ve returned? Welcome back. It appears a flying ship is heading this way… were you aboard it, Your Highness?”

“Yes. It’s a Silvatorian ship. His Majesty Eberhart and Her Highness Adriana will be arriving shortly. Though it’s sudden, please make thorough preparations to welcome them.”

“What did you say…?”

Georg’s expression changes dramatically. Even if the ship itself poses no threat, having distinguished guests aboard means he can’t let his guard down in a different sense.

“In that case… this armor is unnecessary. I shall go change. You there! You heard! Make preparations for the welcome immediately!”

Georg gives instructions while heading back into the castle.

Princess Stephania seemed satisfied, having seen the reaction she expected.

+++

# **284 – The Princess and the Old General's Hospitality**

Princess Stephania’s territory serves as a fairly large stronghold in the northern region. Both the Marquisate of Fobrester and this place play central roles in the north. Most exchanges with Silvatoria occur through these two port towns.

However, the circumstances here differ somewhat from the Marquisate of Fobrester, which places greater emphasis on maritime affairs, due to the nearby forest inhabited by numerous monsters.

It’s said that Princess Stephania’s territory maintains not only strong naval forces but also formidable land troops. This is why Princess Stephania governs the region with Georg, known as a fierce general, serving as her advisor.

Shortly after, Georg returned, having changed out of his armor and apparently finished giving instructions to his subordinates. Now that he had free time, he requested to hear more detailed explanations of the situation.

Though dressed in formal attire, Georg possessed a heavily muscular, massive build. While he seemed to have a bold personality, his demeanor also carried the refined air of nobility, suggesting his long association with the royal family.

With both Princess Stephania and Georg present, one could imagine the soldiers’ morale would be quite high.

Georg is a military officer from Verdgar, nicknamed the “Steel Sword.” I’d even heard his name mentioned in BFO. He’s known for a legendary feat from his youth where he single-handedly stood his ground on a bridge against a band of Orcs that had stormed a frontier village and repelled them.

“I understand that ship belongs to Silvatoria… but how did this come about? For His Majesty Eberhart to visit without any prior communication suggests an extremely urgent matter, does it not?”

“It’s not exactly an emergency, but we couldn’t spare the time for the usual exchange of visit notifications… I suppose that’s the situation. His Majesty Eberhart said since it’s an impromptu visit during travels, we shouldn’t go to any special trouble.”

Princess Stephania conveyed the message in that manner. Having observed the reaction and seeming satisfied, she appeared to be providing cover to ensure subordinates wouldn’t be held responsible even if preparations weren’t perfect.

“Understood. But one might say the timing is quite fortunate. We just happened to hunt down a large boar monster, and our chefs are putting their full effort into preparing it.”

“But… wasn’t that meant to be your share to eat?”

“No, no, we have more than enough.”

Georg flashed a broad grin as he said this, then turned his gaze toward me.

“And this gentleman is?”

“My apologies for the late introduction. I am Theodore Gartner. I accompanied them as an escort from the airship to here.”

“Ah, Theodore-dono! I heard you saved Her Highness Stephania’s life from bandits! Pleased to make your acquaintance, Ambassador-dono.”

“The pleasure is mine.”

Georg brightened his expression and offered a handshake, which I accepted.

Bandits… must be referring to the incident with Roy. I’m not sure how much of the internal details of that incident have been revealed, but it seems some information about me has been shared.

“However, not only are His Majesty Eberhart and Her Highness Adriana here, but Theodore-dono as well. Perhaps your fiancées are also present?”

“Yes, they are.”

“Hmm. Then we must provide a grand welcome indeed.”

Georg laughed heartily. Though he’d been surprised by Princess Stephania earlier, he was already handling the situation adeptly – quite characteristic of a military man. Once he grasped the situation, he became flexible in his response.

Soon the airship approached, docking just before the fortress gate. From there, Grace and the others, along with King Eberhart’s group, disembarked.

The royal family, the Marquis Zilbolt household, elders from the Sages’ Academy, a High Spirit… Looking at the lineup again, even just the Silvatoria side comprised an impressive gathering.

“Lord Georg. It’s been a while.”

“Ah, Lady Rosemary. You haven’t changed. Lady Marlene, you’re looking well.”

Georg exchanged greetings with both women. Not only Rosemary but Marlene also seemed acquainted with Georg, smiling and nodding in response.

Judging by their reactions, Georg appears to be fairly trusted by Marlene as well. Well, considering his legendary feats, that makes sense. He himself seems like quite an interesting character – bold yet gentlemanly.

“My, my, what an assembly. This is quite something. I don’t quite recall such distinguished persons gathering together in this castle before.”

“Well, I’m in a married-away position now.”

Rosemary covered her mouth with her folding fan, acting as if it were nothing. Marlene was smiling cheerfully as usual.

“Lord Georg, is it… Indeed, seeing my sister in her natural state, they might make a good combination.”

Rosemary calmly analyzed the situation.

“First, let me show you to the guest room.”

With the airship arrived at the castle and everyone disembarked, Princess Stephania personally escorted King Eberhart and the other Silvatorian guests.

After passing through stone corridors and being shown to the guest room, everyone finally caught their breath.

“Please wait a little while until dinner. If you need anything, don’t hesitate to ask the servants.”

With these words, Princess Stephania bowed slightly.

“Shall we take care of our promise before dinner?”

When I mentioned the hidden room since I had free time after conveying the necessary information, Princess Stephania gave a wry smile.

“That’s something to look forward to and I’m happy about it, but since you said you plan to depart leisurely tomorrow, I’d like you to rest and recover from your journey today. You’re one of the guests I’m hosting, after all.”

Hmm. If that’s the case, I’ll take you up on your offer. I decided to wait while having some tea until dinner time.

“You’ve returned to Verdgar, haven’t you?”

“Yeah. I suppose so.”

In response to Grace’s words, I took a sip of tea while feeling sentimental. When looking at the time period, it wasn’t really that long, but perhaps because so much had happened, it felt like I’d been away for quite a while.

“I find this quite moving.”

Elliot said this while narrowing his eyes. For Elliot, this would be a homecoming after six years. Though he was smiling gently, he must have had various emotions inside. Ashley nodded quietly at Elliot’s words.

“…Come to think of it, I was suspicious of Marquis Zilbolt and Lord Elliot. I even wrote as much in my secret letter to Steph… I must properly apologize for that lack of thoroughness.”

Seeing this, Princess Adriana spoke apologetically.

Well… it was understandable that Princess Adriana would misunderstand at that point, but knowing the full context now, she might be thinking that she could have inadvertently fueled Princess Stephania’s suspicions toward Marquis Zilbolt and Elliot.

“Your words are too generous.”

“Thank you for your concern.”

Marquis Zilbolt and Elliot responded to Princess Adriana with formal deference.

Although the preparations for hospitality might not have been perfect, the dishes served were still splendid. The boar dish served as the main course was so well-stewed it practically fell apart. It had a more refined taste than one might expect from the word “boar,” and was quite delicious.

“Even though this is a sudden visit, preparing something this elaborate must have been difficult.”

King Eberhart also praised the response unreservedly. By King Eberhart himself speaking these words, the castle staff could breathe a sigh of relief knowing their work had been properly acknowledged.

“We happened to obtain a fine specimen from hunting. I too am relieved to receive Your Majesty’s words.”

“Oh? So this boar meat was from Lord Georg?”

“Yes. Though I’m embarrassed to admit it.”

“Truly worthy of Verdgar’s Steel Sword.”

When Georg answered, King Eberhart nodded with satisfaction. It seemed King Eberhart and Georg were also acquainted.

Considering the era, Georg has likely been a loyal retainer since King Melvin’s time, or perhaps even the previous generation. So it wouldn’t be strange for him to be acquainted with King Eberhart.

“Thank you, Georg. Even though it was such short notice.”

“Not at all. While I was certainly surprised, being prepared for anything at any time is my creed. Though it’s somewhat regrettable that we don’t have a musician.”

While I was satisfied with the meal, Georg still seemed to have some dissatisfaction.

Irmhild and I made eye contact, so I nodded.

“If I may have permission, I could play something after dinner.”

Irmhild said to Princess Stephania. Irmhild is quite service-minded as well.

Well, performing is probably something she takes pride in. It’s also the farewell gift Claudia gave her when leaving the Labyrinth Village.

There’s a saying that skills will support you in life, and music was also what brought her closer to Sheila. Her experience at the theater must have given her confidence too.

Princess Stephania had once come to see the theater, so she knew of Irmhild’s skill. Perhaps because of this, she nodded happily.

“Well then—”

Melodies began to weave forth from Irmhild’s lute. Given it was a hospitality occasion, she played mostly cheerful tunes. Her repertoire seemed to be steadily growing too, as she skillfully played various pieces – from brilliant melodies to light, bouncing tunes – all with just one lute.

“Hmm. This is quite good.”

Tephra closed her eyes and listened to the music Irmhild was playing.

“Magnificent indeed.”

“It’s truly been a long time since we’ve experienced something like this.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina also seemed in high spirits. They had been imprisoned at the Sages’ Academy, so they probably had no entertainment there. King Eberhart and the others also appeared to be quietly enjoying the music.

…Though there was no preparation time, with Georg and his men’s efforts combined with Irmhild’s cooperation… I’d say the hospitality was successful. Even though Irmhild isn’t from Princess Stephania’s territory, it served as a welcome from the Verdgar side.

+++

# **285 – The Princess and the Hidden Room**

“I had so much fun playing to my heart’s content today.”

After performing during the post-dinner hours and returning to the guest room, Irmhild stretched contentedly with a satisfied expression.

“Yeah. It was fun,” Sheila shared her honest impression.

“Good work. You had more variety in your repertoire than before.”

“Everyone seemed to enjoy it, didn’t they?”

In response to Grace’s and my words, Irmhild smiled somewhat bashfully.

“Many of the songs were taught to me by Cyrille and the others. I’ve been secretly practicing them together with everyone.”

Miss Cyrille the Centaur. The residents of the Labyrinth Village.

“About the songs known by the village residents – were they originally from Claudia-sama?”

“Some were taught by me. There are songs passed down from my homeland, as well as songs the village’s original residents already knew.”

Claudia’s homeland – songs passed down from the moon. And then songs passed down among monster tribes, I suppose.

“That’s quite fascinating,” said Rosemary, her curiosity apparently piqued. “If we encounter monster tribes that know the same Cursed Melodies, it could indicate shared ancestry.”

Indeed, that would be the case. There might be research value in tracing roots and studying them.

“It might be interesting to exchange Cursed Melodies if we ever meet monster tribes somewhere.”

The probability of encountering monster species that handle Cursed Melodies isn’t particularly high. The chance of them being hostile is even lower… but I’ll keep it in mind nonetheless. A single Cursed Melody might potentially help avoid a fight.

We exited through the castle gate built on the small hill, crossed the drawbridge, and traveled by carriage down the sloping road veiled in morning mist. Our destination was the Moon Temple within the territory.

The next morning – we decided to visit the Moon Temple first thing in the early hours. Today’s schedule involved resting leisurely at Princess Stephania’s castle, having lunch, and then departing at a relaxed pace, but I wanted to take considerable time creating the hidden room as well.

We descended the slope and traveled through the town. The paved roads were wide and gave a sense of openness. The main street bathed in morning sunlight still had few pedestrians but maintained a bright atmosphere.

“This is my first time visiting Elder Sister’s territory, but it’s quite prosperous, isn’t it?”

When Rosemary said this while peering outside through the carriage window, Stephania, who had volunteered to guide us to the Moon Temple, made a happy expression.

“Oh, I’m glad.”

“…Well, better than I expected.”

Saying this, Rosemary hid her mouth behind her feather fan. From Rosemary’s perspective, she might have been slightly underestimating things. Princess Stephania seemed pleased that Rosemary was letting her guard down. Marlene watched this exchange with amusement. Well, sisters getting along well can’t be a bad thing.

“Alright then, let’s get this done quickly.”

Upon arriving at the Moon Temple, Claudia got off the carriage and used magic just like with Vinesdora. This time, without anyone witnessing it, the Spell Formula was completed effortlessly.

“That should do it. Make sure to notify the shrine maidens of the Moon Temple later.”

“Understood.”

Stephania nodded at Claudia’s words. Now then. Next comes the Magic Construction.

When creating a hidden room… the question arises of where and how to build it. Since we’re adding it afterward, we need to properly incorporate it while considering the building’s structural strength and available space. Hmm. It is a castle, after all. We probably need to consider the outer wall’s strength too.

“Hmm. So this is the Magic Construction I’ve heard about,” said Old Sigmund.

“Well, I’m self-taught.”

“That makes it even more interesting.”

Not only Old Sigmund and Valentina, but Princess Adriana also appeared quite intrigued. However, since they’re from another country, revealing the hidden passage locations would be problematic, so we agreed to create some underground passages first, then temporarily blindfold them to descend, and remove the blindfolds to show them the passages.

The existence of hidden passages and emergency escape routes themselves are common to every country… so their mere existence being known isn’t an issue as long as the entrances remain secret.

So we had the Silvatoria group wait in the guest room for a while. During that time, we moved to Princess Stephania’s room and began work.

“Alright then, Seraphina. As usual, I’m counting on you.”

“Okay. Leave it to me.”

Seraphina, perched on my shoulder, smiled happily. With Seraphina here, I can intuitively understand the building’s structural strength and such. Thanks to that, I can improvise various things.

First, I need to grasp the layout – Princess Stephania’s room and study, what’s directly beneath the rooms, and so on.

Considering the location for the hidden room’s door. This time… a closet might work well. Behind where the closet is placed… separated by just one wall is the attendant’s waiting room for Princess Stephania. Below that is a storage room. Hmm. Let me create a model with Earth Magic to check if this will work… Yeah, seems feasible.

“Then I’ll begin.”

It seems best to create space for a spiral staircase between walls by slightly shifting the walls of the attendant’s waiting room and the storage room below.

First, move the closet that was at the entrance to the hidden passage. Create Golems from the wall. Gradually shift and rearrange the items placed in the attendant’s waiting room.

Then remove the flooring materials. Reform the Golems made from walls and floors into stairs leading downward.

For the storage room below, similar to the attendant’s waiting room, use Golems to move items away from the space we’ll use. From here, we’ll create the underground passage and hidden room.

Create Golems from flooring materials and soil beneath the floor. While digging downward, create stone walls as camouflage walls for both the waiting room and storage room.

Both the waiting room and storage room will become slightly narrower… but it shouldn’t be noticeable unless carefully observed. The waiting room is for personal attendants, so they can coordinate their stories, and the storage room isn’t frequently accessed. Let’s stack items in front of the walls to create the illusion they’ve just become slightly narrower.

After creating the underground passage to some extent, I decided to call everyone who had been waiting.

“Please hold hands and follow my guidance.”

“Hehe. I’ll be in your care then.”

Valentina, while blindfolded, seemed to be enjoying herself quite a bit. Applying Levitation, I slowly led them by hand, walking through the hallway – into Princess Stephania’s room. Entering through the still unfinished entrance area, we descended downward.

Moving with Levitation to avoid giving information about scent, direction traveled, distance, etc. Using Wind Magic to Guard the surroundings.

“These are descending stairs. We’re going down, so please be careful.”

Once we’ve descended the spiral staircase, it should be safe to remove the blindfolds. Following that procedure, I guided Old Sigmund and Princess Adriana downstairs and had their blindfolds removed.

Now then, let’s resume work.

Similar to Gartner County, create a fake room with the hidden room in front of it. Petrify the passage interior to harden and reinforce it. Create the Revolving Concealment door and hidden room.

I’ll have them let me change the Revolving Concealment locations later. This is just a sample for now.

“A pillar around here might be good.”

“Understood.”

Seraphina provides her check. Stack Golems like in formation gymnastics, return them to earth masses for shaping, then Petrify and Enhance to reinforce the structure.

“Hmm. So you create Golems to dig holes, transform them into building materials, and even use them as labor for construction. Quite efficient.”

“Efficient indeed, but impossible to imitate. Manipulating Golems while simultaneously creating walls and digging holes – that would be extremely high Difficulty.”

“Indeed. This speed and precision are remarkable. And you’re not even specializing in Earth Magic.”

Old Sigmund and Valentina analyzed the Magic Construction in that manner. Working while being analyzed by those close to me is somewhat embarrassing… but well, I won’t cut corners.

Dig a hole diagonally downward from the hidden room. This is a passage for emergency escape. It should emerge on the slope of the small hill where the castle stands. I’ll dig a considerable distance but won’t complete it entirely. It’s sufficient for Princess Stephania herself to use Earth Magic to open the tunnel when she needs to use it.

“This is a passage for emergency escape. If you continue digging from here, you’ll reach the surface. When necessary, it would be best to use Earth Magic to dig through the end.”

“Yes, I understand.”

I’ve done everything that needed to be done. This should mark the completion of the work.

“Well, that’s about it.”

“I don’t see any signs of breathing pauses…”

Valentina murmured this while touching the wall. Breathing pauses probably refer to… intervals in magical processing. Come to think of it, Miriam, the Labyrinth Trading Company owner, also mentioned something about seams regarding Magic Construction.

“…Hmm… You’re doing various things beyond common sense. You said you were self-taught… but this won’t serve as reference for others.”

Old Sigmund said this while examining the walls and pillars.

“Hmm. This is nice.”

“Right? Somehow, it tickles my fancy.”

Princess Stephania and Princess Adriana happily looked around the hidden room. Then, they played with the Revolving Concealment at the hidden room entrance, spinning it around together. That’s just a sample. As the final touch, I plan to have everyone leave before changing the locations and such.

The hidden passage entrance in Princess Stephania’s room will be a closet, but the Revolving Concealment part will be inside a wardrobe, designed to rotate only a portion to access the hidden passage side. I’ll make it so the hidden door can be barred from the passage side, preventing entry from behind.

“What should I do? Storing preserved food, weapons, and Grimoires is fine, but desks, chairs, beds… what about the layout? I need to think about it before going to Termwills.”

I’m glad she likes it. Though this feels more like a secret base than a shelter.

I deliberately left the escape exit unfinished, and Princess Stephania seems like someone who maintains boundaries between public and private matters, so she probably won’t use it to flee the castle, but she might hide here occasionally without particular reason.

Well… that’s fine. Let’s continue like this, stop by the Marquisate of Fobrester, create a hidden room, and then return to Termwills.

+++

# **286 – The Return Along the Coast**

For lunch, unlike last night, the main dish was fish cuisine.

It was a simmered white fish with a thick sauce that reminded me of sweet and sour glaze. Quite an elegant flavor.

“The food here is delicious,” Grace said with a smile after thoroughly examining the dishes. Ah, I see. This probably means the repertoire of dishes served at home will expand.

“The head chef used to work at Termwills’ Royal Castle,” Princess Stephania said happily, her eyes narrowing.

“I see, that explains it.”

The wild boar dish also had quite a refined taste. So it seems a chef who served at the royal castle came here to become head chef.

“Normally the food has more of a wild taste. The Knight Order prefers dishes with stronger saltiness. That’s why Georg sometimes works with him in the kitchen too.”

“Oh? Sir Georg does?”

“No, no. I’m nowhere near comparable to the head chef,” Georg modestly replied to King Eberhart’s words… but it shows he has enough skill to share tasks with the head chef. Quite the versatile individual, excelling in both literary and military arts.

“Well then, Your Highness Stephania. Please take care.”

“Yes. Please carry on as usual while I’m away.”

“Leave it to me.”

After exchanging words with Georg and the other retainers who came to see her off, Princess Stephania boarded the airship.

After the meal, we took a break with candy crafts and tea, relaxed for a bit, then departed from Princess Stephania’s territory. From the castle on high ground, you could see the ocean and the city in one view – it was quite a scenic and pleasant place.

Now then. The Marquisate of Fobrester isn’t too far from here. Once we finish our business with the hidden room and the Moon Temple, we can depart immediately and likely reach Termwills by nightfall.

The crew members busily ran about to set the sails.

“Well then, we’re off!”

As Old Sigmund gripped the helm and held his hand over the crystal ball, the ship began to ascend.

He turned the helm, activated the magic tool, and caught the wind in the sails. Changing direction, the ship began to move forward.

As we passed over the city, I could see children running along the main street chasing after us. When Princess Stephania peeked out from the deck and waved to the children of her territory, they waved back with great delight.

The children of the territory, growing gradually smaller, seemed to keep waving at the airship until they were out of sight.

“This is… Your Highness Stephania, Theodore-dono. You’ve returned to Verdgar?”

When Marquis Fobrester saw us peeking out from the wyvern’s back, he showed a relieved expression.

In the Marquis’ territory too, Princess Stephania and I went ahead on wyvernback to inform the Marquis at his castle. The airship’s impact is simply too great, and just showing up would unnecessarily tense up the knights and soldiers.

“Yes. We’ve secured King Eberhart’s cooperation. He’s aboard that ship.”

“What?”

Marquis Fobrester’s eyes widened.

We explained we were stopping for supplies and that we needed to hurry. Since we’d depart immediately after our business was done, it wouldn’t be a full reception, but the Marquis couldn’t not greet us either.

“And so, we’re rather pressed for time and things are hectic, my apologies—”

I brought up the topic of creating a hidden room for Marquis Fobrester as well.

“I had one made too. Well, having a place to hide might be convenient in case of emergency,” Princess Stephania added.

“Oh?”

The Marquis blinked slightly in confusion, but nodded with interest at Princess Stephania’s words.

“Hmm… Then may I request your assistance?”

“Certainly.”

Marquis Fobrester usually stays within his territory and rarely ventures outside.

It seems he spends most of his time working in his office. So I created the hidden room in the Marquis’ castle starting from the first-floor office. The floor beneath the desk slides open, allowing escape to the hidden room from there. Since we started from the first floor, we didn’t have the difficulties like with Princess Stephania’s castle, and the hidden room was completed smoothly. This time, the stairs going down open partway, and we created the real room here. The room at the end of the passage is the decoy.

“You’re quite efficient… you seem experienced at this,” the Marquis murmured as he looked around the completed hidden room after our greetings.

“Yes. I’ve made them several times.”

“I see,” Marquis Fobrester said with a wry smile.

“Interesting indeed. During peacetime, it would be good to store weapons and preserved food here.”

“That might be a good way to use it during normal times. Ah, changing the subject slightly… I’d like to ask you to pass a message to the shrine maidens at the temple in your territory.”

“What is it?”

While I was creating the hidden room, Claudia and the others went to town by carriage to handle preparations with the temple. Looking through Caduceus, it seems they’re already on their way back.

“Actually, with a new spell formula from the temple, we can now discern the content of the shrine maidens’ prayers even from the Termwills side.”

“Oh…”

“This means that in urgent situations like demon attacks, if the shrine maidens offer prayers to Goddess Shuath, we can quickly learn of the situation from the Termwills side.”

“That’s… wonderful. For sending reinforcements and preparing other towns… we can minimize the damage. I’ll definitely inform the shrine maidens.”

“Yes. I think it would be good to establish a system where messengers are sent if anything happens.”

Well, actually, the prayers reach Claudia rather than the Termwills side.

As we were having this conversation and returned to the castle courtyard, Claudia and the others themselves had also returned from the Moon Temple. When Marquis Fobrester appeared, Marlene picked up the hem of her skirt and greeted him. The Marquis smiled and nodded.

Marlene is currently treated as an adopted daughter of House Fobrester due to her marriage arrangement, but originally through her connection with Albert, she’s also close with Ophelia and acquainted with the Marquis.

“Marlene-sama, I’m glad to see you looking well.”

Marlene nodded slightly.

“The temple is fine,” Claudia said.

“Yes. I was just explaining that.”

“The loading of supplies is finished too,” Sheila said.

Regarding supplies, we only loaded drinking water. Since we’re heading straight to Termwills afterward, we have plenty of food.

“Marquis Fobrester. My apologies for the haste. Coming like this and leaving immediately must seem like we’re just causing trouble…”

“Not at all, Your Majesty Eberhart. It’s an honor to welcome you. Being able to witness the pinnacle of Silvatoria’s renowned technology, the Magic Kingdom, is a feast for the eyes. It should provide good stimulation for those in my territory too.”

As we were checking if everyone was present, I could hear King Eberhart and Marquis Fobrester exchanging words.

I took over the ship’s operation from Marquis Fobrester’s territory.

The ship is progressing at a good speed. Since we’re flying along the coast, the scenery is beautiful. Everyone seems to have come out on deck to enjoy the view.

“The Labyrinth City, huh. I’m looking forward to it, Lord Sigmund.”

“Hmm. Indeed. We don’t go out much, you see. Having been shut away for so long makes it all the more so. This journey is quite fresh,” Old Sigmund nodded at Valentina’s words.

The sages of Beriondora… they seem connected to the magician who brought barrier magic. Once we reach Termwills, I’d like to ask about that while looking at materials. We might learn something new.

“I’d like to go down into the labyrinth at least once,” said Princess Adriana. Seeing Princess Stephania nodding thoughtfully beside her was somehow indescribable…

“Sir Elliot, have you ever explored the labyrinth?”

“No, I haven’t. I only visited Termwills once when heading to my study abroad destination by ship, so I know almost nothing about it. But indeed, I’d like to see the inside of the labyrinth at least once,” Elliot said with a smile.

“Theoreme Castle is an amazing structure too… but I’ve heard rumors about new attractions being built recently. That a theater was built?”

“Yes. And hot springs have emerged too.”

“Hot springs! That’s wonderful!”

I noticed Rosemary, who overheard this conversation, hid her mouth with her feather fan and glanced this way for a moment. I’m glad she seems to be enjoying herself.

Leaving the labyrinth aside, as the person involved in building the theater and hot spring district, I suppose I’ll end up giving tours.

Well then… at last, we’re returning to Termwills.

+++

# **287 – Two Kings**

The airship advanced toward Termwills as they watched the sea dyed in twilight colors.

Though they were drawing attention from people traveling along the roads… well, it was probably best to accept it as having the effect of promoting friendly relations between Verdugal and Silvatoria.

Waving from the deck to show the gaping, wide-eyed people that they meant no harm, they continued on while casually brushing off the attention until the sun eventually set.

Soon, night fell completely—but they didn’t lose their direction. In the distance, they could already see lights twinkling here and there on the soaring spires of Theoreme Castle, Termwills’ royal castle.

“Oh… so that’s Theoreme. Its majesty surpasses what I’ve heard.”

“…It’s wonderful. I hear it was created by the labyrinth?”

“So it seems. Indeed… it would be somewhat impossible to build on this scale through normal construction, or even through magic construction.”

Using night vision magic to look at Theoreme, Old Sigmund and Valentina exchanged words.

“It appears certain that the labyrinth side created it. Since demons are involved, I believe we’ll need to discuss that aspect after arriving in Termwills,” said Princess Stephania.

Claudia herself neither denied nor affirmed this, quietly closing her eyes.

As they continued toward Termwills, they saw the Wyvern Corps flying toward them from the Termwills side.

They had contacted Termwills via communication device, so they assumed this was their welcoming party, but to confirm and avoid confusion, I decided to go ahead to meet the Wyvern Corps.

“I’ll go ahead and speak with them. Would you mind taking over for a bit?”

“Hmm.”

After having Old Sigmund take over piloting, I rode Lindwurm ahead of the airship.

The ones riding wyverns toward us were—Chester and his group.

“Theodore-dono. Have you returned?”

“Yes, Sir Chester. As communicated, His Majesty Eberhart and Her Highness Adriana are aboard as well.”

“Understood. We have been ordered to escort you to Termwills.”

I returned and informed them that the Termwills Wyvern Corps would provide escort.

Shortly after, Chester landed on the deck as the Wyvern Corps representative and bowed to King Eberhart.

“I am Chester Glenbel of the Veldgar Kingdom Knights Wyvern Corps. Having heard of Your Majesty Eberhart’s visit, I have come to pay my respects.”

After bowing and introducing himself, he offered to provide ship escort and guidance until their arrival in Termwills. King Eberhart’s expression softened at his words.

“Your service is appreciated. Then I leave it to you, Sir Chester.”

“Yes, it’s an honor.”

“To have the escort of the renowned Wyvern Corps of Verdugal is quite magnificent.”

“You flatter me.”

With that, Chester mounted his wyvern and soared up. The Wyvern Corps formed up around the ship front, back, left, and right, and they proceeded toward Termwills.

Meanwhile, we checked our luggage, hitched the dragon palanquin and wyverns, and made other preparations for landing.

The Wyvern Corps members all seemed to have brought night vision magic tools for night flying.

Though this was probably their first time escorting an airship, since we had notified them in advance of our arrival by ship, they might have trained for it. They guided the ship with flawless formation flying.

Passing over the waiting line of people who were looking at them and making a commotion, they crossed the outer wall, flew over Termwills’ cityscape—and headed straight for the royal castle.

“Do you see the training grounds used as a parade square? Please dock there.”

“Hmm. Understood.”

Old Sigmund nodded.

The training grounds near the Knight’s Tower seemed convenient for docking the airship. Bonfires were lit on the training grounds, making the landing spot visible almost like an airport. They were guided toward it. The sails were furled, and the ship descended.

They dropped anchor to secure the ship. The gangplank was lowered, and they disembarked from the ship onto the training grounds.

It was a familiar place. I soaked in the feeling of having returned. The wyverns that had traveled with us from Termwills were also returning after some time. The dragon palanquin was lowered from the deck, and their gear was removed. When the dragon stable keepers came to greet them, they happily snorted and approached. Only Lindwurm remained aloof toward the keepers, but he seemed to be in good spirits.

“You’ve worked hard during the journey. See you tomorrow.”

I spoke to Lindwurm. He looked back over his shoulder, let out one cry, and returned to the dragon stable. Hmm.

“Oh, Melvin.”

“Eberhart. It’s been a long time.”

King Eberhart called out to King Melvin, who had arrived with Knight Order Commander Mildred and others as his escort. They had said they were old acquaintances, but… they seemed to be on much more familiar terms than I had imagined, like friends or something.

“I heard you were ill, but I’m glad to see you well.”

“Thanks to Theodore-dono’s treatment. I’ve been full of energy for some time now.”

“Hmm. It’s no good to talk standing here. First, let me have you guided to the guesthouse. Why don’t we have some tea there and renew our old friendship? I’ll also ask for introductions of your party then.”

Maids arrived and guided the Silvatoria members away.

King Melvin watched their backs, then turned to face me.

“I’ve returned now.”

“Hmm. You’ve all done well. First, Theodore… I must thank you for curing Eberhart’s illness. These words come not from a king, but from his friend.”

Ah. So they did have a close friendship indeed.

According to King Melvin, they had interacted more frequently before both inherited their thrones. Being fellow crown princes, they had discussed things like the mindset required for rulers, policies, ideals, and principles.

I see. It makes sense that both are praised as wise rulers, recognizing each other’s reigns.

“As a king… I’m not sure what to say first. I suppose I should be glad you returned safely. Given your mother’s situation.”

My mother’s situation. I had reported the gist of it via communication device. King Melvin seemed to have been somewhat concerned that Silvatoria might make her an offer to serve there. But when all was said and done, my mother’s relationship with the Sages’ Academy elders wasn’t actually that bad.

“Indeed, my mother wasn’t exactly disliked… but she has decided that Termwills is where she belongs.”

When I answered, King Melvin closed his eyes and nodded.

“…Hmm. I’ve also received the report about what happened in Silvatoria. It was the best possible outcome we could have hoped for. Though I didn’t anticipate you returning with a flying ship like this. You’ve done well.”

King Melvin looked up at the airship as he spoke. I also smiled wryly in response.

“Thank you.”

Then King Melvin turned to Princess Stephania.

“Stephania. You also performed your difficult role well.”

“It’s not my achievement. Without Theodore-dono, we likely wouldn’t have accomplished it.”

“The part where you earned the trust of Silvatoria’s key figures, starting with Eberhart, was significant. I highly value that aspect.”

“Thank you.”

That’s true. If we had gone to Silvatoria alone, it would have been quite difficult to meet King Eberhart. It’s because Princess Stephania has maintained good relations with Silvatoria for many years.

“And—Elliot Rodias=Siln.”

“Yes.”

“I’ve already received the report about you. Well done on returning. You may have anxieties about your current position, but this is your homeland. I will never treat you poorly for having returned alive like this.”

“Your words are most gracious.”

“I plan to hold important discussions tomorrow onward. I’ll contact you later regarding various matters about this incident. For today, it would be best to rest from your journey’s fatigue.”

At Elliot’s response, King Melvin nodded, then suddenly showed a soft smile. He then entered the guesthouse.

“Elliot-san, please feel free to stay at our house. We have plenty of guest rooms.”

“Thank you. Then… I’ll take you up on that.”

“Shall we head home then?”

At those words, everyone smiled and nodded.

We retrieved the carriage we had left at the royal castle stables and began our journey home. It had been quite an eventful trip… but now that it was over, I felt glad we went. With my mother’s situation, it felt deeply meaningful…

When my eyes met Grace’s by chance, she smiled back at me. …Yeah. Let’s go home and rest properly today.

+++

# **288 – Returning Home**

“I’m home.”

“Welcome back, Master.”

When we arrived home, Cecilia and Mihaela seemed to have been waiting for our return. They came out to greet us at the entrance.

Claire the Arachne, Cyrille the Centaur, Irmhild’s parents, and Fortok were also there. We had informed them we’d be returning by airship, so they must have prepared after seeing our arrival at the castle.

Elliot’s eyes widened at the unexpected welcoming party. Indeed, the residents of the Labyrinth Village might be quite impactful. Fortok is a Carbuncle, after all.

“I’m home, Father, Mother.”

“Ah. Welcome back.”

“Welcome home, Irm. You weren’t injured?”

“No. I’m fine.”

Irmhild and her parents embraced each other, rejoicing in their reunion.

“Everyone, I’m relieved to see you’re unharmed,” said Cecilia.

“Was anything unusual?”

“Everything was perfectly peaceful. The children seemed to prefer spending time in the courtyard and game room rather than going into town.”

The children from the Labyrinth Village are somewhat accustomed to living quietly.

They’d likely be hesitant to go into town, and with limited entertainment options, the courtyard and game room were probably safe and enjoyable for them.

“Thank you for watching over the place.”

“Not at all. You honor us with your words.”

“I’m relieved we were able to fulfill our duties without incident.”

Cecilia and Mihaela smiled gently.

“Let me introduce everyone. This is Elliot Rodias=Siln, Ashley’s brother.”

“Pleased to meet you.”

“The pleasure is mine.”

Elliot and everyone in the household exchanged greetings. With so many people, I figured they could handle individual introductions themselves.

“Dinner is ready.”

Right. Let’s have dinner first then.

“There are many unusual ingredients,” Elliot remarked as he ate the dishes laid out before him.

“Yes, I suppose that’s unique to Termwills.”

With Whisper Mushrooms, Orc meat, and so on… it’s probably because we’re in a Labyrinth City that monster ingredients are so common. Since we’d informed them we’d be returning tonight, the table was laden with quite lavish and elaborate dishes.

After we all had dinner and tea was served, I waited for the right moment when everyone had settled down to discuss future plans.

“Elliot-san. I’d like to talk about what happens from tomorrow onward, if that’s alright?”

“Yes.”

“I’ve been in contact with the Barony of Silun. Kennel-san is supposed to arrive by dragon palanquin tomorrow or the day after… so it might be better to return home after meeting up in Termwills.”

“Kennel… I look forward to that.”

Elliot narrowed his eyes nostalgically.

Well, Kennel isn’t the only one coming to Termwills… Kennel will be riding in Father’s dragon palanquin.

Since Old Sigmund is staying in Termwills, when I informed them about that, Father said he absolutely wanted to speak with Old Sigmund, so he’s planning to come to Termwills.

…I feel sorry for Father… but I hope we can help bridge things smoothly.

“Still, between the landing lights for the airship and everything else… Verdgar seems quite well-prepared, or rather, your messengers are fast. Do you have something like… a magic device for communicating with distant places?”

“Yes. We have such magic tools.”

Right. He’s starting to notice. I thought we could probably give Elliot a communication device too, which is partly why I mentioned contacting Kennel.

“Master. Alfred-sama and the others have arrived.”

“Ah. Did they come to see us?”

I decided to have them shown to the dining room first.

Alfred seemed to have come with Viola the blacksmith and Miriam from the trading company.

“Good evening.”

“Good evening, everyone,” I greeted Alfred and the others.

“Welcome back, Marlene.”

Marlene smiled and gave a small nod to Alfred.

First, let me introduce Alfred and the others to Elliot.

“This is Alfred, a magic engineer from the Brightwelt Workshop, and Viola the blacksmith. And this is Miriam-san, the proprietor of the Brightwelt Labyrinth Trading Company. This is Lord Elliot. Ashley’s brother.”

Viola and Miriam looked slightly surprised before the introductions. Elliot’s features bear some resemblance to Ashley’s. Only Alfred wasn’t that surprised since he already knew the situation through the communication device.

“Pleased to meet you.”

“Likewise.”

They exchanged handshakes. After the introductions were done, I had them take seats, and we talked while nibbling on baked sweets and drinking tea.

“Well, I’m relieved to see you looking well. We heard you’d returned, so we came to say hello.”

“Same here. I’m glad there don’t seem to have been any major problems while I was away.”

“That’s right. But well, the demons seem to be coming around the time of seal releases.”

“That’s true indeed.”

Perhaps the method to cross the barrier is valuable to them.

“But, I wonder. Lately, it feels like their main objective is less about stealing the Orbs and more about sending Miasma Orbs our way.”

Somehow… I get the impression that stealing the Orbs isn’t absolutely essential to the demons’ strategy. In Alvelinde’s case, it seemed like she brought the Miasma Orbs as part of her duties for the demon side, while also engaging in sabotage against Verdgar and monitoring Marquis Zilbolt… and she hinted that she was told to avoid fighting me.

When the demons make their next move… it’ll probably be around the time the seal at the Blazing Fortress is released. Or perhaps… when the Orbs temporarily weaken and the seal on the door leading to the Moonlight Temple is broken.

“What about using teleportation magic to remove the Miasma Orbs from Termwills right when they’re about to be used in an attack? Using teleportation might allow us to make moves the enemy doesn’t anticipate.”

Rosemary put her hand to her mouth and tilted her head.

Hmm. Rosemary’s strategy is probably to use teleportation magic to move the Miasma Orbs somewhere else at the exact moment the enemy tries to use them.

If bringing Miasma Orbs into Termwills is necessary for their plan’s execution, this could thwart that idea.

It seems there are means to detect the location of both the Orbs and Miasma Orbs, but if, for example, they were suddenly teleported to Vinesdora or somewhere else at the crucial moment, even if the demon side could detect them, they probably couldn’t do anything about it.

“…I’m sorry. That’s impossible,” Claudia said apologetically, shaking her head.

“Hm? Is there a problem?”

“Yes. With half-demons, I could easily overpower them and include them in a teleportation. I managed with Alvelinde too. But with that Miasma Orb… it’s no good. The miasma it emits clashes with my power… and for long-distance teleportation, carrying it seems impossible.”

I see… The quality of the miasma it emits must be incomparable to that of half-demons. Compared to Alvelinde… it might be a compatibility issue. Since the Moon Goddess’s Blessing can block miasma… perhaps the miasma, depending on its quality, interferes with Claudia’s power.

On the other hand, if we try to move it by ordinary means, there’s a high chance the demons would locate the Miasma Orb and attack again to bring it back to Termwills.

Even if we intercept them, splitting our forces isn’t ideal. As Rosemary mentioned before, defeating them individually in Termwills is optimal, but…

“Well… Somehow we ended up talking about demons, but I think we have a few days to relax, so let’s change the subject for today.”

We’ll likely discuss the Orbs and Miasma Orbs with King Melvin, King Eberhart, and Old Sigmund present. Those discussions will probably happen later at the royal castle.

“In that case, how about showing Brother Elliot the game room?”

“The guest rooms are wonderful too. This house is quite advanced,” Miriam replied to Ashley, who was smiling.

Right. As a way to settle our stomachs after the meal, it might not be a bad idea for everyone to go to the game room and deepen our friendship with Elliot and Tephra.

As I was thinking that, a message came through on the communication device. It was from Mercedes.

『My apologies for disturbing your rest. It seems the topic of Theodore-sama’s residence being built with magic construction came up. Her Highness Adriana says she would like to see it. Would there be a convenient day?』

Hmm… It seems things have settled down at the royal castle for now.

Might as well invite Old Sigmund, Valentina, Princess Stephania, and Princess Adriana too. That might not be a bad idea.

So… tonight is fine. Tomorrow or the day after might have plans, so it’s uncertain, I replied. After a short while, the response came that everyone said they’d like to come now.

Well, it wouldn’t be bad for everyone to play together.
